1 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


No. 92,831


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


750 So. 2d 643; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 2178; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 1



December 22, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict Second District - Case No. 96-02517. (Hillsborough County).



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for review of the decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) which found that 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 95-182 violated the single subject rule found in the Fla. Const. art. III § 6. Defendant claimed that ch. 95-182 violated the single subject rule and sought to have the trial court precluded from sentencing her under ch. 95-182.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with three criminal offenses. After charging the defendant with these felony offenses, the state filed a notice of intent to have her sentenced as a "Habitual Felony/Habitual Violent Felony Offender/Violent Career Criminal" pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 775.084 (1995). The version of § 775.084 applicable in the defendant's case had been amended by the passage of 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 95-182, which created the violent career criminal sentencing category for certain criminal offenders. The defendant filed a motion to preclude the trial court from sentencing her as a violent career criminal and to declare unconstitutional ch. 95-182, claiming that the chapter law violated the single subject rule of the Fla. Const. art. III § 6. The court determined that ch. 95-182 was violative of the single subject rule because the various sections of 95-182 addressed two different subjects.


OUTCOME: Remanded for resentencing; the court determined that a career criminal sentencing statute was violative of the single subject rule of the Florida constitution because the various sections of the statute addressed two different subjects.

 

2 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Van Hubbard


No. 94,116


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


751 So. 2d 552; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 2170; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 575



December 16, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. First District - Case No. 97-2666. (Santa Rosa County).



DISPOSITION: Approved Hubbard in part and quashed it in part, approved Melvin under the reasoning expressed herein, and remanded for proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, convicted of DUI manslaughter, claimed on appeal that the trial court erred in utilizing a standard jury instruction and not the special requested instruction containing a negligence element. First District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed the trial court's ruling and certified direct conflict with the Fourth District's Melvin decision.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the DUI manslaughter standard jury instruction should not be modified to include a negligence element. They also found that the improper admission of prior bad acts evidence of a deadly accident, was harmful error. The court found that respondent's past driving record was of marginal, if any, relevance in establishing the elements of DUI manslaughter. Because the court was unable to conclude that the improper admission of this unfairly prejudicial evidence was harmless, they held that respondent was entitled to a new trial on this basis. Additionally, the court approved of the holding in Melvin.


OUTCOME: Affirmed that portion of the district court's decision that reversed and remanded for a new trial on the ground that irrelevant and prejudicial evidence was admitted; quash that portion that held that it was error to give the standard jury instruction on DUI manslaughter. The court approve holding in Melvin.

 

3 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Goodwin v. State


No. 93,491, No. 93,805


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


751 So. 2d 537; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 2167; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 583



December 16, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Name of this Case has been Corrected December 28, 1999. Released for Publication February 14, 2000. Rehearing Denied February 14, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Two Cases Consolidated:. Fourth District - Case No. 97-2086 and First District - Case No. 97-909. (Broward and Duval Counties).



DISPOSITION: Jones quashed. Remanded to the district court for further consideration in light of this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This application for review, a consolidation of two cases, one from the Fourth District, the other from the First district, seeks clarification of decisions of the District Court of Appeal, Florida, both certifying the same question.


OVERVIEW: Applicants for review questioned whether in appeals not involving constitutional error, did the enactment of Florida Stat. ch. 924.051(7) (1996) abrogate the harmless error analysis in case law? The Fourth District, on appeal, held "bad neighborhood" testimony was not "constitutional error." Instead finding defendant failed to meet his burden of demonstrating "prejudicial error" pursuant to Florida Stat. ch. 924.051(7) (1996). In the other case, the trial court allowed the introduction of "collateral crimes evidence" over defendant's objection. The first district affirmed, based on section 924.051(7), but certified the identical question for this court's review. By limiting the certified question to appeals not involving "constitutional error," a term not utilized in the statute, the first and fourth Districts, as well as the state, acknowledged that in cases of constitutional error, state appellate courts were bound by the harmless error standard enunciated in case law. Question answered in the negative on review.


OUTCOME: Question answered in the negative. Reviewing the record, ascertaining whether an error is harmless, is essential appellate function, shifting burden to defendant abdicates judicial responsibility, could lead to unjust results of affirming conviction where appellate court not convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that error did not affect the defendant's conviction.

5 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Senate v. Harris


No. 95,960


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


750 So. 2d 626; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1859; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 505



October 28, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Request for Writ of Mandamus Granted, Governor's request Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Florida Senate sought writ of mandamus ordering Secretary of State to expunge gubernatorial veto directed at portions of proviso language in Line Item 117C of 1999-2000 General Appropriations Act, ch. 99-226, Laws of Florida. Respondent governor counter-petitioned for writ of mandamus requiring expunction of proviso as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, Florida Senate and Senate President, sought writ of mandamus ordering the Florida Secretary of State to expunge the gubernatorial veto directed at portions of the proviso language of the 1999-2000 General Appropriations Act, ch. 99-226, Laws of Florida. Respondent governor vetoed only the operations grants portion of a prolonged school year program. That proviso did not expressly state the amount of funds assigned to the operations grants, but included a formula for calculating the grants. The court found respondent could have vetoed the whole appropriation for the program but could not separate out operations component from the appropriation. The veto was unconstitutional. Respondent cross-petitioned, contending that the operations grants funding formula unconstitutionally amended the statutory funding process of the Florida Education Finance Program. The court found since there were no direct and immediate adverse effects, recourse was in suit for declaratory decree in circuit court, not in mandamus.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's request for writ of mandamus granted and respondent's request denied because mandamus was not proper remedy for his cross-petition. Secretary of State ordered to expunge from official records veto because respondent could have vetoed whole appropriation but could not constitutionally separate out operations component from appropriation.

 

6 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 86,134


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


750 So. 2d 22; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1794; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 487



October 14, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Amended November 9, 1999. Rehearing Denied January 12, 2000. Released for Publication January 12, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Arthur I. Snyder, Judge. Case No. F91-21601AB.



DISPOSITION: Johnson's convictions affirmed. Death sentence vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions of first-degree murder, armed burglary, armed robbery, and the commission of a felony with a firearm, by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), and imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, with a co-defendant, by a jury of first-degree murder, armed burglary, armed robbery, and the commission of a felony with a firearm. Both defendants were sentenced to death. On appeal, the defendant raised several issues claiming error in both the guilt and penalty phases. In affirming the convictions, the court found no error in admissions of his confession, or of other testimony; the jury's inadvertent view of the defendant in handcuffs also did not warrant reversal; and the defendant waived any objection to the court's disallowance of his peremptory challenge. However, his absence during a critical stage of the penalty phase without a knowing and intelligent waiver of his right to be present resulted in an unfair penalty phase proceeding, so the death penalty was vacated, and the court remanded for a new penalty phase proceeding before a new jury.


OUTCOME: Convictions affirmed because there was no error in the guilt phase; death sentence vacated and remanded for a new penalty phase proceeding before a jury based upon the absence of defendant and his counsel during a critical part of the penalty phase proceedings.

 

7 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Provenzano v. Moore


No. 95,973


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


744 So. 2d 413; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1627; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 443



September 24, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1439. As Corrected September 29, 1999. Original Proceedings-Heabeas Corpus



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the circuit court's (Florida) conclusion that the electric chair did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment, and was therefore not unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus, a petition to invoke the court's all writs jurisdiction, and a petition for extraordinary relief. The court directed the circuit court to hold an evidentiary hearing regarding the functioning of the electric chair. Following that four-day hearing, the circuit court rendered findings of fact with respect to the functioning of the electric chair and concluded that the electric chair did not constitute cruel or unusual punishment. The defendant appealed this finding of fact. The court determined that in order for a punishment to constitute cruel or unusual punishment, there must be involved torture or lingering death or the infliction of' unnecessary and wanton pain. The court decided that execution by electrocution rendered an inmate instantaneously unconscious, thereby making it impossible to feel pain.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; death by electric chair did not constitute cruel or unusual punishment because there must be involved torture or lingering death or the infliction of' unnecessary and wanton pain; electric chair did not meet these criteria.

 

8 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Provenzano v. State


No. 96,453


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


750 So. 2d 597; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1626; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 434



September 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bradford County, E. Randolph Bentley, Senior Judge. Case No. 99-286CFA.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded to the circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal by appellant of order of the Bradford County Circuit Court (Florida) finding him sane to be executed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.812.


OVERVIEW: Appellant appealed an order entered by the trial court finding him sane to be executed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.812. The court concluded that lower court abused its discretion when it denied appellant's motion for continuance. The court stayed the execution and remanded case to the trial court with directions to afford appellant reasonable opportunity to present testimony of clinical psychologist as expert witness regarding appellant's competency to be executed. The court also directed the trial court to allow defense counsel opportunity to cross-examine psychiatrist appointed by the Governor to examine appellant's competency for execution regarding appellant's rational appreciation of the connection between his crime and the punishment he was sentenced to receive. The court found no merit to appellant's claim that the test for competency under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.811 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Execution stayed and case remanded to trial court; trial court was directed to afford appellant reasonable opportunity to present the testimony of clinical psychologist as expert witness regarding appellant's competency to be executed.

 

9 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. O.C.


No. 94,513


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


748 So. 2d 945; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1558; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 425



September 16, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Fifth District - Case No. 97-3075.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which declared Fla. Stat. § 874.04, a law that provides for a penalty enhancement if the defendant is a gang member, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of attempted aggravated battery and misdemeanor battery. After the finding of guilt, Plaintiff state moved to have defendant declared a gang member for penalty enhancement purposes pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 874.04. Defendant opposed the motion, asserting that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court denied defendant's constitutional challenge to the statute, found defendant to be a criminal street gang member, and stated that defendant's third-degree felony and misdemeanor would be enhanced. The appellate court determined that Fla. Stat. § 874.04 was unconstitutional, and plaintiff state appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the statute was unconstitutional as a violation of substantive due process. The court held that Fla. Stat. § 874.04 violated defendant's substantive due process rights because the statute subjected defendant to conviction for a higher degree crime than originally charged, resulting in an increased penalty range, based only upon defendant's simple association with others, who may or may not have been criminals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision that the penalty enhancement statute was unconstitutional, holding that the law was a violation of substantive due process in that it subjected defendant to an enhancement penalty based only upon defendant's simple association with the gang members.

 

10 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Conner v. State


No. 92,835


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


748 So. 2d 950; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1556; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 428



September 16, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing January 27, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Fla. LEXIS 83.
Certiorari Denied June 26, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 4366.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Second District - Case No. 96-03016 (Polk County).



DISPOSITION: We hold that the hearsay exception for elderly adults in criminal cases is unconstitutional. We quash the Second District's decision in Conner and remand to the district court for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of District Court of Appeal, Second District (Florida) judgment that expressly declared constitutional the hearsay exception for elderly persons or disabled adults, pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 90.803(24).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with the armed burglary of a dwelling, armed robbery, and armed kidnapping in connection with an elderly victim. A few hours after the incident, the victim provided an initial statement to the police and then two weeks later provided a sworn statement to the police. The prosecution did not introduce the victim's testimony before his death pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.190(j), but did inform petitioner prior to trial that it intended to introduce hearsay statements of the victim pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 90.803(24), pertaining to hearsay statements of elderly adults. Petitioner attacked the exception as violative of his right to confront witnesses, the lower court denied his challenge, and petitioner then pleaded nolo contendere. The lower court convicted petitioner, who sought review. The court held that Fla. Stat. § 90.803(24), the elderly hearsay exception, did violate petitioner's right to confrontation and was not firmly rooted.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the lower court's judgment and remanded the case, holding that the key statute was facially violative of petitioner's right to confrontation, was not firmly rooted, and no other state had a similar exception.

 

11 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Ray v. Mortham


No. 94,653


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


742 So. 2d 1276; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1462; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 412



September 2, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal of Judgment of Circuit Court, in and for Leon County, P. Kevin Davey, Judge, Case No. 98-1024 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 98-4705.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After First District Court of Appeal (Florida) invoked pass-through jurisdiction, appellants, registered voters, challenged decision of Circuit Court, in and for Leon County (Florida) that granted final summary judgment in favor of appellee on appellant's complaint that sought to enjoin enforcement of state constitutional amendment that imposed term limits for certain candidates.


OVERVIEW: In compliance with Fla. Const. art. XI § 3, court issued advisory opinion, which was a prerequisite to a ballot initiative, that a citizens' initiative petition with respect to term limits dealt with only one subject. Voters passed this initiative. State constitution was amended to limit number of consecutive terms of office for state and federal officials. Three years later, United States Supreme Court held that state attempts to restrict candidacy for U.S. Congress violated the U.S. Const. amend. X. Appellants argued that amendment's compliance with single-subject requirement mandated that entire amendment be stricken. Court concluded that unconstitutional provisions with respect to federal legislators were severable. Amendment remained viable because it accomplished its purpose of limiting political terms of state officeholders. Court declined to revisit its prior advisory opinion that amendment satisfied single-subject requirement. Court found amendment constitutional under U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV.


OUTCOME: Decision affirmed; court applied same test to determine severability of unconstitutional provision of state constitutional amendment that was passed by voters' initiative as it would have applied to legislation. Court determined that unconstitutional provision that imposed term limits on federal legislators was severable and amendment was enforceable with respect to state elected officials.

Provenzano v. State


No. 95,959


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


751 So. 2d 37; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1461; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 406



August 26, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bradford County, Clarence T. Johnson, Jr., Senior Judge - Case No. 99-286CFA.



DISPOSITION: This case remanded for a hearing pursuant to rule 3.812.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court, Bradford County, (Florida), denying defendant's motion filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.811 wherein defendant claimed he was not competent to be executed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been sentenced to death and appealed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.811 wherein defendant claimed that he was not competent to be executed. The court remanded the case for a hearing pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.812. The court held that the evidence presented by defendant, which consisted of an expert report and other corroborating evidence of defendant's bizarre behavior, when taken alone, established reasonable grounds to believe that defendant was incompetent to be executed. The evidence presented by the state, which also included expert reports, created questions of fact on this issue. The court held that these factual disputes should be examined and resolved in the crucible of an adversarial proceeding and, thus, remanded the case for such a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for an adversarial hearing to examine and resolve the factual disputes regarding defendant's competency to be executed.

 

13 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Peede v. State


No. 90,002


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


748 So. 2d 253; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1368



August 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Peede v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 4 (Fla., Jan. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Michael Cycmanick, Judge. Case No. 83-1682.
Peede v. Florida, 477 U.S. 909, 106 S. Ct. 3286, 91 L. Ed. 2d 575, 1986 U.S. LEXIS 2223, 54 U.S.L.W. 3841 (1986)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which denied his amended Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion after he was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for first degree murder of his estranged wife. After the trial court denied his amended Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion, defendant sought review. On appeal, the court held defense counsel could not be deemed ineffective for failing to object to jury instructions, which merely inquired whether jury members could follow the law. The court affirmed in part because the state correctly conceded the need for an evidentiary hearing for issues raised as to defendant's mental competency, the adequacy of competency examinations, and the adequacy of counsel's representation for the mental issues. The court reversed in part to require an evidentiary hearing on ineffective assistance of counsel claims, mental competence claims, public records request, and because a factual dispute remained as to whether counsel was ineffective for failing to discover evidence as to defendant's mental history. The court found that defendant alleged sufficient facts about the existence of this mitigation and counsel's failure to investigate or present it that were not refuted by the record. Therefore, an evidentiary hearing should have been held on that claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part because the state correctly conceded that a hearing was needed concerning defendant's mental competency, adequacy of competency examinations, and adequacy of counsel's representation for mental issues. The court reversed in part for a hearing on claims of ineffective assistance, mental competence, and a public records request.

 

14 of 1586 DOCUMENTS



Brennan v. State


No. 90,279


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


754 So. 2d 1; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1186; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 365



July 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised October 21, 1999. Rehearing Denied October 21, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1822. Released for Publication October 21, 1999.
Rehearing denied by Brennan v. State, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1822 (Fla., Oct. 21, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lee County, William J. Nelson, Judge--Case No. 95-911CFB WJN.
Nelson v. State, 748 So. 2d 237, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 904 (Fla., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Death sentence vacated and reduced to life imprisonment without a possibility of parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of the Lee County Circuit Court (Florida), entered upon a jury verdict, and even though he was only 16 years old at the time of the offenses, convicted him of first-degree murder and robbery and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for first-degree murder and robbery, notwithstanding mitigating factors that included the fact that he was only 16 years old at the time of the offenses. On appeal, the convictions were affirmed but the death sentence reversed and reduced to life imprisonment. The court ruled that the convictions were supported by sufficient evidence and allowing a medical examiner to testify as to the cause of death of one victim, even though she had not performed the autopsy, was not an abuse of discretion because the witness made independent conclusions using objective evidence, including the autopsy records. In addition, statements made by a codefendant in defendant's presence were admissible as admissions by acquiescence. However, imposition of the death penalty upon a defendant who was 16 years of age at the time of the offense was cruel or unusual punishment, under Fla. Const. art. I, § 17, and was disproportionate with respect to sentences in other cases. In addition, the scheme set out in Fla. Stat. § 985.225 (1997), which provided that juveniles were subject to the death penalty, was suspect under the U.S. Constitution.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed, but the sentence reversed because, although, inter alia, the convictions were supported by sufficient evidence and admission of expert testimony by a medical examiner who had not performed the autopsy; admissions by acquiescence was proper; and the imposition of the death penalty for a crime committed when a defendant was 16 years of age constituted cruel or unusual punishment under the Florida constitution.


 

15 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


No. 95,845


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


742 So. 2d 233; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1133; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 345



July 1, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Peter Fryefield, Judge - Case No. 82-4752-CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the Duval County Circuit Court (Florida) order that denied petitioner's fourth postconviction motion pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, a motion to inspect the electric chair, and a motion to compel production of public records, after petitioner was convicted of several murders and was placed under a death warrant.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought to prevent the use of the electric chair. The court affirmed denial of petitioner's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion. The Florida courts recently performed numerous reviews of the procedures and electrical engineer evaluations of the Florida electric chair, and the court affirmed the findings that the chair was in excellent condition, performed as expected, and that there was insufficient basis alleged to overcome the presumption that the executive branch would perform its duties properly. There was at most harmless error if due process was violated by the refusal to require production of condition and operation records due to the numerous recent reviews. A PET scan, 17 years after the murders took place and after defendant's counsel testified that defendant remembered the murders, would not produce probative evidence of defendant's mental state at the time of the murders, and was procedurally barred as an abuse of process.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to vacate the judgment and sentence of death, motion for a stay of execution, motion to inspect the electric chair, and motion to compel production of records were affirmed. No motion for rehearing would be permitted.

Gaskin v. State


No. 90,119


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


737 So. 2d 509; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1135; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 341



July 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1999. Released for Publication August 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, S. James Foxman, Judge - Case No. 95-34327.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's summary order on Gaskin's original and amended 3.850 motion and remanded this case with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida), which summarily denied his motion for postconviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 after he was convicted of two counts of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder. After the trial court summarily denied his motion for postconviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, defendant appealed. On appeal, the court found several claims to have been procedurally barred because they were raised on direct appeal. The court affirmed on most issues, but reversed in part the trial court's summary order on defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion and remanded to hold an evidentiary hearing on defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim. The court disagreed with the trial court's denial of defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim arising from trial counsel's status as a deputy sheriff. The court found several claims based on ineffective assistance of counsel legally and facially sufficient to warrant relief despite the failure to raise an appropriate objection or otherwise preserve the issues for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the denial of defendant's motion and remanded to hold evidentiary hearing on defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim. The court disagreed with trial court's summary denial of defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim arising from trial counsel's status as deputy sheriff.

Hall v. State


No. 92,008


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


742 So. 2d 225; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1137; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 350



July 1, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Sumter County, Richard Tombrink, Jr., Judge - Case No. 78-52-CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from the Circuit Court in and for Sumter County (Florida), which denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion after he was sentenced to death following conviction for abduction and murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the abduction and murder of a young woman and was sentenced to death. After the trial court denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion, defendant sought review. On appeal, the record showed that mitigators either were not established or were entitled to little weight. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion because the record reflected that competent, substantial evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that defendant was competent at the time of his resentencing. The court concluded that there was a full and fair evidentiary hearing as to defendant's competency claims in which the judge heard testimony from all relevant defense counsel and from four mental-health experts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the motion because the record reflected that competent, substantial evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that defendant was competent at the time of his resentencing.

 

18 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Shere v. State


No. 91,614


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


742 So. 2d 215; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1130; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 301



June 24, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 24, 1999. Released for Publication August 24, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hernando County, Raymond T. McNeal, Judge - Case No. 88-0028-CF.
Shere v. State, 579 So. 2d 86, 1991 Fla. LEXIS 567 (Fla., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment by the Hernando County Circuit Court (Florida), denying his second motion for postconviction relief, Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, and claiming that he had each received ineffective assistance of counsel, in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI, with respect to his murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: After his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence were upheld on direct appeal, and his first motion for postconviction relief stricken because it was unsworn and legally insufficient, defendant filed a second motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, that asserted 23 claims, including claims that he had been deprived of his right to effective assistance of counsel, in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI. The motion was denied and defendant appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that the vast majority of the claims were either insufficiently presented or procedurally barred because defendant did not identify the alleged error, the claim was decided on direct appeal, or defendant failed to properly raise the issue on direct appeal. Moreover, defendant failed to demonstrate his attorneys' performance was deficient at trial or that the alleged deficiencies rendered the result unreliable, including failure to present certain mental mitigation evidence. His attorneys' tactical and strategic decisions regarding the calling of certain witnesses and presentation of evidence would not be second-guessed.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed because most of the claims were insufficiently presented or procedurally barred and because defendant failed to show he was deprived of effective assistance of counsel; the court would not second-guess his attorneys' tactical and strategic decisions in calling witnesses and presenting evidence; and failure to present mental mitigation did not render the result unreliable.

20 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


H & F Land v. Pan. City


No. 92,299


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


736 So. 2d 1167; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1047; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 264



June 10, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 97-1546. (Bay County).



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the affirmative and decision approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellate court certified the question of whether the Marketable Record Title Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 712, operated to extinguish an otherwise valid claim of a common law way of necessity when such claim was not asserted within 30 years. The appellate court held that it did and upheld a grant of summary judgment to respondent.


OVERVIEW: A corporation conveyed land to a county, which in turn conveyed it to a city airport board, which then conveyed it to respondent. As a result of the original transfer, part of the land retained by corporation became both water- and landlocked. The parties agreed that an implied common law way of necessity over respondent's property was created. However, no notice of a claim to such a way of necessity was ever filed in the public records or asserted by use. Petitioner acquired the remaining land and thereafter filed suit asserting that with its acquisition it also acquired the right to a way of necessity across respondent's land. The appellate court affirmed a grant of summary judgment to respondent but certified the question of whether the Marketable Record Title Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 712, operated to extinguish an otherwise valid claim of a common law way of necessity when such claim was not asserted within 30 years. The court answered in the affirmative and affirmed. The court held that because petitioner's predecessor in title failed to use or record its way of necessity or assert it in any way, MRTA mandated extinguishment of the interest in favor of respondent.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the affirmative and affirmed the lower court's decision. Petitioner's predecessor in title to the implied right asserted by petitioner could have recorded a notice of claim any time within the approximately 14 years following the adoption of the Marketable Record Title Act and the end of the 30-year period following the effective date of the "root" of respondent's title.

 

21 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Metro. Dade County v. Chase Fed. Hous. Corp.


No. 92,536


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


737 So. 2d 494; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1048; 48 ERC (BNA) 1859; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 267



June 10, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Third District - Case Nos. 97-857, 97-50 & 97-49. (Dade County).



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the affirmative and decision approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county appealed a decision of the District Court of Appeal for the Third District (Florida), which determined that the Legislature expressed clear intent to retroactively apply Fla. Stat. ch. 376.3078(3) and (9) because of the comprehensive nature of the Dry Cleaning Contamination Cleanup Act, the fact that the statute applied to contamination that occurred prior to its enactment, and the absence of a savings clause.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county sued defendants, who had leased space to dry cleaning establishments, to recover costs expended in investigating and addressing contamination allegedly caused by drycleaning solvents. Plaintiff also sought an injunction to compel containment of on-site and off-site contamination. Defendants moved for summary judgment claiming immunity under Fla. Stat. ch. 376.3078 of the Dry Cleaning Contamination Cleanup Act (Act) Defendants' motions were granted and the appellate court affirmed but certified the question as to whether the immunity provisions applied retroactively. The court answered the certified question in the affirmative, finding that because the statute provided conditional immunity from liability for contamination occurring before the statute's enactment, the immunity provisions operated retroactively. The court held that a consideration of both the express terms of the Act and its purpose demonstrated that the Legislature intended the immunity provisions to protect entities from suits to recover the costs of rehabilitation even if those costs were incurred before the Act went into effect, as long as the entities were eligible under the statute.


OUTCOME: The lower court's decision was approved and the question of the retroactivity of the Dry Cleaning Contamination Cleanup Act (Act) was answered in the affirmative because the Legislature clearly expressed its intent through the language of the statute as well as the structure and purpose of the Act to apply the immunity provisions found in the statute to preclude plaintiff's lawsuit to recover its rehabilitation costs.

Young v. State


No. 90,207


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


739 So. 2d 553; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1051; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 277



June 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 1, 1999. Rehearing Denied September 15, 1999. Released for Publication September 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Harold Cohen, Judge - Case No. 86-8682 CF A 02.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order entered by Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County (Florida), which denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for first-degree murder despite his claim of self-defense. The trial testimony conflicted as to whether defendant or victim fired the first shot. The jury convicted defendant and, by a vote of 10 to two, recommended a death sentence. After finding aggravating circumstances and few mitigating circumstances, the trial judge sentenced defendant to death. In his sentencing order, the trial judge expressly relied on testimony of a witness as to which shot was fired first. On postconviction, the lower court denied defendant's claim that the state failed to disclose Brady material relating to the testimony of the witnesses as a whole on the issue of which gun was fired first. The court reversed and remanded for a new sentencing hearing, finding that although the alleged Brady violation was not material as to defendant's conviction, it was material to the sentence of death. The court found defendant was not entitled to a self-defense argument on his conviction for felony murder but the evidence as to who shot first was specifically considered by the judge in imposing the death sentence such that the state was obligated to disclose the material cited by defendant.


OUTCOME: The lower court's order was reversed because it erred in limiting the scope of a postconviction evidentiary hearing so as to exclude review of exculpatory evidence that should have been disclosed pretrial. Because of the substance of the Brady information, the court remanded for a new sentencing proceeding before a jury. The discovery sought by defendant was not material as to defendant's conviction but was material as to the sentence of death.

Nelson v. State


No. 89,540


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


748 So. 2d 237; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 904; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 250



May 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised September 30, 1999. Rehearing Denied September 30, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1693. Released for Publication September 30, 1999.
Rehearing denied by Nelson v. State, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1693 (Fla., May 27, 1999)
Related proceeding at Brennan v. State, 754 So. 2d 1, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1186 (Fla., 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Nelson v. Florida, 528 U.S. 1123, 120 S. Ct. 950, 145 L. Ed. 2d 825, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 684 (2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at Nelson v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1570 (Fla., July 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lee County, William J. Nelson, Judge - Case No. 95-911-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Lee County (Florida), which convicted defendant of capital murder and imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and accomplice lured victim to remote street where defendant hit him with a bat. After victim agreed to give them his car, they decided to kill him to avoid being caught. Accomplice then attacked victim with a box cutter, and both continued to strike victim with the bat. Defendant and accomplice fled the state. Accomplice twice made statements to their companions about the crime in the presence of defendant without objection. After being caught, defendant gave an audio and video taped confession. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, finding that although it was error for the trial court to allow a DNA expert to testify regarding a calculation derived from a particular source without establishing that the source was generally accepted in the scientific community, the error was harmless in light of the fact that it actually helped defendant and in light of the confession. The court found defendant's silence in the face of the accomplice's statement about the crime amounted to an admission, and that the lower court properly considered the aggravating and mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed because, while it was error for an expert witness to testify regarding a calculation derived from a particular source without first establishing that the source was generally accepted in the scientific community, the error was harmless. Defendant's silence in the face of his accomplice's statements about the crime amounted to an admission.

Chiles v. State Emples. Attys. Guild


No. 93,665


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


734 So. 2d 1030; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 861; 161 L.R.R.M. 2359; 138 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,664; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 225



May 20, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 1999. Released for Publication June 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District - Case No. 97-2359.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the decision below. Declined to address the additional issue raised by the State.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant governor, sought review of the decision of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) which declared unconstitutional Fla. Stat. Ch. 447.203(3)(j) (1997). That statute prohibited those persons who by virtue of their positions of employment were regulated by the Florida Supreme Court, from engaging in collective bargaining with their government employer .


OVERVIEW: Appellee filed an action seeking declaration that Fla. Stat. ch. 447.203(3)(j) (1997) was unconstitutional. The lower court struck down the statute concluding that it unconstitutionally infringed upon the right of government lawyers to bargain collectively. On appeal, the court found that those government agencies that allowed collective bargaining had not suffered any adverse impact from such collective bargaining. In affirming the lower court, the court held the state did not demonstrate that a blanket ban on collective bargaining by public employees working as attorneys was the least onerous means of protecting the attorney-client relationships between the lawyers and the public entities which employed them. Evidence of collective bargaining procedures in other jurisdictions showed that collective bargaining procedures could be fashioned to accommodate both the public employers' interests in assuring fidelity and competence in their attorneys and the attorneys' constitutional right as public employees to bargain collectively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court which held Fla. Stat. ch. 447.203(3)(j) (1997) to be unconstitutional, because the state had failed to prove the requisite necessity for a wholesale ban on collective bargaining by government lawyers.

Downs v. State, 572 So. 2d 895, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 1191 (Fla., 1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the trial court's order summarily denying all of the claims raised in Downs' motion for postconviction relief.

26 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Alachua County v. State


No. 93,344


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


737 So. 2d 1065; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 803; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 212



May 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Stricken July 19, 1999. Released for Publication July 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Alachua County - Bond Validations. Frederick D. Smith, Judge - Case Nos. 97-3088-CA, 97-3518-CA, 97-4368-CA & 97-4715-CA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court (Florida) in and for Alachua County, in an action by appellant for a complaint of bond validation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a county government, imposed a monthly fee on electric utilities for the privilege of using county rights-of-way to deliver electricity. The ordinance contained a pass-through provision, making the fee a debt of the electric utility customer to the electric utility. The ordinance allowed an electric utility to retain 1 percent of the monthly fee for "collecting and transmitting" the Privilege Fee to the county, which used the revenue for county operations. The ordinance also provided for issuance and sale of bonds for financing of "various capital improvement projects," to be paid by a pledge of the revenue flowing from the Privilege Fee. In order to avoid having the Privilege Fee declared an unconstitutional tax, the county argued that the fee was a reasonable rental fee, a user fee, or a franchise fee. The trial court ruled that the Privilege Fee was an unconstitutional tax and that the bond was therefore invalid. The court held that if the Privilege Fee (or fee) was a tax, it was unconstitutional and void. Because revenue was used to provide general tax relief the use of the fee indicated that it was an unlawful tax that no general law authorized.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the "Privilege Fee" was not a rental fee, as it did not represent a bargained-for agreement between the county and any electric utility. It was unilaterally imposed upon the electric utilities by the county. The county gave nothing up in exchange for the Fee. The Privilege Fee was an unconstitutional tax and the bond was, therefore, invalid.

Collier County v. State


No. 93,802


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


733 So. 2d 1012; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 768; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 206



May 6, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Collier County - Bond Validations Hugh D. Hayes, Judge - Case No. 98-1703-CA.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Collier County (Florida) refusing to validate revenue certificates authorized by a county ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant county, pursuant to a county ordinance, sought to issue revenue certificates to be paid for by a collection of fees authorized by the ordinance. The lower court denied the request for authorization and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the lower court's decision holding that the fee was not a valid special assessment or fee, but rather an impermissible tax, and that it conflicted with the ad valorem taxation scheme enacted by the legislature. The court noted that the fee was enacted only to offset the delay in payment of ad valorem taxes and that the fee had all the indicia of a tax in that it did not confer a specific benefit on the land burdened by the assessment. Therefore, the lower court's decision not to validate the revenue certificates was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The lower court's decision not to validate appellant county's revenue certificates was affirmed because the fee to repay the certificates did not specifically benefit the land burdened with it and was therefore a tax and not an assessment.

Scott v. Butterworth


No. 91,853


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


734 So. 2d 391; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 665; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 195



April 29, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, F. E. Steinmeyer, III, Judge - Case No. 95-4716.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant death row inmate sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida) denying his complaint for disclosure of public records by the attorney general's office. Appellant claimed that the trial court failed to sufficiently review the withheld documents for Brady materials and that the court erroneously ruled that the items withheld by the state were not public records.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a death row inmate, filed a complaint for disclosure of public records by defendant, the attorney general's office. The trial court denied the complaint and granted defendant's motion for summary judgment. Appellant sought review of the denial of his complaint claiming that the trial court failed to sufficiently review the withheld documents for Brady materials and that the court erroneously ruled that the items withheld by the state were not public records. The court affirmed the trial court's order first explaining that, because appellant made a general request for exculpatory material under Brady, it was for the state to decide what information must be disclosed and the state's decision was final unless appellant brought to the trial court's attention that exculpatory evidence was withheld. Further, the court rejected appellant's claim that the trial court erred in ruling that the withheld documents were not public records where the documents consisted almost entirely of handwritten notes and drafts of pleadings constituting mere precursors of governmental records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of appellant inmate's complaint for disclosure of public records explaining that the state's decision as to what information must be disclosed was final unless appellant brought to the court's attention that exculpatory evidence was withheld. Further, the withheld documents were not public records where they consisted of handwritten notes and drafts of pleadings constituting mere precursors of governmental records.

Woods v. State


No. 90,833


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


733 So. 2d 980; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 577; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 183



April 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 15, 1999. Released for Publication June 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, Jerry T. Lockett, Judge - Case No. 96-965-CFA-JL.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida) where he was found guilty of murder and attempted murder and received the death penalty. Appellant asserted the trial court erred in denying his motion for judgment of acquittal, the trial court erred in denying his motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence, the death sentence was disproportionate, and other issues regarding his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of killing two people over a car purchase dispute. Appellant sought review and asserted the trial court erred in denying his motion for judgment of acquittal, the trial court erred in denying his motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence, and other issues regarding his sentence. On review, the court held that the motion for acquittal was properly denied. The appellant merely submitted a boilerplate motion for acquittal without fully setting forth the specific grounds upon which the motion was based. In any event, upon review of the record, the court found no error. The court found no error in the trial court's denial of the motion for new trial even thought appellant claimed newly discovered evidence of innocence. This was because a new witness produced by appellant had several inconsistencies and lacked credibility and because appellant failed to carry his burden to demonstrate that this testimony would have changed the result of the trial. However, the court reversed the death sentence. This was because, under a proportionality review, the facts mitigated the sentence of death. The case was remanded for the imposition of a life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed with reference to appellant's convictions and denied the motion for acquittal and the motion for a new trial. However, the court reversed with respect to the appellant's death sentence due to mitigating factors and proportionality review and remanded the matter for the imposition of a life sentence without the possibility of parole.

DISPOSITION: The certified question answered in the negative, the Fourth District's decision reversing the trial court's order of dismissal with prejudice quashed, and this case remanded for proceedings consistent herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reviewed a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), that reversed an order that dismissed respondent taxpayers' claim with prejudice in an action challenging the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 320.072(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Respondent taxpayers filed a complaint challenging the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 320.072(1)(b). Respondents sought a refund for the taxes paid pursuant to the statute. Petitioner Department of Revenue filed a motion to dismiss the complaint, alleging that respondents failed to comply with Fla. Stat. Ann. § 215.26. The lower court reversed the trial court's order dismissing respondents' complaint as time barred. The court quashed the lower court's reversal and remanded the case, holding that respondents failed to file suit challenging the constitutionality of § 320.072(1)(b) within the three-year time limit prescribed by Fla. Stat. Ann. § 215.26(2). The court held that administrative claims may be avoided and filed in court when the sole basis of a claim is constitutionality. However, the court found that the respondents failed to file the suit within the three-year limitations period. The court quashed and remanded the lower court's reversal of the dismissal of respondents' complaint.


OUTCOME: The court quashed and remanded the lower court's reversal of the dismissal of respondent taxpayers' complaint because respondents failed to file the suit within the three-year limitations period. The court also held that the due process claims were without merit.

Palm Beach County v. Cove Club Invs.


No. 90,750


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


734 So. 2d 379; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 570; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 162



April 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District - Case No. 96-0367 (Palm Beach County).



DISPOSITION: Answered the certified question in the affirmative and, approved the decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which determined that appellee country club was entitled to compensation for lost monthly recreational fee assessments in an inverse condemnation action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant county purchased a residential mobile home lot through eminent domain for a road improvement project. The lot was subject to a restrictive covenant that required the owner of the lot to pay a monthly recreational fee in exchange for the right to use the recreational facilities of appellee country club. Appellee filed an inverse condemnation action against appellant contending that appellant took from it a property right. Appellant contended that having to pay the recreational fee placed an intolerable burden on the county and the public to compensate owners of such restrictions. The lower courts found for appellee. On review, the court held that, under U.S. Const. amend. V, a restrictive covenant imposed a duty which ran with the land taken which constituted a compensable interest. A restrictive covenant was generally deemed a property right under federal law. Therefore, the decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the liability determination against appellant county because the restrictive covenant was deemed a property right under federal law and under the Fifth Amendment. The court held that the restrictive covenant imposed a duty which ran with the land taken and constituted a compensable interest.

Schultz v. Love PGI Partners, LP


No. 92,803


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


731 So. 2d 1270; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 510; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 152



April 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal. Direct Conflict. Fifth District - Case No. 96-1973. (Citrus County).



DISPOSITION: Fifth District's decision below approved, and Robbins v. Yusem disapproved to the extent it is inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An application for review of a decision in direct conflict with another decision was filed from the District Court of Appeal (Florida), on the issue of whether zoned use of land was, as a matter of law, determinative of the actual, good faith, agricultural use of the land for ad valorem tax assessment purposes under Fl. Const. art. VII, § 4(a) and Fl. Stat. § 193.461(3)(b) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Decision of the lower court which conflicted with existing case law was granted review on the issue of whether zoned use of land was, as a matter of law, determinative of the actual, good faith agricultural use of the land for ad valorem tax assessment purposes under Fl. Const. art. VII, § 4(a) and Fl. Stat. § 193.461(3)(b) (1993). The court approved the decision of the lower court and held that when determining the actual, good faith use of the land for tax purposes, the zoned use was but one factor that an assessor or reviewing court could consider along with the other specified factors provided in Fl. Stat. § 193.461(3)(b)1-7 (1993). The court held that the determination of the actual, good faith use of the land for tax purposes also required an evaluation of the various factors surrounding the alleged agricultural use as provided in Fl. Stat. § 193.461(3)(b), which included the duration and continuity of the use, the purchase price and size of the land, whether the land was cared for in a manner to support the alleged use, whether there was a lease and, if so, its terms, and "such other factors" as might have been apparent. The court disapproved the inconsistent case.


OUTCOME: The court approved a decision of the lower court upholding an ad valorem tax assessment on certain land at issue and held that in addition to examining the zoned use of the land for determining the actual, good faith use of the land for tax purposes, the court was required to also evaluate the various statutory factors surrounding the alleged agricultural use.

Jones v. State


No. 90,976


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


732 So. 2d 313; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 446; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 145



March 25, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 25, 1999. Released for Publication May 25, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 05/25/1999
Writ of mandamus denied Jones v. Moore, 794 So. 2d 579, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1362 (Fla., 2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jones v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 824 (Fla., May 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, Philip J. Padovano, Judge - Case No. 88-3111.
Jones v. Florida, 502 U.S. 878, 112 S. Ct. 221, 116 L. Ed. 2d 179, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 4925 (1991)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida), which denied appellant's motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced to death for the first-degree shooting murder of a police officer. Affirming the judgment of the lower court denying appellant's motion for postconviction relief, the court held that appellant had not been denied effective assistance of counsel during the penalty phase of his trial and that appellant had failed to establish that the state had withheld exculpatory material. Because the trial record established that appellant's counsel had motioned the court to appoint a clinical psychologist to help in developing evidence of statutory and non-statutory mitigation and because counsel made reasonable efforts to investigate and present the available mitigating evidence, the court found appellant failed to establish that his counsel was ineffective and, therefore, failed to demonstrate any resulting prejudice. Where appellant's death sentence was based upon numerous objective aggravating factors, the court found that the record supported the trial court's factual findings and imposition of the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court denying appellant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed where appellant failed to present sufficient evidence that he had been denied effective assistance of counsel and where there was sufficient objective evidence of aggravating circumstances which supported the imposition of the death sentence.

 

36 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Musculoskeletal Inst. v. Parham


Nos. 91,966, 92,382, & 92,451


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


745 So. 2d 946; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 365; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 120



March 11, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 30, 1999. Released for Publication April 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Three Cases Consolidated: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case No. 96-03037 (Hillsborough County).



DISPOSITION: Answered the rephrased certified question in the affirmative, approved the decision on review, and amended Florida Rule of Civil Procedure 1.650(d).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a trial court held that respondent's medical malpractice action against petitioners was procedurally barred, the District Court of Appeal, Hillsborough County (Florida), certified the question of whether the extensions of the statute of limitations for medical malpractice suit permitted under Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 766.104(2) and 766.106(4) (1989) also extended the statute of repose contained in § 95.11(4)(b).


OVERVIEW: Respondent filed a medical malpractice suit against petitioners. The trial court held that the suit was barred by the statute of limitations, and on appeal the district court of appeal reversed and remanded, but certified to the court the question of whether the extensions of the statute of limitations for medical malpractice actions allowed by Fla. Stat. Ann. § 766.104(2) and § 766.106(4) (1989), which allowed for the statutorily mandated reasonable investigation of claims, also extended the statute of repose contained in § 95.11(4)(b). The court answered the certified question in the affirmative. It held that solely for the purpose of the statute of repose, an action for medical malpractice was commenced with the service of a notice of intent to initiate litigation pursuant to § 766.106 or on petition to the clerk of the court filed pursuant to § 766.104(2), and that the tolling provisions of these statutes and Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.650(d) applicable to the statute of limitations were equally applicable to the statute of repose in § 95.11(4)(b).


OUTCOME: In response to the certified question, the court held that the notice of intent to initiate litigation and the reasonable investigation requirements which were statutory prerequisites to bring a medical malpractice action applied to toll the medical malpractice statute of repose.

Teffeteller v. Dugger

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


734 So. 2d 1009; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 259; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 110



March 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised June 17, 1999. Rehearing Denied June 21, 1999. Released for Publication June 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus and Two Notices of Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, S. James Foxman, Judge - Case No. 79-931-BB.
Teffeteller v. Dugger, 676 So. 2d 369, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 335 (Fla., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the trial court's order denying Teffeteller's rule 3.850 motion and petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida) that denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for postconviction relief. Appellant also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Subsequently, appellant sought review of the trial court's denial of his postconviction relief motion brought pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. While the court discussed many of appellant's issues raised on appeal, it noted that the substantive claims raised by appellant were procedurally barred because they either could have been raised on direct appeal or were raised on appeal and found to be without merit. In affirming the trial court's decision, the court agreed with the trial court that no evidentiary hearing was necessary because the trial court conducted a lengthy hearing where both sides were allowed to present arguments as to the issues raised in appellant's motion to vacate. Appellant also asserted problems with the assistance he received from his trial counsel. However, the court concluded that neither per se nor actual conflict existed between appellant and his attorney and that appellant failed to show that he was prejudiced in any way by his counsel's performance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's denial of appellant's motion for postconviction relief. The court found the issues raised by appellant on appeal to be moot or to have been waived because they were not raised on direct appeal. Appellant's petition for writ of habeas corpus was also denied.

Fernandez v. State


No. 84,700


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


730 So. 2d 277; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 256; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 102



February 25, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 15, 1999. Released for Publication April 15, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 04/15/1999
Petition denied by State v. Fernandez, 806 So. 2d 492, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 1851 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2002)
Dismissed by Fernandez v. State, 884 So. 2d 942, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17598 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Fernandez v. State, 913 So. 2d 734, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 17223 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Rodolfo Sorondo, Judge - Case No. 92-2141A.
Fernandez v. State, 660 So. 2d 421, 1995 Fla. App. LEXIS 10092 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Appellant's convictions affirmed, his death sentence reversed, and remand for a sentence of life in prison without possibility of parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) following his conviction for murder and the imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death for his part in the death of a policeman during the commission of a robbery. Appellant made several arguments as to the substance of his conviction, but the court found that none of appellant's points of error were meritorious. However, the court did agree with appellant's contention that the sentence imposed was disproportionate to the crime and violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII as cruel and unusual punishment. The court concluded that a death sentence for appellant, who did not directly participate in the actual killing, was disproportionate relative to the life sentences that several co-defendants, who also did not directly participate in the killing, received. It was unconstitutional to permit the imposition of the death penalty on a defendant who aided and abetted a felony in the course of which a murder was committed by others, but who did not himself kill, attempt to kill, or intend that a killing take place or that lethal force be employed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's death sentence was reversed as disproportionate because the evidence demonstrated that appellant did not participate in the actual killing.

Halifax Hosp. Med. Ctr. v. News-Journal Corp.


No. 92,047


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


724 So. 2d 567; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 47; 27 Media L. Rep. 1379; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 46



January 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fifth District - Case No. 96-3115 (Volusia County).



DISPOSITION: The rephrased certified question answered in the negative and held that section 395.3035(4), Florida Statutes (1995), is unconstitutional under article I, section 24(b) and (c) of the Florida Constitution. The decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the question of whether the exemption to the Sunshine Law, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 395.3035(4), was constitutional under the provisions of Fla. Const. art. I, §§ 24(b) and (c).


OVERVIEW: Respondent newspaper brought action against petitioner hospital for declaratory and injunctive relief, challenging the legality of a series of closed meetings held by petitioner. Respondent contended that the closed meetings violated the Sunshine Law, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 286.011. Petitioner argued that the closed meetings were covered under the exemption to the Sunshine Law, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 395.3035(4). The circuit court held that the statutory exemption was unconstitutional and hence the agreement was void ab initio. The court of appeals affirmed and certified the question of whether the statutory exemption was constitutional under the provisions of Fla. Const. art. I, §§ 24(b) and (c). The court held that the exemption was facially unconstitutional because it did not meet the exacting constitutional standard of specificity as to stated public necessity and limited breadth to accomplish that purpose. The court reasoned that the exemption allowed a board to close the portions of their meetings at which written strategic plans were discussed, but the statute contained neither a definition of "strategic plans" nor a justification for the breadth of the exemption.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statutory exemption to the Sunshine Law was facially unconstitutional because it did not meet the exacting constitutional standard of specificity as to stated public necessity and limited breadth to accomplish that purpose.

 

40 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Mem'l Hospital-West Volusia v. News-Journal Corp.


No. 90,835


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


729 So. 2d 373; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 48; 27 Media L. Rep. 1353; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 52



January 21, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 31, 1999. Released for Publication March 31, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction Fifth District - Case No. 96-2608 (Volusia County).



DISPOSITION: Approved the decision of the district court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hospital sought review of a decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeals (Florida) in favor of respondent newspaper in respondent's action seeking a declaratory decree that, pursuant to Fla. Const. art. I, § 24, petitioner's records were subject to the Public Records Act, Fla. Stat. Ann. ch. 119, and that meetings of petitioner's board of directors were subject to the Sunshine Law, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 286.011(1).


OVERVIEW: Respondent newspaper sought a declaratory decree that petitioner hospital's records were subject to the Public Records Act, Fla. Stat. Ann. ch. 119, and that meetings of petitioner's board of directors were subject to the Sunshine Law, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 286.011(1). The lower court found for respondent. On appeal, the court approved the lower court decision. Petitioner was a private nonprofit corporation to which operation of public hospital facilities had been transferred. Petitioner was acting on behalf of a state agency in performing and carrying out obligations under their agreement, and the totality of factors showed that the agency's authorized function had been delegated to petitioner. An exemption from public records access was available under Fla. Const. art. I, § 24, only if the legislature provided by general law for the exemption of records. It was clear that petitioner was acting on behalf of a public agency. The court did not decide the constitutionality of the recently passed Fla. Stat. Ann. § 395.3036, which would have made the records confidential, because respondent did not follow the usual procedure for constitutional challenges.


OUTCOME: The court approved the lower court's decision requiring petitioner to provide access to its records and meetings because a governmental agency had delegated its authorized role to petitioner. The court did not decide whether the statute making petitioner's records was constitutional because the issue had not been raised at the trial level.

 

41 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Dryden v. Madison County


No. 87,594


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


727 So. 2d 245; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 50; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 47



January 21, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court January 22, 1999. Certiorari Denied June 21, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 4224.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case Nos. 95-466 95-978 (Madison County).



DISPOSITION: Our decision in Dryden v. Madison County reaffirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the United States Supreme Court, the court reconsidered its judgment which held that petitioner taxpayer was not entitled to a refund of special tax assessments which were later declared invalid.


OVERVIEW: The county government adopted several ordinances levying special assessments on property located in the county to pay for garbage services, landfill closure, ambulance service, and fire protection. Several years later, the assessments were declared invalid, and petitioner and other residents sought refunds. The trial court found that petitioner was not entitled to a refund. The district court affirmed. The court approved the district court decision. The United States Supreme Court remanded the matter to the court for reconsideration based on its recent decision in a similar case, and the court reaffirmed its decision. The court opined that the U.S. Supreme Court case was inapplicable to the present action because it was a taxpayer remedy case involving a different statute. The court noted that the remedy petitioner chose was never an issue, but instead the parties focused exclusively on the merits of his refund claim. Because the county acted in good faith in levying the assessments, and because the invalid tax scheme applied across the board and conferred a commensurate benefit, equitable considerations precluded a refund to petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court reaffirmed its decision denying petitioner's refund claim. The court ruled that equitable considerations precluded a refund of the assessments because the invalid tax scheme applied across the board and conferred a commensurate benefit on taxpayers.
