Smith v. Welton


Nos. 92,930 & 92,973


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


729 So. 2d 371; 1999 Fla. LEXIS 4; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 41



January 14, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 22, 1999. Released for Publication March 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated on Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District - Case Nos. 96-3777 97-639.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county property appraisers, petitioned for review of judgments of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida) striking down tax assessment valuation increases of appellees' homestead properties after holding that Fla. Stat. § 193.155 (1995) violated Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4. The cases were consolidated by the court on appeal.


OVERVIEW: In two separate cases, appellants, county property appraisers, retroactively increased significantly the assessed value of properties that served as family homesteads after determining that they had mistakenly undervalued improvements to the properties. Appellees, the property owners, filed complaints protesting the increases. Appellants asserted that Fla. Stat. § 193.155(8)(a) (1995) bestowed upon them the authority to reach back and correct an erroneous calculation of the base year "just value" assessment and then apply that corrected value to subsequent years. In both cases, a court eventually struck down the increase in value after it determined that Fla. Stat. § 193.155 (1995) violated Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4, which set forth guidelines for the taxing of homesteads. The court consolidated the appeals. The court affirmed the denials of the retroactive application of the increased valuations, holding that appellants lacked authority under Fla. Stat. § 193.155(8)(a) to retroactively change the base year "just value" assessment of a property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denials of the retroactive application of the increased valuations to appellee property owners homestead properties, holding that appellants, county property appraisers, lacked statutory authority to retroactively change the base year "just value" assessments of the properties.

State v. Lancaster


No. 86,312


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


731 So. 2d 1227; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2577; 24 Fla. L. Weekly S 30



December 24, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 10, 1999. Released for Publication February 10, 1999. As Corrected February 25, 1999. Second Correction March 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. Fourth District - Case No. 94-2471. (Indian River County).



DISPOSITION: Approved the result of the Fourth District's decision finding that the State cannot cancel or forfeit Lancaster's Provisional Credits or his Administrative Gain Time.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of Florida, appealed a decision of the finding of the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida) that the state could not cancel or forfeit respondent inmate's provisional credits or administrative gain time.


OVERVIEW: The case involved the application of ex post facto principles to a legislative change in the gain time statutes. Respondent inmate was given an incarcerative sentence followed by a specified period of probation. Due to the award of several types of gain time including administrative gain time and provisional credits, respondent was released. Respondent violated his probation and it was revoked and he was then resentenced. At that time, respondent was given credit for his previously awarded incentive and basic gain time. However, respondent was not given credit for his previously awarded overcrowding gain time. The court noted that an ex post facto inquiry involved not only looking at the time of offense, but also involved looking at subsequent time frames as well to determine whether a possible, yet speculative benefit had become more definite. The court found that the state could not apply the Safe Streets Initiative, Fla. Stat. ch. 944.278 to respondent to cancel his administrative gain time or provisional credits without violating the Ex Post Facto Clause.


OUTCOME: The holding of the district court finding that the state could not cancel or forfeit respondent inmate's provisional credits or administrative gain time was affirmed because the cancellation or forfeiture would violate the Ex Post Facto Clause.

The Florida Bar v. Ross


No. 89,012


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


732 So. 2d 1037; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2635



December 24, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 6, 1999. Released for Publication May 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - The Florida Bar.

Previously Reported at: 725 So. 2d 373 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.



DISPOSITION: Ross disbarred. Judgment entered against Ross in favor of The Florida Bar for costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A referee's findings of fact and recommendation with regard to alleged ethical violations warranting disbarment of respondent attorney, including fraud in violation of R. Reg. Fla. Bar 4-8.4(c), were submitted for adoption.


OVERVIEW: A referee submitted a recommendation that respondent, a previously suspended attorney, be disbarred for soliciting a bribe in exchange for giving deposition testimony and for avoiding legal service of process. Respondent sought a bribe in exchange for testifying favorably to the landlord in a real estate dispute. The state's highest court held that it had continuing jurisdiction over suspended attorneys such as respondent pursuant to R. Reg. Fla. Bar 3-5.1(e) and pursuant to the court's inherent authority to discipline attorneys who were suspended, disbarred, or had resigned in lieu of facing disciplinary charges by holding such attorneys in contempt of the terms of the court orders under which they were disciplined. The court rejected respondent's argument that R. Reg. Fla. Bar. 4-8.4(c) was unconstitutionally vague, even though the rule left the term "dishonesty" undefined. The referee did not clearly err in finding, as an aggravating factor, that respondent acted with a dishonest or selfish motive. Because respondent's actions undermined the integrity of the judicial process, disbarment was not too harsh a sanction. The court adopted the referee's recommendation.


OUTCOME: The court adopted the referee's recommendation that respondent attorney be disbarred because the court had continuing jurisdiction to discipline respondent, who solicited a bribe in exchange for deposition testimony, for undermining the integrity of the judicial process by acting dishonestly.

State v. Am. Tobacco Co.


Nos. 93,148 and 93,195, No. 93,633


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


723 So. 2d 263; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2199; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 593



November 13, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1998 and December 18, 1998. Released for Publication December 18, 1998. As Corrected December 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Three Cases Consolidated: An Appeal of Judgment of Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Harold J. Cohen, Judge, Case No. 95-1466 AH - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Case Nos. 98-01738; 98-01430; 98-1669 & 98-1747 and an Original Proceeding - Writ of Prohibition.



DISPOSITION: The case remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion. All stays previously entered by this Court and by the district court removed. Any issues remaining in the case which are not within this Court's decision today are to proceed in the circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Florida, on consolidated appeal, sought review of judgments from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County (Florida) and the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida), ordering payment of legal fees to respondents for representing appellant's legal interests in litigation against appellee tobacco companies. Appellant also sought an original writ of prohibition preventing the lower courts from paying respondents.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the State of Florida, challenged on direct appeal, on certified appeal, and on a writ of prohibition the lower courts' decisions ordering appellant to pay respondent attorneys for services rendered in representing appellant's legal interests in litigation against appellee tobacco companies to recover Medicaid expenses for treatment of tobacco-related illnesses. After appellant and the tobacco companies settled, respondents sought payment for services. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court had no authority to order disbursement of funds to respondents based upon their charging liens because the terms of the parties' contract for legal services controlled. Payment of legal fees was contractually based upon a contingency fee percentage of the settlement amount paid to appellant by appellees. The court required respondents to seek payment in a separate and distinct action. In response to the parties' post-appeal filing of a suggestion of mootness, the court dismissed appellant's writ of prohibition but declined to enter a consent degree, remanding the matter to the circuit court for further consideration. The court granted relief to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of appellant State of Florida, holding that respondent attorneys' charging liens against a settlement fund paid by tobacco companies to appellant to cover the costs of treating tobacco-related illnesses were invalid and that the circuit court lacked authority to order appellant to pay respondents' legal fees out of that fund because payment was governed by the parties' contract for legal services.

 

46 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Von Eiff v. Azicri


No. 91,647


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


720 So. 2d 510; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2197; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 583



November 12, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Third District - No. 96-3273 (Dade County).



DISPOSITION: Declared subsection 752.01(1)(a) facially unconstitutional, quashed Von Eiff, disapproved the First District's opinions in S.S. and Sketo, and approved the Fourth District's opinion in Russo and the Fifth District's opinion in Fitts. Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parents challenged the judgment of the Third District Court of Appeals (Florida) that upheld the constitutionality of the Grandparental Visitation Rights statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(a), and allowed respondent grandparents reasonable visitation.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, the biological maternal grandparents, filed a petition for unsupervised visitation with petitioner parents' child, as authorized by the Grandparental Visitation Rights statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(a), alleging that the biological father and adoptive mother had refused reasonable visitation with the child and that such visitation was in the child's best interests. Petitioners countered that they had a fundamental privacy right to determine with whom the child associated and that subsection (1)(a) violated that right. The court noted that while an implicit right of privacy was recognized under the federal constitution, Floridians enjoyed an explicit right of privacy under Fla. Const. art.1, § 23, which granted the citizens of Florida more protection from governmental intrusion than that afforded under the federal constitution. The court found that petitioners possessed a constitutional right of privacy in their decision to limit the grandparents' visitation with their child. The court declared that § 752.01(1)(a) was facially unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court found that a subsection of the Grandparental Visitation Rights statute was facially unconstitutional because government's interference in a parent's decision to exclude or limit grandparental visitation could not be countenanced without a showing of a compelling state interest and no compelling state interest existed. Therefore, the order granting respondent grandparents visitation rights was quashed and remanded.

Knight v. State


No. 87,783


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


721 So. 2d 287; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2196; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 587



November 12, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing and Clarification March 11, 1999, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2651. Released for Publication March 11, 1999. Certiorari Denied November 8, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7479.
Clarified by Knight v. State, 746 So. 2d 423, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2651 (Fla., 1998)
Rehearing denied by Knight v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 406 (Fla., Feb. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County Rodolfo Sorondo, Jr., Judge - Case No. F74-5978.
Knight v. Dugger, 863 F.2d 705, 1988 U.S. App. LEXIS 16770 (11th Cir. Fla., 1988)



DISPOSITION: Knight's sentences of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant death row inmate challenged the death sentences imposed on resentencing by the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant death row inmate was sentenced to death for kidnapping and murder. On death row he murdered a prison guard and was again sentenced to death. A federal appeals court mandated a resentencing proceeding. The resentencing was challenged on the basis of 17 claims of error. The court affirmed, disposing of several claims as procedurally barred. The court also ruled that a detective witness's presence in the courtroom was permitted as sequestration was not required for expert or unique fact witnesses. The jury instructions on consecutive life sentences were adequate because the judge explained that the sentence's total could ensure appellant a life sentence. Appellant was properly excluded from the court room due to his obstructionist behavior. Additionally, prosecutorial misconduct allegations did not warrant voiding the entire proceeding. Finally, the court reviewed the aggravators and mitigators and upheld them, with the exception of the "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravator as no evidence was given of the victim's last hours spent with appellant.


OUTCOME: Appellant death row inmate's death sentences were upheld because his claims of error were either procedurally barred or not supported by the record or rule of law regarding sequestration of witnesses, jury instructions on consecutive life sentences, exclusion from the courtroom for obstructionist behavior, and prosecutorial misconduct. However, the finding that a "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" sentence aggravator existed was reversed.

 

48 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Knight v. State


No. 87,783


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


746 So. 2d 423; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2651



November 12, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing and Clarification March 11, 1999. Released for Publication March 11, 1999. Certiorari Denied November 8, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7479.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Knight v. Florida, 528 U.S. 990, 120 S. Ct. 459, 145 L. Ed. 2d 370, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7479 (1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Knight v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2124 (Fla., Nov. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County Rodolfo Sorondo, Jr., Judge - Case No. F74-5978.

Original Opinion of November 12, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2196.
Knight v. State, 721 So. 2d 287, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2196 (Fla., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Knight's sentences of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contested his death sentence by the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), raising errors as to improper admission of testimony and prosecutorial comments, withholding of sentencing intentions, prejudicial judicial comments, improper rebuttal testimony, violation of the right against self incrimination and to counsel, improper removal of jurors, and imposition of erroneous mitigating factors and aggravators.


OVERVIEW: On direct appeal of a death sentence, several of appellant's claims were procedurally barred where he failed to object to them at trial. The court did find error in granting appellee state's motion to allow a witnessing detective to remain in the courtroom, but his presence did not implicate any of the dangers normally implicit when a witness hears other testimony prior to testifying and was within the lower court's discretion. Where the jury was informed that consecutive life sentences could be imposed, it was sufficient apprised of the consequences of a life recommendation. The court found no error in the jury instructions, and the judge acted within his discretion in removing appellant for disruption. Further, there was no abuse of discretion in the removal of three jurors. The trial court erred in finding the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator, but the error was harmless. In affirming, the court held that appellant's death sentences were proportional to other death sentence cases.


OUTCOME: Finding that appellant's claims were procedurally barred for failure to preserve error, that there was no error in allowing a witness to remain in the courtroom, that removal of a disruptive appellant or jurors was proper, that the sentences were proportional to like situations, and that although error occurred in applying an improper aggravator it was not reversible, the court affirmed appellant's death sentence.

Avatar Dev. Corp. v. State


No. 91,424


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


723 So. 2d 199; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2063; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 552



October 22, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 28, 1998. Released for Publication December 28, 1998. As Corrected December 31, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Fourth District - Case No. 96-1639 (Broward County).



DISPOSITION: Decision of the district court approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners development corporation and individual sought review of a decision from the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) that reversed a trial court's dismissal of respondent environmental agency's criminal charges against petitioners for violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 403.161 (1993) and reversed its holding that the statute was unconstitutional as invalid delegation of legislative policy. The appellate court declared the statute valid.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, a development corporation and an individual, were charged with violating Fla. Stat. ch. 403.161(1)(b) (1993) for failing to comply with special conditions to prevent pollution expressly set out in a dredge and fill permit issued by respondent environmental agency. A trial court dismissed the charges against petitioners because it held the statute unconstitutionally delegated legislative power to impose criminal penalties on pollution violators. The district court of appeal reversed the decision and expressly held the statute was constitutional. On appeal to the state supreme court, the decision of the appellate court was affirmed. The court held that the statute appeared to strike a practical and proper balance between the legislature's function in establishing fundamental policy and an administrative agency's administration and fulfillment of that policy. The court further held that the fact that the statute provided criminal sanctions for the willful violation of administrative rules and regulations was of little consequence where it was the legislature that had declared such acts were unlawful based upon express legislative policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's reversal of the trial court's decision that had found the delegation of power to respondent environmental agency to impose criminal penalties on pollution violators unconstitutional. The court held that the statute constituted a valid delegation of legislative authority to an administrative agency.

Ragsdale v. State


No. 89,657


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


720 So. 2d 203; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1904; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 544



October 15, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Wayne L.Cobb, Judge - Case No. CR86-00091CFAES.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida) that denied his motion to vacate judgment and sentence filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Appellant had been convicted of armed robbery and first degree murder; the trial judge followed the jury's recommendation of a death sentence, finding no factors in mitigation and three factors in aggravation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of armed robbery and first degree murder. The trial judge followed the jury's recommendation of a death sentence, finding no factors in mitigation and three factors in aggravation. Appellant sought review, raising numerous claims. Among other things, appellant claimed that he was deprived of an adversarial testing in the guilt and penalty phases of his trial. For several reasons, the court found that the trial judge properly denied an evidentiary hearing on appellant's claim as to the guilt phase. As to the penalty phase, however, the court found that appellant had stated sufficient allegations of mitigation that were not conclusively refuted by the record to warrant an evidentiary hearing to determine whether counsel failed to properly investigate and present mitigation evidence. The same rationale applied to appellant's claim that he was denied an effective mental health expert. Thus, the order was both affirmed and reversed in part and the trial court was directed to conduct an evidentiary hearing on appellant's contentions that his trial counsel was ineffective and that appellant was deprived of an effective mental health expert.


OUTCOME: The denial of relief to appellant was reversed in part because appellant had stated sufficient allegations of mitigation for warranting an evidentiary hearing to determine whether his counsel failed to properly investigate and present mitigation evidence in the penalty phase of appellant's trial. The trial court was directed to hold an evidentiary hearing on that contention, and as to the claim of deprivation of an effective mental health expert.

52 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ellis


No. 90,729


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


723 So. 2d 187; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1914; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 541



October 15, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 15, 1998. Released for Publication December 15, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District - Case No. 96-3143.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state government sought reversal of the judgment of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) upholding the trial court's finding that the perjury statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 837.02 (1993), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee criminal defendant was charged with perjury. Prior to her trial, she moved to dismiss the charges on the ground that the state perjury statute was unconstitutional because it did not allow the jury to decide the element of materiality. Dismissal was affirmed by an intermediate appellate court, but on further appeal the state supreme court reversed. The court held that the lower courts erroneously relied upon federal precedent dealing with a federal perjury statute that unequivocally made materiality a factual element. While it was true that juries must decide all factual elements, a state legislature was not required to make materiality in a perjury case a factual element. In the case of Florida's perjury statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 837.02 (1993), materiality was not a factual element but was instead a question of law for the court to decide preliminarily. Accordingly, the order was reversed and the case remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's ruling was reversed and the case remanded for trial. Florida's perjury statute was not unconstitutional for taking a factual element away from the jury because the legislature permissibly chose not to define the element of materiality as a factual element.

Brown v. State


No. 89,537


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


721 So. 2d 274; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1891; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 514



October 1, 1998, Decided

Rehearing denied by, 11/30/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Brown v. Florida, 526 U.S. 1102, 119 S. Ct. 1582, 143 L. Ed. 2d 677, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 3082 (1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Brown v. State, 846 So. 2d 1114, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 630 (Fla., 2003)
Motion denied by State v. Brown, 911 So. 2d 793, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1239 (Fla., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Brown v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 945 (Fla., June 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, R. Michael Hutcheson, Judge - Case No. 92-34756CFAES.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgement rendered by the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida) that sentenced him to death for murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree premeditated murder and first-degree felony murder. The jury recommended a sentence of death. The trial court sentenced appellant to death. The trial court found four aggravating factors and two non-statutory mitigating factors. Appellant sought review of the judgment. Appellant argued that the evidence does not support the trial court's finding that the murder was heinous, atrocious, or cruel (HAC). The court reasoned that although the stabbing lasted only for a period of minutes, expert testimony at trial indicated that the victim was alive and conscious during the attack and obviously had moved either in an effort to stand or to evade his attacker. Similar to other case law, the court found that this evidence sufficient to support the trial court's finding that the murder was HAC. Appellant asserted that the evidence was insufficient to support the trial court's finding that the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP). The court affirmed the sentence. The court found that appellant's plan to find a car and kill the person who owned it demonstrated calculation and planning necessary to find the CCP aggravator.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's death sentence because the court found that the heinous, atrocious, or cruel and the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravators were appropriate.

 

54 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Advisory Opinion to the Ag Re Term Limits Pledge


No. 92,162


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


718 So. 2d 798; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1893; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 505



October 1, 1998, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State Attorney General requested review of a proposed citizen initiative amendment to the Florida Constitution dealing with the election-related powers of the Secretary of State.


OVERVIEW: The State Attorney General sought review of a proposed citizen initiative amendment to the Florida Constitution. The ballot concerned a term limits pledge, under which the Secretary of State would permit, but not require, candidates for the United States Congress to pledge to serve a maximum of three terms if elected to the House of Representatives and two terms if elected to the Senate. It would also require that all primary, special, and general election ballots indicate which candidates took the pledge and which broke it. The court concluded that the proposed amendment could not be placed on the ballot. There was no violation of the single subject requirement in the ballot. However, it affected Fla. Const. art. IV and VI, neither of which granted constitutional recognition to the Secretary of State's election-related powers and duties. Florida statutes, not the Florida Constitution, established the Secretary of State as the chief election officer of the state. Fla. Stat. ch. 97.012 (1997). The ballot failed to inform the public that the Secretary of State would be granted discretionary constitutional powers not presently possessed.


OUTCOME: The court issued an advisory opinion that a ballot for a proposed amendment to the state constitution adopting a voluntary pledge for term limits by members of the United States Congress was not permissible. The ballot failed to inform the public that it would grant the Secretary of State new, discretionary constitutional powers.

Chrysler Corp. v. Pitsirelos


No. 90,533


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


721 So. 2d 710; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1684; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 464



September 17, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 10, 1998. Released for Publication December 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Fourth District - Case Nos. 96-0215 & 96-0514 (St. Lucie County).



DISPOSITION: Decision below quashed and this case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner car dealer sought review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, St. Lucie County (Florida), which held that respondent buyer was entitled, under the state's lemon law, to damages for purchase of a car with defects,


OVERVIEW: Respondent buyer purchased a car from petitioner car dealer. After respondent had trouble with the car, he provided notice, and when the defect was not repaired, he obtained favorable arbitration under the state's lemon law. Upon petitioner's filing for de novo appeal, the lower court awarded respondent damages, fees, and costs. Petitioner appealed that decision, which expressly upheld the lemon law, Fla. Stat. ch. 681. On review, the court concluded that the lemon law was constitutional. It also held that under lemon law procedures, the burden of proof was on the party appealing the arbitration board's determination, in this case petitioner. The decision of the arbitration board was properly admitted into evidence below, but it was improperly granted a presumption of correctness. The court therefore quashed the lower court's decision and remanded the case with directions to conduct a new proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision of the lower court and remanded petitioner car dealer's challenge to a decision favorable to respondent buyer under the state lemon laws. The lower court erred in according a presumption of correctness to the arbitration board's decision on the merits of respondent's claims.

Alston v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


723 So. 2d 148; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1676; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 453

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 17, 1998. Released for Publication December 17, 1998.
Rehearing denied by, 12/17/1998
Writ of mandamus denied Alston v. State, 817 So. 2d 844, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 653 (Fla., 2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Alston v. Fla., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 7446 (U.S., Oct. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Aaron K. Bowden, Judge - Case Nos. 95-5326 CF and 94-5373 CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions of first-degree murder and armed robbery from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), and his death sentence for the murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, armed robbery, and armed kidnapping. Appellant challenged the murder and robbery convictions and his death sentence, raising 17 issues on appeal. The court rejected them all and affirmed. Appellant forced the victim into his vehicle with his two assailants, drove to a remote location, ignored the victim's repeated pleas to live, had an accomplice shoot the victim once, and then he shot the victim twice. First, appellant's statements to police were not involuntary and should not have been suppressed. Second, a videotape of appellant's walk-over from the police station to the jail should not have been excluded from evidence, as the trial court properly performed the balancing test under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.403. Third, appellant was not entitled to an instruction on psychotropic medication based only on his assertion in his motion that he was on the medication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's first-degree murder and armed robbery convictions and his death sentence because the court found no error by the trial court in the 17 issues appellant raised on appeal.

OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder. Appellant pleaded guilty and was sentenced to death. Appellant appealed the death sentence and claimed that the prosecution's case improperly focused on appellant's alleged hatred of homosexuals and that the prosecution failed to establish any connection between appellant's alleged hatred and the victim's murder. 58 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Chiles v. Phelps


Nos. 92,474 and 92,730


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


714 So. 2d 453; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1289; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 372



July 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Consolidated Original Proceedings - a Writ of Mandamus and a Writ of Quo Warranto.



DISPOSITION: Petitions denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner governor filed a writ of mandamus challenging the override by respondents, the Florida legislature and its officers, of his vetoes on Committee Substitute for House Bill 1227 and 1597 during their regular session. Petitioners clinic and doctor filed a writ of quo warranto, seeking a determination that respondents exceeded their authority in overriding the petitioner governor's vetoes at the next regular session.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners clinic and doctor filed a writ of quo warranto, alleging that respondents, the state legislature and its officers, exceeded their authority in overriding petitioner governor's veto of Committee Substitute for House Bill 1227. Petitioner governor sought a writ of mandamus challenging the override of the same bill and Committee Substitute for House Bill 1597. The court denied both petitions, noting that because the issues created uncertainty, immediate determination was required. It considered whether respondents violated the Florida Constitution by failing to take up the vetoed bills at the special session and then voting to override them at the next regular session. It held that there was no express requirement that respondents take up the veto messages when they were presented. Without that requirement, the court could not conclude that respondents acted without authority in postponing consideration of the vetoed bills until the next regular session. Thus, the court denied the petitions and held that respondents did not violate the constitution by overriding petitioner governor's vetoes of these bills at the next regular session rather than at the special session.


OUTCOME: Where there was no express requirement that the legislature consider vetoed bills at a special session, there was no violation of the legislature's constitutional authority when it considered those vetoed bills at the next regular session. Therefore, petitioners' writs challenging the authority of respondent, the state legislature and its officers, to override the vetoes were denied.

 

59 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Raydo


No. 91,161


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


713 So. 2d 996; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1202; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 361; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 404



June 25, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions First District - Case No. 96-370 (Escambia County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state applied for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Direct Conflict of Decisions First District, Escambia County (Florida), claiming that the court erred in holding that respondent's plea of nolo contendere could not be used as impeachment evidence to show a prior conviction. Respondent had pled nolo contendere to counts of burglary and petit theft but had proceeded to trial on a robbery count.


OVERVIEW: Following his nolo contendere pleas on counts of burglary and petit theft and was convicted at trial on a count of robbery. The court considered whether a ruling on impeachment was preserved for review where respondent did not testify. The court determined that a lower court's ruling on an impeachment issue did not amount to a constitutional violation unless the subject of the ruling itself had constitutional implications. Because the court did not find an unconstitutional infringement on respondent's right to testify, the lower court's ruling did not rise to an unconstitutional infringement. Thus, the lower court's preliminary ruling did not impermissibly violate respondent's right to testify. The court quashed the lower court's decision, holding that where respondent did not testify, there was no way to assess whether his failure to testify was harmful to his case. Further, he failed to preserve his claim of improper impeachment by not testifying. Finally, his credibility could not be impeached by a nolo contendere plea where there was no conviction entered.


OUTCOME: The court held that respondent had not preserved his claim of improper impeachment for review where he did not testify at his trial and that his credibility could not be impeached by a prior conviction where he had pled nolo contendere because, by the nature of the plea, no conviction was entered.

San Martin v. State


No. 84,702


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


717 So. 2d 462; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1045; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 335



June 11, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied April 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2675. Rehearing Denied September 9, 1998. Released for Publication September 9, 1998.
Rehearing denied by, 09/09/1998
Writ of certiorari denied San Martin v. Florida, 526 U.S. 1071, 119 S. Ct. 1468, 143 L. Ed. 2d 553, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2675 (1999)
Related proceeding at San Martin v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1460 (Fla., Aug. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Rodolfo Sorondo, Jr., Judge. - Case No. 92-2141C.
Fernandez v. State, 660 So. 2d 421, 1995 Fla. App. LEXIS 10092 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 1995)



DISPOSITION: San Martin's convictions affirmed. Death sentence vacated and remanded for imposition of a life sentence without possibility of parole in accordance with the jury's recommendation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment and sentence of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which convicted appellant of first-degree murder of a law enforcement officer, and other violent felonies, and overrode a jury recommendation of life imprisonment and imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of first-degree murder of a law enforcement officer, argued trial court error during the jury selection process. The court disagreed, ruling that alleged prosecutorial misconduct during voir dire was not preserved for review, that no abuse of discretion occurred when requested individual voir dire was refused, and that peremptory challenges could be used by both parties against persons -- not challengeable for cause -- inclined against their interests. While the admission of codefendants' confessions against appellant was error, it was harmless in view of appellant's own confession, freely given following Miranda warnings. Nor was reversal required when the conviction might have rested on an inadequate legal theory without evidentiary support, when an alternative theory existed for which evidence was sufficient. And testimony regarding the officer's last words was admissible to show that he was acting as a law enforcement officer, not a security guard. But the override of a jury recommendation of life imprisonment was reversible error, given such mitigating factors of appellant's borderline intelligence, his brain lesion, and that he was not the triggerman.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed convicting appellant of first-degree murder of a law enforcement officer, and other violent felonies, as alleged errors during jury selection and the trial's guilt phase were either not preserved for review, harmless, or without merit, but trial court's override of jury recommendation of life imprisonment and imposition of death sentence reversed, as mitigating factors -- appellant was not armed -- supported recommendation.

State v. Mancino


No. 90,516


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


714 So. 2d 429; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1166; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 301



June 11, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District - Case No. 97-00409 (Pinellas County).



DISPOSITION: Mancino approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed the denial of respondent inmate's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion for credit for time served and held that Rule 3.800 was a proper vehicle for raising a credit time issue where credit could be determined from court records. That court then certified the question for review because its decision was in direct conflict with other district court of appeal decisions.


OVERVIEW: Respondent inmate entered pleas of no contest and was sentenced in two cases. He then made a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion requesting jail credit and alleged that court records reflected that he was entitled to credit for time spent in county jail but that he had not received credit at sentencing. On appeal from a denial of the motion, the lower court reversed, holding that Rule 3.800 was a proper vehicle for raising credit time issues. The lower court certified the opinion in which it so held as being in direct conflict with other district court opinions. The court affirmed the lower court's decision, holding that credit time issues were cognizable in a Rule 3.800 motion when it was affirmatively alleged that the court records demonstrated on their face an entitlement to relief. The court noted that failure to grant proper jail credit for time served created an illegal sentence under Rule 3.800 because Fla. Stat. ch. 921.161(1) (1995) affirmatively mandated that no sentence could be imposed without crediting a defendant with jail time already served. The court determined that such an illegal sentence could be corrected at any time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's reversal of the denial of respondent inmate's motion for credit for time served because that credit time issues were cognizable in a post-conviction motion when it was affirmatively alleged that the court records demonstrated on their face an entitlement to such relief.

Benedith v. State


No. 89,368


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


717 So. 2d 472; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1053; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 303



June 11, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 10, 1998. Released for Publication September 10, 1998.
Rehearing denied by, 09/10/1998
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Transferred by Benedith v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1542 (Fla., July 5, 2011)
Dismissed by, Motion denied by, As moot Benedith v. State, 147 So. 3d 520, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 2302 (Fla., 2014)
Petition dismissed by Benedith v. State, 173 So. 3d 960, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 1481 (Fla., 2015)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Benedith v. Jones, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 2246 (Fla., Oct. 6, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Notice and Cross-Notice of Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, John Dean Moxley, Jr., Judge. - Case No. 93-15786-CFA.



DISPOSITION: Convictions for armed robbery and first-degree murder affirmed. appellant's death sentence vacated. We direct that upon remand he be sentenced to life imprisonment without eligibility for parole for twenty-five years.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Brevard County (Florida) that convicted him of first-degree felony murder, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: A witness observed appellant and another man with the victim beside a car in a motel parking area. The witness heard gunshots and saw the victim's body on the ground. The witness observed the other man get out of the vehicle before it sped away. The police found victim's car abandoned a few blocks from the murder scene. Appellant's fingerprints were on the car. Appellant was later found with the murder weapon. He was convicted of first-degree premeditated murder and robbery with a firearm. Appellant was sentenced to death. He sought review. The court affirmed the conviction because there was sufficient evidence from which the jury could have inferred guilt to the exclusion of all other inferences. Even though there was sufficient evidence that appellant robbed and murdered the victim, the death sentence was a disproportionate punishment for the crime because there was not proof of appellant's mental state beyond a reasonable doubt that he actually killed victim. Mere participation in a robbery that resulted in murder was not enough culpability to warrant the death penalty, thus the case was remanded and with instructions to sentence appellant to life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of first-degree premeditated murder and robbery with a firearm was affirmed because there was sufficient evidence from which the jury could have inferred guilt. The court reversed appellant's death sentence because the record lacked competent, substantial evidence to support that appellant had a culpable state of mind.

Mordenti v. State


No. 89,959


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


711 So. 2d 30; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 946; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 287



May 28, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, J. Rogers Padgett, Judge - Case No. 90-3870.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of decision from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) denying his motion to vacate judgment filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Appellant alleged the trial court erred in summarily denying motion to vacate without holding any type of hearing. Appellant argued under Huff decision a hearing was required to allow attorneys the opportunity to argue the merits of holding an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of decision denying his motion to vacate judgment filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Appellant was convicted of conspiracy to commit murder and first degree murder. Appellant argued the trial court erred in denying his motion to vacate without holding any type of hearing. Appellant alleged that under the Huff decision, a hearing was required to allow the attorneys the opportunity to argue the merits of holding an evidentiary hearing. The prosecution conceded that a Huff hearing was required; however, it asserted that the error was harmless. The court reversed the judgment and concluded that pursuant to Huff, trial judges must allow attorneys in a capital case the opportunity to be heard on an initial Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion. Such a hearing was necessary due to the severity of the punishment at issue in death cases. The purpose of a Huff hearing was to allow the trial judge to determine whether an evidentiary hearing was required and to hear legal argument relating to the motion. The court concluded appellant was entitled to be heard on legal arguments as to why an evidentiary hearing was necessary.


OUTCOME: In an appeal from denial of a motion to vacate judgment, the judgment was reversed. Appellant was convicted of conspiracy to commit murder and first degree murder. The action was remanded for a Huff hearing at which the trial court must allow appellant's counsel an opportunity to be heard on the motion. Trial judges must allow attorneys in a capital case the opportunity to be heard on an initial motion to vacate judgment.

Brown v. State


No. 90,891


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


715 So. 2d 241; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 860; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 266



May 14, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 95-3308 (Leon County).



DISPOSITION: Question certified to be one of great public importance. Decision below approved and disapproved Tascarella, Vallieres, J.T., and Heller to the extent they conflict with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A question was certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida) as to whether an exceptional circumstance extension under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(l) was valid when made and obtained during the 5/10-day recapture window provided for in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(p)(3).


OVERVIEW: The district court certified a question as to whether an exceptional circumstance extension under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(l) was valid when made and obtained during the 5/10-day recapture window provided for in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(p)(3). Petitioner asserted such an extension was valid only where made and obtained before the expiration of the basic 175-day period provided in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(a). The court held Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191 contained three time periods: Rule 3.191(a) provided a speedy trial period for those cases in which speedy trial was not demanded; Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(b) provided a speedy trial period for those cases in which a speedy trial was demanded; and Rule 3.191(p)(3) provided a grace period for the state in those cases which eclipsed the times set out in Rules 3.191(a) and (b). The court held under the plain language of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(i), the state was entitled to request an extension of any of the time periods contained in Rule 3.191, so long as the time period it sought to have extended had not expired at the time the extension was requested.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the affirmative, holding that under the plain language of the rule, the state was entitled to request an extension of any of the time periods contained in Rule 3.191, so long as the time period it sought to have extended had not expired at the time the extension was requested.

Havill v. Scripps Howard Cable Co.


Nos. 87,357 & 87,381


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


742 So. 2d 210; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 617; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 234



April 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 10, 1999. Released for Publication June 10, 1999. As Revised June 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fifth District - Case Nos. 94-731 & 94-1301. (Lake County).



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the negative and the decision Fifth District Court of appeal approved and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appraiser appealed a decision from the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) which reversed the trial court's ratification of the appraiser's tax assessments, and the district court certified the question of whether the income/unit rule method of appraisal was an appropriate method of assessing the tangible personal property of television cable companies.


OVERVIEW: Respondent cable company challenged the county's ad valorem tax assessment of its tangible personal property by petitioner appraiser for four years. Petitioner's assessments were based on the income/unit rule method of valuation. The district court reversed the trial court's ratification of the tax assessments and certified the question of whether the income/unit rule method of appraisal was an appropriate method of assessing the tangible personal property of television cable companies. The court noted that the Fla. Const. prohibited local government entities from levying ad valorem taxes on intangible personal property. It then found that that insofar as both the income and unit rule methods taxed intangible property, they were an unconstitutional method for use with cable companies. The court further found that the reassessment for the 1989 tax year was done without authority because the 1989 tax rolls had been certified and the taxes were paid before reassessment could occur. Thus, the decision of the district court was approved.


OUTCOME: Decision reversing the ratification of petitioner appraiser's tax assessments was approved and the certified question answered in the negative because the local government was prohibited from levying ad valorem taxes on intangible personal property and both the income and unit rule methods taxed intangible property, and the 1989 reassessment was improper because the tax rolls had been certified and the taxes paid.

State Ex Rel Butterworth v. Kenny


No. 92,343


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


714 So. 2d 404; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 618; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 229



April 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 13, 1998. Released for Publication July 13, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Quo Warranto.



DISPOSITION: Petitions granted and writ of quo warranto.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an attorney, petitioned the court for a writ of quo warranto seeking to prevent respondents, the Office of the Capital Collateral Regional Counsel for the Southern and Northern Regions and others, from representing death row inmates in civil rights lawsuits and to require withdrawal of their representation from all such pending civil cases.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, an attorney, petitioned the court for a writ of quo warranto seeking to prevent respondents from representing death row inmates in civil rights lawsuits and to require withdrawal of their representation from all such pending civil cases. Respondents initiated a lawsuit seeking declaratory and injunctive relief regarding whether the functioning of Florida's electric chair rendered it an unconstitutional method of execution. The court granted the petition and found that respondents were not statutorily authorized to initiate the federal civil rights action. The court found that respondents' representation was limited by statute to actions challenging the validity of a defendant's conviction and sentence such as habeas corpus, coram nobis, and actions established by the court in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, 3.851, and 3.852. Respondents' representation was limited to traditional postconviction relief actions that challenged only the validity of the conviction and sentence, and the representation did not include the authority to bring civil actions challenging the means and the methods of carrying out a validly imposed sentence.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's request for relief, finding that respondents did not have the authority to bring civil actions challenging the means and the methods of carrying out a validly imposed sentence.

Mahn v. State

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded with directions.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida), which imposed the death penalty upon defendant after he was convicted of first-degree murder.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder, but reversed the death sentence and remanded for resentencing. A review of the record revealed no advanced planning or preconceived design by defendant to kill his victims, and the court found no evidence of heightened premeditation to show beyond a reasonable doubt a finding of cold, calculated, or premeditated behavior.

Remeta v. State


No. 92,670


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


710 So. 2d 543; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 485; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 189



March 29, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, Carven D. Angel, Judge - Case No. 85-1471-CFA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, who was scheduled to be electrocuted on a certain date, challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Marion County (Florida), which denied his motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 to vacate his judgment and sentence of death. Appellant previously had been convicted of several first degree murders in Kansas, and after being extradited to Florida, he was sentenced to death for another first degree murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murders, among other crimes, in various states. For multiple first degree murders committed in Kansas, appellant received consecutive life sentences. After extradition, appellant later was convicted in Florida of first degree murder and was sentenced to death. After various denials of relief in state and federal court, appellant filed a second motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 (Rule 3.850) to vacate his judgment and death sentence; the trial court denied appellant's claims, finding them procedurally barred for several reasons. On review, the court found that appellant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel based on an alleged lack of funding for a defense counsel agency to investigate new leads was without merit, because appellant had had made no showing as to why the discovery of that newly discovered evidence was not available through due diligence either at the time of trial or within the time limits set forth in Rule 3.850. Even if appellant was able to overcome the due diligence element, he failed to establish that the new leads would have resulted in an acquittal on retrial. Among other findings, the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The denial of appellant's motion to vacate his judgment and death sentence for his conviction of first degree murder was affirmed, because the court held, among other findings, that appellant failed to show why discovery of new evidence was not available through due diligence either at the time of trial or within a procedural rule's time limits. Appellant also did not establish that the new leads would have resulted in an acquittal on retrial.

State v. Hootman


No. 91,105


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


709 So. 2d 1357; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 480; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 164



March 26, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal of Judgment of Circuit Court, in and for Pinellas County, Raymond O. Gross, Judge, Case No. CRC96-02944DFANO-K - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Second District, Case No. 97-02118.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the trial court approved and held that section 921.141(5)(m) may not be retroactively applied against Hootman.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, in and for Pinellas County (Florida), which found that Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(m) could not be retroactively applied to respondent, who was charged with first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was charged with first-degree murder. After the grand jury indictment, the prosecution filed a written notice of its intent to seek the death penalty pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(m), which was enacted after the date of the murder. Respondent argued that the application of the new law to his case violated the ex post facto clauses of Fla. Const. art. I, § 10 and U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1. The trial court agreed and the prosecution sought review. The court affirmed, finding that Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(m) could not be applied to respondent because the change in law was substantive where it altered the definition of criminal conduct or increased the penalty by which a crime was punishable, and its retroactive application to respondent would be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision finding that state statute could not be retroactively applied to respondent charged with first-degree murder because the statute was substantive in nature and increased the potential penalty for respondent, whose crime was committed prior to enactment of the aggravating factor.

Bitterman v. Bitterman


Nos. 90,074 & 90,075


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


714 So. 2d 356; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 481; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 168



March 26, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 17, 1998. Released for Publication July 17, 1998.
Certiorari Denied March 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1690.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Fourth District - Case Nos. 94-0411 & 94-0412 (Palm Beach County).



DISPOSITION: Result of the district court's decision approved in part and disapproved in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeals (Florida) affirmed the probate court's judgment, which granted additional attorney fees under Fla. Stat. ch. 733.6171(7) (1993) to appellee attorney (the appointed administrator ad litem) and appellee attorneys of petitioner co-personal representative. Petitioner appealed, raising a conflict over the issue of the point in time when appellee attorneys' substantive right to collect attorney fees vested.


OVERVIEW: The testator died in 1991. Pursuant to the will, petitioner and another brother were appointed co-personal representatives. Because bitter conflict marked the administration of the estate by 1992, each personal representative retained separate attorneys and all parties agreed to the probate court's appointment of appellee attorney to serve as administrator ad litem. After a settlement was reached, the lower courts ruled that petitioner's attorneys and appellee administrator ad litem were entitled to attorney fees under Fla. Stat. ch. 733.6171(7) (1993). Finding that appellee attorneys' substantive rights derived from the former statute, ch. 733.617(1) (1991), that was in effect when their representation began, the court held that the attorneys had no right to recover under ch. 733.6171(7), which did not take effect until 1993. Although ch. 733.6171(7) could have no retrospective effect, the court nevertheless sustained the award of attorney fees to appellee attorneys because petitioner's egregious conduct provided grounds for applying the inequitable conduct doctrine -- a limited exception to the general American Rule that each party must bear its own attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court disapproved of the lower court's reasons for awarding additional attorney fees to appellee attorney (the appointed administrator ad litem) and appellee attorneys of petitioner co-personal representative, holding that the new statute did not take effect until after appellee attorneys began their representation. The court approvedthe result, however, because petitioner's egregious conduct made the inequitable conduct doctrine applicable.

Buenoano v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a prisoner under sentence of death and a third death warrant, challenged an order from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) denying her motion for postconviction relief and her request for a stay of execution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the murder of her husband by arsenic poisoning, and was sentenced to death. At the trial, evidence was introduced regarding the death of a second man with whom appellant lived and the poisoning of a third man. An FBI agent's lab report about the capsules given to the third poisoning victim was admitted at the trial, but the FBI agent was later investigated for his performance. Appellant filed numerous public document requests and suits requesting information about this investigation, and based her third motion for postconviction relief on the documents she received, arguing, inter alia, that they were exculpatory Brady materials. The trial court summarily denied the motion, and she appealed. The court agreed that there was no reasonable probability that the result of the proceedings would have been different had the evidence regarding the agent's problems at the FBI laboratory been disclosed to the defense. The verdict and sentence were affirmed because there was no reasonable probability that the new evidence would result in an acquittal or recommendation of life on retrial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for postconviction relief because even if the information was considered newly discovered, because it could not have been known by appellant or her counsel at the time of trial by the use of due diligence it was not of such a nature that it would probably produce a different result on retrial.

Doe v. Mortham


No. 88,677


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


708 So. 2d 929; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 470; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 153



March 19, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal of Judgment of Circuit Court, in and for Leon County, Nikki Ann Clark, Judge, Case No. 96-630 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 96-2583.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida), which declared several Florida statutes facially unconstitutional, the District Court of Appeal, First District, certified that the order involved issue of great public importance and thereby required the court's resolution. The statutes at issue, Fla. Stat. ch. 106.071, 106.143, and 106.144 (1995), all concerned campaign advertising and financing.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed for a declaratory judgment that Fla. Stat. ch. 106.071, 106.143, and 106.144 (1995), all governing campaign advertising and financing, were unconstitutional on grounds that the statutes were overbroad and infringed on their right to engage in anonymous political advocacy under U.S. Const. amend. I. The trial court denied the complaint and the appellate court certified the issue to the court. Appellants argued on appeal that the reporting and identification requirements of the statutes were overbroad and violated two United States Supreme Court decisions. The court held that the statutes were not substantially overbroad, and thus were not facially unconstitutional. The court saw no reason to discard the statutes in toto because the rights of some Florida citizens might be chilled in some way. Moreover, Florida courts were capable of addressing any infirmity in the statutes that could be alleged in the future on an "as applied" basis. As such, the court found that its construction of the statutes was not incongruous with the United States Supreme Court decisions, and it affirmed the trial court's order upholding the statutes' constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order upholding the constitutionality of several Florida statutes governing campaign advertising and financing was affirmed, because the court held that the statutes were not substantially overbroad and thus were not facially unconstitutional in light of United States Supreme Court decisions. The court also found that the state courts were capable of addressing any future claims of infirmity on an "as applied" basis.

Johnson v. Butterworth


No. 89,022


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


713 So. 2d 985; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 447; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 385



March 19, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Withdrawn from Bound Volume.
Released for Publication April 3, 1998. As Revised on Denial of Rehearing July 9, 1998. Released for Publication July 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, F. E. Steinmeyer, III, Judge - Case No. 95-3894.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state death row prisoner sought to overturn a ruling from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida), which denied appellant's lawsuit seeking to compel appellee state attorney general to disclose certain internal office documents dealing with appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state death row inmate filed suit against appellee state attorney general, seeking compelled disclosure of appellee's records with respect to appellant. The trial court, after reviewing the requested documents in camera, denied appellant's request, finding that the documents in question were either not public records or were exempt from disclosure. On direct appeal to the state supreme court, the trial court's ruling was affirmed. The state supreme court held that the documents in question were simply preliminary guides intended to aid the attorneys when they later formalized the knowledge, and not final evidence of knowledge obtained in connection with the transaction of official business. Under the state's public records act, Fla. Stat. ch. 119, the documents did not fall within the definition of public record. The trial court thus did not err, and its ruling was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying compelled disclosure of internal documents dealing with appellant state death row priosoner was affirmed. The documents did not seek final evidence of knowledge obtained in connection with the transaction of official business, and thus did not qualify as public records under the state's public records law.

Pierpont v. Lee County


Nos. 90,357, 90,573 & 90,775


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


710 So. 2d 958; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 390; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 133



March 12, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 1, 1998. Released for Publication June 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Three Consolidated Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District - Case Nos. 95-04657; 96-00552 & 96-01360 (Lee County).



DISPOSITION: Question certified of great public importance. Disapproved in part and approved in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, § 3(b)(3), (4), the District Court of Appeal, Lee County (Florida), certified a question of great public importance concerning the payment of attorney fees to petitioner landowners under the eminent domain statute contained at Fla. Stat. Ann. § 73.092 (Supp. 1994).


OVERVIEW: Respondent county filed eminent domain proceedings in three separate cases, and there was a dispute over the amount of attorney's fees to be paid by respondent county under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 73.092 (Supp. 1994). Petitioner landowners alleged that benefits should be determined by subtracting respondent's good-faith estimate of value from the amount that was finally paid for the land. Respondent asserted that benefits achieved for the client were based upon the difference between the amount of respondent's written offer and the ultimate award. The trial court accepted petitioner landowners' arguments and awarded the larger amount of attorney's fees. The appellate court reversed, finding that the good-faith estimate of value did not constitute a written offer as contemplated by Fla. Stat. Ann. § 73.092(1)(a) (Supp. 1994). The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court and held that a good-faith estimate of value did not constitute a written offer as set forth in Fla. Stat. Ann. § 73.092 (Supp. 1994). Therefore, the court found that attorney fees were calculated based upon a percentage of the difference between the amount of respondent's written offer and the ultimate award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, finding that the language of the eminent domain statute did not permit the court to conclude that a good faith estimate of value was the equivalent of a written offer for purposes of awarding attorney fees to petitioner landowners.

Kalway v. Singletary


No. 89,724


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


708 So. 2d 267; 1998 Fla. LEXIS 297; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 102



February 26, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 15, 1998. Released for Publication April 15, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District - Case No. 96-00425 (Hardee County).



DISPOSITION: Kalway approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District, Hardee County (Florida), which denied his petition for writ of mandamus as time-barred under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 95.11(8) (1995).


OVERVIEW: During a routine inspection of petitioner's prison cell, officers discovered fifteen gallons of a heady brew and charged petitioner with manufacturing an unauthorized beverage. Following a hearing petitioner was disciplined. After his administrative appeals were denied, he filed a petition for writ of mandamus, which was denied as time-barred under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 95.11(8) (1995), and the district court affirmed. Petitioner then claimed that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 95.11(8) (1995), constituted a violation of the separation of powers doctrine. Upon review, however, the court noted that the interplay between Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.630, which set forth general filing requirements, including time restrictions, and Fla. Stat. Ann. § 95.11(8) (1995), which provided the specific time for prisoners seeking relief from disciplinary action taken by the Department of Corrections, was not anomalous and did not constitute a separation of powers violation. Consequently, the court approved the decision.


OUTCOME: Decision, which denied petitioner's writ of mandamus as time-barred, was approved as proper, where relevant statute did not constitute a separation of powers violation.

DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the affirmative, First District's opinion quashed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was a certified question from the First District Court of Appeal, Bay County (Florida), regarding whether a warrantless seizure of a motor vehicle under the Florida Contraband Forfeiture Act, Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 932.701-932.707, violated U.S. Const. amend. IV so as to render the evidence seized in a subsequent inventory search of the vehicle inadmissible in a criminal prosecution. Petitioner was convicted of cocaine possession.


OVERVIEW: After the appellate court affirmed his conviction for cocaine possession, petitioner sought review, claiming that respondent state's warrantless seizure of his car was error. The lower court certified a question to this court regarding whether the warrantless seizure of a car under a forfeiture act, absent other exigent circumstances, violated U.S. Const. amend. IV so as to render evidence seized in a subsequent inventory search of the vehicle inadmissible in a criminal prosecution. The court answered the certified question in the affirmative. The court quashed affirmation of petitioner's conviction and remanded because it held that a citizen's property was protected by the federal and Florida constitutions against warrantless seizure even when the seizure was done pursuant to a statutory scheme for forfeiture. The court found that the automobile exception to the warrant requirement was inapposite in the case.


OUTCOME: The court quashed affirmation of petitioner's conviction and remanded because it held that a citizen's property was protected by the federal and Florida constitutions against warrantless seizure even when the seizure was done pursuant to a statutory scheme for forfeiture.
