Cole v. State


No. 87,337


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


701 So. 2d 845; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1436; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 587



September 18, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 29, 1997. Released for Publication October 29, 1997. Certiorari Denied March 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2208.
Writ of certiorari denied Cole v. Florida, 523 U.S. 1051, 118 S. Ct. 1370, 140 L. Ed. 2d 519, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2208 (1998)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Post-conviction relief denied at Cole v. State, 841 So. 2d 409, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 34 (Fla., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Cole v. State, 895 So. 2d 398, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2117 (Fla., 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Cole v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2752 (Fla., Dec. 17, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, William T. Swigert, Sr., Chief Judge Case No. 94-498-CF-A-X.



DISPOSITION: Each conviction affirmed. Additionally, the death sentence affirmed. However, in issue thirteen, Cole contends and the State concedes that the trial court erred in sentencing Cole to a twenty-five year minimum mandatory sentence for each of the other felony convictions. Therefore this case remanded to the trial court to impose an appropriate sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Florida), on the basis that his conviction for first degree murder and the imposition of the death penalty resulted from the trial court's abuse of discretion in the admission of certain evidence and in the handling of aggravating and mitigating factors.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of first degree murder along with various other crimes and was sentenced to death. On review, appellant raised various contentions challenging his conviction and sentencing. The court held that the record contained competent, substantial evidence to support the convictions and affirmed the judgment of the trial court and the death sentence. The court found that the portion of the surviving victim's testimony which was reread to the jury was directly responsive to the jury's request and was not misleading and did not place undue emphasis on portions prejudicial to appellant. Because the victim-impact evidence was limited to that which was relevant under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 921.141(7), there was no reversible error in allowing the introduction of the evidence. There was competent, substantial evidence to support the trial court's findings regarding aggravating factors. The trial court also afforded the nonstatutory mitigation factors their appropriate weight. In light of the determination regarding aggravating and mitigating circumstances, the court found that under the proportionality review the imposition of the death penalty was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for first degree murder and the imposition of the death penalty on the basis that the trial court did not abuse its discretion and that there was competent substantial evidence to support the conviction and sentence.

 

104 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Elledge v. State


CASE NO. 83,321


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


706 So. 2d 1340; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1443; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 597



September 18, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing March 5, 1998. Released for Publication March 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Charles M. Greene, Judge - Case No. 75-87CF. Cir. Crt. Case No. 75-87CF (Broward County).



DISPOSITION: Sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court, Broward County (Florida), where the trial court denied his motion for rehearing on the application of mitigating factors to his sentence. Appellant had been sentenced to death following his plea of guilty to the crime of murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to rape, murder, and robbery. Following numerous rehearings, appellant was, for the fourth time, sentenced to death for the murder. Appellant challenged his death sentence. The Supreme Court of Florida affirmed and held that appellant had full understanding of the significance of his plea and its voluntariness as required by Florida Rule of Criminal Procedure 3.170(j). Appellant's confessions and guilty plea were properly admitted. The supreme court found its later decision on confessions and guilty pleas, rendered almost seventeen years after the plea was entered, inapplicable. Reconsideration of the law of the case was warranted only in exceptional circumstances and where reliance on the previous decision would result in manifest injustice, neither of which applied to the case in question. Appellant objected to the trial court's ordering a mental examination under Florida Rule of Criminal Procedure 3.202(d). Although Rule 3.202 became effective three years after appellant's resentencing, the supreme court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by compelling the exam.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for rehearing on the issue of mitigating factors relating to his death sentence, and affirmed his sentence of death, because appellant had full understanding of the significance of his plea and its voluntariness. The trial court's order of a mental examination, three years after appellant's resentencing, was not an abuse of discretion.

 

105 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mitro


No. 89,249


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


700 So. 2d 643; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1358; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 532



September 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 21, 1997. Released for Publication October 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Third District - Case No. 95-2995 (Dade County).



DISPOSITION: District court's decision quashed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision from the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed appellee's conviction for issuing identification cards without proper proof of age in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 877.18 (1993) and declared the statute invalid.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was convicted of violating Fla. Stat. ch. 877.18 (1993) because he issued identification cards without having the recipients present proper proof of age as established in Fla. Stat. ch. 232.03 (1993). The district court reversed appellee's conviction because it held that Fla. Stat. ch. 877.18 (1993) was vague. The district court held that the reference to Fla. Stat. ch. 232.03 (1993), which only applied to children under 16 years old, was ambiguous as to whether the documentation requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 877.18 (1993) applied to all applicants or only those under 16 years old. On appeal, the supreme court quashed the district court's decision and remanded for further proceedings. The statute was not vague because Fla. Stat. ch. 877.18 (1993) set forth the methods of acceptable proof of age for both children and adults. The legislature would have been better served setting out the proof of age requirements, rather than referring to Fla. Stat. ch. 232.03 (1993), but the reference did not make Fla. Stat. ch. 877.18 (1993) ambiguous.


OUTCOME: The supreme court quashed the decision and remanded the action for further proceedings. The statute, making it unlawful to issue identification cards without proper proof of age, was not vague because it set forth the methods of acceptable proof of age for children and adults.

 

106 of 1586 DOCUMENTS



Walker v. State


No. 84,113


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


707 So. 2d 300; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1353; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 537



September 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied March 24, 1998. Released for Publication March 24, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Michael H. Salmon, Judge - Case No. 93-28436A.



DISPOSITION: All of Walker's convictions and his sentences for noncapital felony offenses affirmed, but case remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Dade County (Florida), convicting him of first degree murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, arguing that the evidence concerning his desire that his victim abort their child was unduly prejudicial and inadmissible under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 90.403, that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress his confession on the grounds that his right to counsel was violated when he indicated to the interrogating officers his desire to have a lawyer, and that the trial court erred in denying his motion for mistrial immediately after a witness referred to defendant's purported commission of an uncharged offense. The court ruled that although § 90.403 was mandatory in its exclusion of unduly prejudicial evidence, a large measure of discretion rested in the trial judge to determine whether the probative value of the evidence was substantially outweighed by its prejudicial effect. Further, the court held that a trial court's ruling on a motion to suppress was accorded great deference and that the trial court's denial of defendant's motion was supported by the record. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that a mistrial was not warranted based on the error by the testifying witness.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant was affirmed and remanded for a reconsideration as to the sentences for capital felonies where the police did not lack probable cause to arrest defendant during his interrogation, discrete instances of prosecutorial misconduct were harmless beyond a reasonable doubt and did not warrant a new sentencing trial, and defendant's abusive upbringing was accorded consideration in the trial court's sentencing process.


 

107 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Banks v. State


No. 83,774


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


700 So. 2d 363; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1337; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 521



August 28, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 14, 1997. Released for Publication October 14, 1997.
Certiorari Denied March 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1941.
Writ of certiorari denied Banks v. Florida, 523 U.S. 1026, 118 S. Ct. 1314, 140 L. Ed. 2d 477, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1941 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Banks v. State, 842 So. 2d 788, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 387 (Fla., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Stay denied by Banks v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 3258 (Fla., Nov. 3, 2014)
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Banks v. Sec'y, Fla. Dep't of Corr., 2014 U.S. App. LEXIS 21503 (11th Cir. Fla., Nov. 13, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Notice and Cross-Notice of Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Gadsden County, William Gary, Judge - Case No. 92-841-CFA.



DISPOSITION: Sentence of the trial court imposing the death penalty on Chadwick D. Banks is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Gadsden County (Florida), which sentenced him to death after his conviction for first-degree murder. Appellant argued that the trial court's cold, calculated, and premeditated instruction was erroneous, and that the trial court erred in applying both the Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(d) (1991) and the heinous, atrocious, and cruel aggravating factors.


OVERVIEW: Holding that an erroneous cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) instruction was harmless, and that the consideration of a heinous, atrocious, and cruel (HAC) aggravating factor in conjunction with the Fla. Sta. ch. 921.141(5)(d) (1991) factor did not result in improper doubling, the court affirmed appellant's death sentence. The court found that the trial court's CCP instruction was erroneous, because it did not explain that this aggravating factor required a higher degree of premeditation than that required to support a first-degree murder conviction, and also because it did not define cold and calculated. The court held that the error was harmless, however, because the trial court ultimately found that the CCP aggravator had not been established beyond a reasonable doubt, and because substantial evidence existed tending to support CCP. The court also found that there was no improper doubling of aggravators. The court noted that because the HAC aggravator was determined by reference to the victim's suffering, and not the objective circumstances of the crime, it was properly considered along with the sexual assault supporting the ch. 921.141(5)(d) aggravator.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's death sentence. The court held that an erroneous cold, calculated, and premeditated instruction was subject to harmless error analysis, and held that the state had proved a lack of prejudice beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that the listed felony and heinous, atrocious, and cruel aggravators were properly applied in conjunction, because the latter considered the victim's suffering, not the crime per se.

 

108 of 1586 DOCUMENTS



Kimbrough v. State


No. 84,989


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


700 So. 2d 634; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1305; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 510



August 21, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 21, 1997. Released for Publication October 21, 1997.
Certiorari Denied March 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1957.
Writ of certiorari denied Kimbrough v. Florida, 523 U.S. 1028, 118 S. Ct. 1316, 140 L. Ed. 2d 479, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1957 (1998)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Kimbrough v. State, 886 So. 2d 965, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 958 (Fla., 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Kimbrough v. Crosby, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14280 (M.D. Fla., Feb. 26, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Kimbrough v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2353 (Fla., Oct. 31, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Dorothy J. Russell, Judge - Case No. CR92-10868.



DISPOSITION: Convictions and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), affirming appellant's convictions for first-degree murder, burglary of a dwelling, sexual battery, and the appellant's death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, burglary of a dwelling, sexual battery, and was sentenced to death. Appellant raised numerous issues on appeal, but the court affirmed his sentence finding substantial evidence supported the verdict and sentence. First, the court held that ample evidence demonstrated that the killing was premeditated and a felony murder, the jury was properly charged on both offenses, and the evidence supported either theory. Second, appellant was properly barred from admitting evidence under the reverse Williams-rule because he failed to show how the victim's boyfriend's prior bad acts were relevant. Third, it was proper to charge the jury on the aggravators because abundant evidence showed that the murder unnecessarily torturous to the victim. Fourth, a prospective juror was properly excused for cause over appellant's objection because the prospective juror repeatedly expressed strong reservations about her ability to be impartial on the death penalty issue. Fifth, ample evidence supported a finding that the murder was committed during the course of a sexual battery.


OUTCOME: Appellant's numerous challenges to his conviction and death sentence were denied because ample evidence supported the verdict and sentence. The court found it was proper to charge the jury on the relevant aggravators because abundant evidence showed that the murder was unnecessarily torturous to the victim.


 

109 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Lane v. Chiles


No. 88,609


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


698 So. 2d 260; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1301; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 506



August 21, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, Philip J. Padovano, Judge, Case No. 95-2972 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 96-2434.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed and hold that article X, section 16, is constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, commercial fishermen, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court in Leon County (Florida) upholding the constitutionality of Fla. Const. art. X, § 16, which limited marine net fishing, and the court of appeal certified the trial court order to be of great public importance requiring immediate resolution by the court.


OVERVIEW: Through an initiative petition, defendant state adopted Fla. Const. art. X, § 16, which was known as the net ban amendment. The amendment restricted certain methods of net fishing. Less than two weeks before the amendment was to be effective, plaintiffs, commercial fishermen, brought an action challenging the amendment's validity on both procedural and substantive grounds. On cross-motions for summary judgment, the trial court upheld the amendment's constitutionality. Plaintiffs appealed. The court of appeal certified the trial court order to be of great public importance requiring immediate resolution by the court. The court affirmed, holding that the rational basis test applied to the amendment because fishing was not a fundamental right and commercial fishermen were not a suspect class, the amendment did not constitute special interest legislation, the amendment did not violate due process of law or equal protection, the amendment protected the resources of the state by restricting certain methods of net fishing in a rational manner, and plaintiffs' challenge to the form of the ballot summary was untimely because it was made eight months after the amendment was adopted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order upholding the constitutionality of the net ban amendment, holding that the rational basis test applied, the amendment did not violate due process or equal protection, the amendment protected state resources in a rational manner by restricting certain methods of net fishing, and plaintiffs' challenge to the form of the ballot summary was untimely.

 

110 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mark Marks, P.A.


No. 85,920


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


698 So. 2d 533; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1056; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 439



July 17, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District - Case Nos. 93-3259; 94-0339 & 93-3308 (Broward County).



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the affirmative. District Courts decision approved, remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of Florida, sought review of a question of law certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida), as to whether Fla. Stat. Ann. § 817.234(1) and (3) (1987) were unconstitutionally vague as applied to respondent attorneys in the representation of their clients because the statute did not provide adequate notice of when an omission in submitting an insurance claim would result in an "incomplete" claim.


OVERVIEW: Upon a certified question of law, petitioner, the State of Florida, challenged whether Fla. Stat. Ann. § 817.234(1) (1987) was unconstitutionally vague when applied to respondent attorneys. Respondents were indicted for a variety of federal and state fraud-related crimes, including insurance fraud, grand theft, perjury, and conspiracy in connection with forging medical reports and submitting false medical tests in insurance claims for clients. On appeal, the court held that by using the term "incomplete," Fla. Stat. Ann. § 817.234(1), the false and fraudulent insurance claim statute, did not provide sufficient notice of the conduct by attorneys that it proscribed and that it was subject to arbitrary enforcement when applied to attorneys in the representation of their clients. Therefore, the statute was void for vagueness. The statute also applied to third-party insurance claims. However, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 817.234(3), although also applicable to third-party claims, was not void for vagueness. The court dismissed all claims brought against respondents under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 817.234(1) but reinstated all claims under subsection (3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's dismissal of filing fraudulent insurance claim charges against respondent attorneys because the Florida statute charging the offense of insurance fraud was unconstitutionally vague when applied to attorneys representing clients. However, another subsection of the same statute was not vague, and offenses under that subsection were chargeable against respondents.

 

111 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Wike v. State


No. 86,537


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


698 So. 2d 817; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1059; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 483



July 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied September 2, 1997. Released for Publication September 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: A Notice and Cross-Notice of An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Paul Rasmussen, Judge - Case No. 88CF-547.



DISPOSITION: Wike's sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County (Florida), which sentenced appellant to death for first-degree murder. Appellant argued that this resentencing proceeding was tainted by the trial court's refusal to allow his counsel to withdraw, admitting cumulative, prejudicial, and irrelevant evidence, that jury instructions were inadequate, and that aggravators were doubled impermissibly.


OVERVIEW: Appellant struck co-counsel in open court during his sentencing hearing. Holding that because any prejudice resulting from the act was appellant's fault he was not entitled to a mistrial, the court affirmed the sentence. The court stated that appellant had no constitutional right to select his own court-appointed counsel, and that appellant could not benefit from a conflict of his own making. The court stated that where co-counsel was not ineffective, the denial of his motion to withdraw was not error. The court held that evidence of other crimes appellant perpetrated on the victim's sister immediately before killing the victim was properly presented to the jury. Noting that this was a resentencing remand, the court held that under Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(1) (1993) evidence could be presented as to any matter that the trial court deemed relevant to the nature of the crime. The court also held that consideration of both the avoiding arrest and cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravators did not constitute improper doubling. The court held that the former related to the purpose for which the crime was committed, while the latter referred to the manner in which it was committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's death sentence. The court held that the court's denials of appellant's motion for a mistrial and his counsel's request to withdraw were proper, because appellant's contumacious behavior alone was responsible for any conflict of interest. The court also held that jury instructions on aggravators were proper, as was the consideration of two aggravators based on the same facts.

 

112 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Sexton v. State


No. 86,132


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


697 So. 2d 833; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1058; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 469



July 17, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Robert Mitcham & Diana Allen, Judges Case No. 94-1299 Div. B.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Hillsborough County (Florida) which convicted him of first-degree murder and imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction and death sentence for first-degree murder because admission of evidence regarding defendant's treatment of his children was reversible error. The relevance of the evidence was substantially outweighed by its prejudicial effect. The court held that it was not error to admit evidence of certain of defendant's collateral bad acts because the evidence was relevant, and although the acts were dissimilar to the acts for which defendant was on trial, Fla. Stat. ch. 90.402 permitted the admission of any relevant evidence unless specifically excluded by a rule of evidence. The court, however, held that it was error for the lower court to admit evidence of defendant's abusive relationship with his children because although the evidence might have been relevant to the state's case, its relevance was substantially outweighed by its prejudicial effect on defendant pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 90.403. The court found that the admission of such evidence was reversible error because the jury could only have been inflamed by it and might have been moved to punish defendant for the abuse by finding him guilty of first-degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment convicting defendant of first-degree murder and sentencing him to death. It was reversible error to admit evidence of defendant's abusive relationship with his children where the relevance of the evidence was substantially outweighed by prejudice, and the jury could have been inflamed by the evidence and chosen to punish defendant for the collateral acts by finding him guilty of first-degree murder.

 

113 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Krischer v. McIver


No. 89,837


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


697 So. 2d 97; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1053; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 443



July 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Palm Beach County, S. Joseph Davis, Jr., Senior Judge, Case No. CL-96-1504-AF - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Case No. 97-00379.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Constitutionality of section 782.08 upheld.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the trial court, in and for Palm Beach County (Florida), granting a declaratory judgment that Fla. Stat. ch. 782.08 (1995) violated the Privacy Clause of the Florida Constitution and the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellee patient suffered from acquired immune deficiency syndrome (AIDS) and appellee physician wished to assist patient in committing suicide by intravenous means. A declaratory judgment that Fla. Stat. ch. 782.08 was unconstitutional was reversed and the constitutionality of the statute was upheld. Patient's asserted right to assistance in committing suicide was not a fundamental liberty interest. There was a logical and recognized distinction between the right to refuse medical treatment and assisted suicide. The public policy of the state as expressed by the legislature was opposed to assisted suicide. Three of the four recognized state interests were so compelling as to clearly outweigh patient's desire for assistance in committing suicide. The case was not decided on the basis of the court's own assessment of the weight of the competing moral arguments. By broadly construing the privacy amendment to include the right to assisted suicide, the court would run the risk of arrogating to itself those powers to make social policy that as a constitutional matter belonged only to the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and upheld the constitutionality of the assisted suicide statute because the compelling state interests outweighed the individual's interest and the court was not in a position to usurp the legislature's social policy authority.

 

114 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Gore v. State


CASE NO. 80,916


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


706 So. 2d 1328; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1057; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 471; 23 Fla. L. Weekly S 129



July 17, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County, Dan L. Vaughn, Judge - Case No. 83-361 CF. Cir. Ct. Case No. 83-361 CF (Indian River County).
Gore v. State, 614 So. 2d 1111, 1992 Fla. App. LEXIS 11398 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Sentence of the trial court imposing the death penalty on David Allen Gore affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Indian River County (Florida), where he had been convicted of murder and sentenced to death, and sought review of the trial court's overruling of his objections for alleged trial and sentencing errors.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder. The jury recommended a sentence of death. The trial court relied on evidence that appellant participated in a detailed plan to kidnap a young girl using a gun, handcuffs, and rope, to transport her to his residence, commit sexual battery, terrorize, and then murder her. He also threatened to kill another girl and told her he was "going to do it anyway." The jury was correctly instructed that a life sentence for the murder included eligibility for parole after twenty-five years according to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(1) (1983). The cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) instruction incorporated some, but not all, of the provisions of the CCP instruction suggested in the current standard criminal jury instruction on CCP. Assuming, without deciding, that the CCP instruction as given was inadequate, the state supreme court was convinced that any error in the instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, in light of the overwhelming evidence of CCP, as well as the other circumstances of the case. The court found no error in the doubling of aggravators because the avoid arrest and CCP aggravators were based on different aspects of the crime.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the convictions of appellant for murder and his sentence to death because, among other reasons, the cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) jury instruction, while inadequate, was harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt in light of the overwhelming evidence of CCP.

Escobar v. State


No. 77,735


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


699 So. 2d 984; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1012; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 623



July 10, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. As Correction on Denial of Rehearing October 2, 1997. Released for Publication October 2, 1997. Certiorari Denied April 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2768.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Sidney B. Shapiro, Judge - Case No. 89-11887-A.



DISPOSITION: Reversed appellant's convictions and sentences for first-degree murder and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony. Did not disturb the conviction and sentence for automobile theft, which appellant did not challenge. Remanded for a new trial. Found remainder of appellant's claims to be moot or without merit. Motion for rehearing denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions for first-degree murder and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony and the sentence of death imposed by the Dade County Circuit Court (Florida). Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in granting the state's motion for rejoinder of defendant's trial with that of the co-defendant in violation of his federal constitutional right of confrontation of that witness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions and death sentence for first-degree murder and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in granting the state's motion for rejoinder of his trial with the co-defendant's trial. The court agreed and found that that Fla. Stat. ch. 90.804(2)(c) (1989), was an improper basis upon which to rejoin, because the trial court's admission of co-defendant's written confession statement which incriminated defendant violated his federal constitutional right to confront the non-testifying co-defendant. The court addressed defendant's other arguments in anticipation of a new trial and instructed the trial court to review application of the controlling case law precedent and Fla. R. Crim. Pro. 3.152(b)(2). The court ruled that the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress the co-defendant's confession because the co-defendant's waiver of Miranda rights was voluntary. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial subject to the instructions provided in its opinion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for first-degree murder and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony and the imposition of the death sentence. The trial court erred by granting the state's motion for rejoinder of defendant's trial and co-defendant's trial, which violated defendant's constitutional right to confrontation where incriminating portions of the co-defendant's confession were admitted into evidence.

Sager v. State

699 So. 2d 619; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 949; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 381

DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, death sentence vacated, remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida), that upheld a jury verdict that found appellant guilty of first-degree murder and sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was drinking with some associates. After a fight broke out, appellant and a cohort tied victim to a chair with telephone cords and searched the residence for things to steal. Victim was making noise so cohort dragged victim into a bedroom and stabbed victim in his throat. While in custody appellant confessed. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder by a jury. The court affirmed the conviction but reversed the sentence, holding that the record contained competent, substantial evidence to support the first-degree murder conviction, but that the totality of the circumstances did not place the murder in the most aggravated category for which the death penalty was reserved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the murder conviction but reversed the sentence. The court held that the totality of the circumstances did not place the murder in the most aggravated category for which the death penalty was reserved, even though the record contained competent, substantial evidence to support conviction.

Franqui v. State


No. 83,116


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


699 So. 2d 1312; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 946; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 373



June 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 6, 1997. Released for Publication October 6, 1997. Certiorari Denied March 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2096. Certiorari Denied April 27, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2869.
Related proceeding at Franqui v. State, 699 So. 2d 1332, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 976 (Fla., 1997)
Writ of certiorari denied Florida v. Franqui, 523 U.S. 1040, 118 S. Ct. 1337, 140 L. Ed. 2d 499, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2096 (1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Franqui v. Florida, 523 U.S. 1097, 118 S. Ct. 1582, 140 L. Ed. 2d 796, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2869 (1998)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by Franqui v. State, 14 So. 3d 238, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1121 (Fla., 2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Franqui v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 188 (Fla., Jan. 26, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Rodolfo Sorondo, Jr., Judge - Case No. 92-6089-B.
Franqui v. State, 632 So. 2d 1040, 1994 Fla. App. LEXIS 730 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 1994)
Fernandez v. State, 660 So. 2d 421, 1995 Fla. App. LEXIS 10092 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Among other claims, appellant contended that the trial court erred in failing to exclude his own confession from evidence and admitting into evidence at their joint trial a codefendant's confession incriminating appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant participated in a robbery attempt in which a man was killed. Appellant was convicted of attempted murder, murder, and other offenses and was sentenced to death. On appeal, appellant claimed that the trial court erred in failing to exclude his confession because the state did not independently prove the corpus delicti, in admitting a codefendant's confession, and in various other matters. On review, the appellate court found that there was a sufficient showing of the intent to commit the crime of robbery and found proof of corpus delicti. The court found that the codefendant's statements were properly admitted due to sufficient indicia of reliability where the statements were individually self-incriminatory and had particularized guarantees of trustworthiness. The right to confrontation was not violated. The court noted that initial confessions without those qualifiers were improperly admitted but that the error was harmless. The attempted murder convictions were vacated and the charges were remanded because the record did not show whether the jury relied on an impermissible theory, attempted first-degree felony murder. The other convictions and sentences were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's attempted murder convictions and remanded the charges where it was impossible to tell whether the jury improperly convicted him of attempted felony murder, which did not exist. The court affirmed the remaining convictions and sentences. Appellant was not denied his right to confrontation where codefendant's statements were individually self-incriminatory and had particularized guarantees of trustworthiness.

Voorhees v. State


No. 83,380


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


699 So. 2d 602; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 742; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 357

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Stanley Mills, Judge - Case No. 92102-CFAWS-3.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, death sentence vacated, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment and sentence from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida) in which appellant was convicted of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced to death for the deadly beating and stabbing of a man in his home. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, but vacated the death sentence and remanded for imposition of a sentence of life imprisonment, without the possibility of parole for 25 years. Appellant had asserted the trial court abused its discretion by denying appellant's motion to suppress evidence. The court found that appellant's initial encounter with Mississippi officers was consensual because appellant and his co-defendant had just accepted help from the officers when they were wet and lost in an unfamiliar area. They agreed to go to jail to sleep and dry their clothes, but they were always free to leave. There was no error by the court in denying suppression of the knife that was used to kill the victim. Appellant had given the knife to the officers before going to jail for the night. The court vacated the death penalty and remanded because the mitigating circumstances of extreme alcohol abuse, drinking from an early age, and having an abnormal reaction to alcohol had not been considered by the court as mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment because the court had not abused its discretion in denying appellant's motion to suppress evidence. The court vacated the death sentence and remanded to the trial court for resentencing because imposition of the death sentence was not supported by the evidence.

Lara v. State


No. 79,849


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


699 So. 2d 616; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 740; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 362

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Martin D. Kahn, Judge - Case No. 81-26182.



DISPOSITION: Sentence of death vacated and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) sentencing defendant, after a resentencing proceeding, to death for his conviction of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, second-degree murder, and involuntary sexual battery. For the first-degree murder, defendant was sentenced to death. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence of death. Defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief based on the ineffectiveness of his trial counsel in the penalty phase. Defense counsel objected and offered an expanded instruction. The jury again recommended a sentence of death, and the trial court sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed. The court vacated the sentence and remanded for a new penalty-phase proceeding before a new jury, holding that the instruction was unconstitutionally vague, the trial court erred in failing to give the requested expanded instruction, and the error was not harmless considering defendant's substantial mitigating evidence and expert testimony.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence of death and remanded for a new penalty-phase proceeding before a new jury, holding that the instruction was unconstitutionally vague, the trial court erred in failing to give the requested expanded instruction, and the error was not harmless in light of the substantial mitigating evidence and expert testimony defendant presented.

Steverson v. State


No. 86,590


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


695 So. 2d 687; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 734; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 345



June 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Dennis P. Maloney, Judge - Case No. CF94-1320A1-XX.



DISPOSITION: Steverson's convictions and sentence reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Polk County Circuit Court (Florida) convicting him of first degree murder and sentencing him to the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to the death penalty. Defendant appealed, arguing that evidence of a collateral crime involving the shooting of a police officer prejudiced his trial. The court reviewed the evidence and determined that the challenged evidence distracted the jury from the facts of the case being tried. Extensive details of defendant's shooting of the police officer were offered by several witnesses, and along with photographs of the officer's injuries were so inflammatory that they could have unfairly prejudiced the jury against defendant. The admission of such evidence was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court therefore reversed defendant's sentence and conviction, and remanded the matter for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The order convicting defendant of first degree murder and sentencing him to the death penalty was reversed and the matter remanded for a new trial because extensive evidence of a collateral crime unfairly prejudiced the jury against defendant.

 

121 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Lott v. State


No. 86,108


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


695 So. 2d 1239; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 684; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 289



May 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 20, 1997. Released for Publication June 20, 1997. Certiorari Denied November 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6980.
Writ of certiorari denied Lott v. Florida, 522 U.S. 986, 118 S. Ct. 452, 139 L. Ed. 2d 387, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6980 (1997)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Lott v. State, 839 So. 2d 698, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 333 (Fla., 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lott v. AG, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 124613 (M.D. Fla., July 18, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Dorothy Russell, Circuit Judge - Case No. CR94-4667.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed Lott's conviction and sentence of death.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which entered a judgment of conviction of first-degree murder and sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: After eliciting a woman's automatic teller machine number, appellant stabbed and struck her, causing her death, and stole her diamond bracelet. The jury sentenced appellant to death. On appeal, the court affirmed. The jury was entitled to believe the testimony of appellant's acquaintance that appellant told him about the murder, and the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction. The trial court properly refused to allow the acquaintance's brother to testify as to his opinion of the acquaintance's truthfulness because it was not admissible reputation evidence. The trial court's denial of appellant's motion to sanction the prosecution's witnesses for violating witness sequestration was not an abuse of discretion where the witnesses were unaware that sequestration was in effect and the conversation did not cause any of them to change their testimony. The torture of the woman supported the finding that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel. The jury properly found that appellant planned to rob the victim, planned to kill her after realizing that she could identify him, and deliberately taped her and searched the house for valuables before killing her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and the death sentence; the evidence, including that of appellant's acquaintance, was sufficient to support the conviction; the trial court properly refused to sanction the prosecution's witnesses who inadvertently violated the rule of witness sequestration; the sentence was appropriate because the crime was especially cruel and appellant planned the robbery and murder.

Poe v. Hillsborough County


No. 90,223


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


695 So. 2d 672; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 686; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 284



May 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 18, 1997. Released for Publication June 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County - Bond Validations Sam D. Pendino, Judge - Case Nos. 96-6515 & 96-8748 Div. C.



DISPOSITION: Reversed the trial court's order below and remanded with directions to enter a judgment validating the bonds proposed to be issued by the TSA for the new community stadium project in Tampa.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants county and city sports authority sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida), invalidating a proposed bond issue for the construction of a new professional football stadium.


OVERVIEW: The voters of appellant county and appellant city approved an bond ordinance levying a surtax in order to finance a new stadium primarily for the use of the local professional football team, although the stadium would host other events. Appellee taxpayer claimed that the bonds were invalid under Fla. Const. art. VII, § 10(c). The trial court found that the new stadium would serve the public but invalidated the bond because under the terms of finance, the professional football organization would receive $ 2 million in revenue from events other than professional football games. On appeal, the court reversed and validated the bond. The private benefit to the football team was incidental to the greater public purpose, and the bond thus did not violate Fla. Const. art. VII, § 10(c) or Fla. Const. art. IX, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order invalidating the bond issue and remanded for validation; the football organization's initial revenue from non-professional football events was a benefit incidental to the larger public benefit; the bonds were therefore constitutional.

Jones v. Butterworth


No. 90,231


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


701 So. 2d 76; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 688; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 659



May 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 20, 1997. Petitioner's Motion for Rehearing Denied and Respondent's Motion for Rehearing and/or Clarification Denied June 13, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 736.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - All Writs.



DISPOSITION: Jones's stay of execution vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, under warrant of death, sought all writs jurisdiction and a determination of whether electrocution in Florida was cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV and Fla. Const. art. I, §17.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate petitioned to determine whether electrocution in Florida was cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV and Fla. Const. art. I, §17. Appellant's execution was stayed during the proceedings. Appellant presented arguments that Florida's electric chair utilized a method that inflicted pain during its operation and that its use was unusual because the trend was to move away from the chair as a form of capital punishment. The trial court denied the petition. Appellant claimed error in the trial court's refusal to admit certain evidence that would establish his claim. Appellant sought all writs jurisdiction from the appellate court. The court vacated the stay and held that there was competent substantial evidence in the record to support the order of the trial judge. The court held that electrocution in Florida's electric chair was not cruel or unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's stay of execution and found that electrocution was not a form of cruel and unusual punishment because electrocution was not per se unconstitutional.


 

124 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Muller


No. 88,221


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


693 So. 2d 976; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 678; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 264



May 15, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Second District - Case No. 94-02958 (Pasco County).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a judgment of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held that a provision of the driving under the influence statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193(6)(d), was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellee driver was arrested for driving under the influence (DUI), entered a no contest plea, and was placed on probation after being adjudicated guilty. The trial court declined to impose the impoundment provision of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193(6)(d), holding the provision was unconstitutional. Appellant state filed an appeal and the appellate court affirmed the trial court's reasoning and held that the aforementioned provision unconstitutionally vague and provided no mechanism for enforcement and failed to define mobilization. Appellant challenged the appellate court's decision. The court reversed the lower court's decision and reasoned that Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193(6)(d) provided notice that upon a DUI conviction, appellee's vehicle would be impounded. The vehicle impoundment clause only set forth an additional penalty if convicted of a DUI. Moreover, the court reasoned the appellate court's contention that the statute lacked of an enforcement mechanism did not render it unconstitutionally vague or unenforceable. Additionally, appellee's arguments that his equal protection and due process rights were violated as a consequence of the impoundment provision were without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court, holding the impoundment provision of the driving under the influence (DUI) statute unconstitutionally vague, was reversed. The court reasoned the provision was not vague and set forth an additional penalty only if appellee was convicted of DUI. Furthermore, the fact that the provision lacked the specificity of who would be enforcing the impoundment was of no consequence to the constitutionality of the provision.

 

125 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Dryden v. Madison County


No. 87,594


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


696 So. 2d 728; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 671; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 268



May 15, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 9, 1997. Released for Publication July 9, 1997. Certiorari Granted March 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1453.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case Nos. 95-466/95-978 (Madison County).



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the affirmative, decision in Dryden approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, Madison County (Florida), certified the question whether plaintiffs, county residents in a class action suit who successfully challenged the validity of four ordinances that levied special assessments, were entitled to refunds for all five of the years for which they sought reimbursement.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, county residents in a class action suit, challenged the validity of four ordinances that levied special assessments for garbage services, landfill closure, ambulance service, and fire protection. The trial court ruled that the ordinances were invalid and that plaintiffs were entitled to refunds for three out of five years with interest. The district court affirmed the judgment regarding refunds but reversed the judgment regarding interest because no final money judgment had been entered on the refunds. The court held that the district court did not err in determining that plaintiffs were only entitled to tax refunds for three out of the five years in question. The assessments for the first two years were non-discriminatory and conferred a commensurate benefit on plaintiffs. The county also acted in good faith in imposing these assessments. Thus, equitable considerations precluded a refund for those two years. The court also disagreed with plaintiffs that the county should be required to pay interest on the refunds from the latter three years. Plaintiffs were not presently entitled to postjudgment interest because the amount owed was still indeterminate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that plaintiffs, county residents in a class action suit who sought refunds for illegal ordinances, were only entitled to tax refunds for three out of the five years in question. Plaintiffs were not entitled to refunds for the first two years because the county acted in good faith in imposing the assessments, which were non-discriminatory and conferred a commensurate benefit on plaintiffs.

DISPOSITION: Certified question, as reworded, affirmed; and we quashed that portion of the district court's decision that rules the fire protection services special assessment invalid.

The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of petitioner. The court of appeal affirmed the summary judgment as to the solid waste disposal assessment. However, the court of appeal found that the fire protection assessment was invalid because the services provided no special benefit to the assessed properties different from benefits provided the community as a whole. The court of appeal certified as a question of great public importance whether the assessments were valid. Respondents appealed. The court reworded the question as whether the assessments provided a special benefit to the assessed properties, answered the question in the affirmative, and quashed the portion of the decision of the court of appeals ruling the fire protection services assessment invalid. The assessment provided a special benefit to the assessed properties through, at a minimum, lower insurance premiums and enhanced property value.


OUTCOME: The court reworded the question as whether the assessments provided a special benefit to the assessed properties, answered the question in the affirmative, and quashed the portion of the decision of the court of appeals ruling the fire protection services assessment invalid. The assessment provided a special benefit to the assessed properties through, at a minimum, lower insurance premiums and enhanced property values.

Willacy v. State


No. 86,994


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


696 So. 2d 693; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 558; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 19



April 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1997. Released for Publication June 4, 1997. Certiorari Denied November 10, 1997, Reported at 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6764.
Writ of certiorari denied Willacy v. Florida, 522 U.S. 970, 118 S. Ct. 419, 139 L. Ed. 2d 321, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6764 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Willacy v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1141 (Fla., June 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Theron Yawn, Senior Judge - Case No. 90-16062-CF-A.
Willacy v. State, 640 So. 2d 1079, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 738 (Fla., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida), which imposed the death penalty on resentencing for his first-degree murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: The victim walked in on appellant, her neighbor, burglarizing her house. Appellant beat, choked, and strangled her and, because she was still alive, doused her with gasoline and set her on fire. He was convicted of first-degree murder, among other things, and sentenced to death. The death sentence was vacated and the matter was remanded. The trial court again imposed the death sentence at resentencing. On appeal, the court held that the denial of appellant's motion to disqualify the trial judge was proper. The motion was filed almost 3 months after learning of the grounds for disqualification, long after the required 10 day filing period had expired. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in finding several aggravating circumstances. The murder was committed to avoid arrest because there was little reason to kill the victim except for the fact that she was a witness. Additionally, because of the aggravating circumstances of the commission of arson and the commission for pecuniary gain were unrelated, they did not constitute improper doubling. Finding the remaining arguments to be meritless, the court affirmed the order imposing the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The order imposing the death sentence upon appellant for first-degree murder was affirmed because appellant's motion to disqualify was untimely, the evidence supported a finding that the murder was committed to avoid arrest, the aggravating circumstances were unrelated and did not constitute improper doubling, and the remaining arguments were meritless.

James v. State


No. 86,834


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


695 So. 2d 1229; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 559; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 223



April 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied June 20, 1997. Released for Publication June 20, 1997. Certiorari Denied December 1, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7152.
Writ of certiorari denied James v. Florida, 522 U.S. 1000, 118 S. Ct. 569, 139 L. Ed. 2d 409, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7152 (1997)
Post-conviction proceeding at James v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 53 (Fla., Jan. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, Alan A. Dickey, Judge - Case No. 93-3237-CFA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida) that sentenced him to death for first-degree murder. Defendant claimed that in sentencing, the trial court erred in applying the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator to the murder of the strangulation victim and in rejecting the statutory mitigator that defendant was under the influence of an extreme mental disturbance at the time of the murders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his death sentence for first-degree murder after he stabbed and strangled two people. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in applying the heinous, atrocious, or cruel (HAC) aggravator as to the murder of the strangulation victim and in rejecting the statutory mitigator that defendant was under the influence of extreme mental disturbance at the time of the murders. The appellate court affirmed the sentence, holding that the HAC aggravator was appropriate for the strangulation because the victim opened her eyes and looked at defendant as he grabbed her neck. The victim died quickly, but she was conscious of her impending death, and the terror of the victim during events leading up to a murder could make an otherwise quick death especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel. The appellate court also held that the trial court did not err in rejecting the extreme mental disturbance mitigator. The trial court determined that defendant was under the influence of a moderate mental disturbance at the time of the murders. The trial court gave that finding significant weight in sentencing, so the appellate court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision to sentence defendant to death for the stabbing and strangling of two people. The appellate court held that the trial court properly applied the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator as to the strangulation because the victim opened her eyes and was conscious of her impending death, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in rejecting that extreme emotional disturbance mitigator.

Onwu v. State


No. 89,026


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


692 So. 2d 881; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 562; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 217



April 24, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Writ of Prohibition.



DISPOSITION: Administrative order I-96-C-6 declared invalid and Judge Horowitz directed to take no further steps toward a commitment of Onwu under chapter 916.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed for a writ of prohibition challenging an administrative order entered in the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit Court, Broward County (Florida), which set a hearing for commitment proceedings in petitioner's criminal prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a defendant in the county court criminal division. Following competency evaluations and a hearing, the trial judge found petitioner incompetent to proceed on his misdemeanor charge and directed counsel to set a commitment hearing. Petitioner filed a motion to declare the judge's administrative order unconstitutional on the ground that the judge did not have the authority to commit him. The motion was denied. Petitioner then filed for a writ of prohibition. The court declared the administrative order invalid and directed the trial court to take no further steps toward commitment proceedings against petitioner. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 916 (1995), a county court judge did not have authority to order commitments. Only the circuit court was permitted to make the findings necessary for a forensic commitment under the law. Because only a county court was permitted to try petitioner, as he was only charged with a misdemeanor, the trial court's administrative order was invalid.


OUTCOME: An administrative order entered in petitioner's criminal prosecution setting a hearing for commitment proceedings was declared invalid and the court directed the county court to take no further steps toward commitment of petitioner. Under the law, county court judges were precluded from ordering commitments.

Murray v. State


No. 83,556


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


692 So. 2d 157; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 429; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 203



April 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Sheppard & White, P.A. v. City of Jacksonville, 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 15592 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Nov. 22, 1999)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Murray v. State, 838 So. 2d 1073, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1942 (Fla., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Alban E. Brooke, Judge - Case No. 92-3708-CF.
Taylor v. State, 630 So. 2d 1038, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1945 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Convictions and sentences reversed, case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motions to suppress hair and DNA evidence, the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) entered a judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder, burglary with an assault, and sexual battery. Defendant appealed, raising 23 claims of error.


OVERVIEW: After his convictions for first degree murder, burglary with an assault, and sexual battery, defendant appealed. Inter alia, defendant asserted that the trial court abused its discretion in denying his motion to suppress hair evidence seized pursuant to an allegedly defective search warrant and in allowing the state's expert to testify about the results of DNA typing. Despite finding that the trial court reasonably could have denied defendant's motion to suppress hair evidence on the ground that a detective's testimony that defendant voluntarily consented to give a hair sample was more credible than defendant's testimony to the contrary, the court reversed and remanded. The Frye test for admissibility of scientific evidence was not met where the trial court failed to conduct the step-by-step inquiry as to whether either the polymerase chain reaction method of DNA typing used by the state's expert, or the probability calculations used to report the test results, could be admitted at the trial. Thus, the state failed to prove the general acceptance of both the underlying scientific principle and the testing procedures used to apply that principle to the facts.


OUTCOME: Although the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion to suppress hair evidence, the court reversed and remanded defendant's convictions and sentences for first degree murder, burglary with an assault, and sexual battery because the trial court did abuse its discretion in admitting DNA evidence that did not meet the Frye standard for admissibility. Thus, defendant's remaining claims of error were rendered moot.

Gudinas v. State


No. 86,070


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


693 So. 2d 953; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 336; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 181



April 10, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied October 20, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6371.
Writ of certiorari denied Gudinas v. Florida, 522 U.S. 936, 118 S. Ct. 345, 139 L. Ed. 2d 267, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6371 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Gudinas v. State, 816 So. 2d 1095, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 539 (Fla., 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Gudinas v. McNeil, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 104850 (M.D. Fla., Sept. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Belvin Perry, Jr., Chief Judge - Case No. CR94-7132.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court, Orange County (Florida) convicting him of first-degree murder, two counts of sexual battery, attempted sexual battery, and attempted burglary with an assault. Appellant also sought review of his death sentence alleging numerous points of error.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. In support of his death sentence, the trial court found statutory aggravating factors. Appellant's aggravating factors were that he had been convicted of a prior violent felony, the murder was committed during the commission of a sexual battery, and the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel. Appellant alleged that the trial court improperly allowed the joinder of his offenses against the victim with those against another attempted victim. The court held that appellant's offenses constituted a crime spree and were properly joined in one trial. The court found that the aborted entry into the witness' car, the actual rape, and the extreme violence of the murder demonstrated a meaningful relationship between the two attacks so as to justify joinder of the offenses. Prior to trial, appellant objected to appellee state's proposed introduction of six slides of the victim's body. The court held that admission of the photographs was proper and did not unfairly prejudice appellant. The court upheld the death sentence finding it proportional to other cases in which sentences of death had been imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions and his death sentence. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in consolidating all five counts in the information into one trial. The court concluded that the slides of the victim's body were not unfairly prejudicial because they were necessary in order for the location and extent of the victim's wounds to be accurately explained to the jury.

Reese v. State


No. 82,119


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


694 So. 2d 678; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 314; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 150



March 20, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, L. Page Haddock, Judge - Case No. 92-4174 CF.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of conviction affirmed, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) convicting him of first-degree murder, sexual battery with great force, and burglary with assault, and he also challenged his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, sexual battery with great force, and burglary with assault. The trial court imposed the death penalty. Appellant challenged his conviction and death sentence, raising nine issues on appeal. The court affirmed appellant's conviction but remanded to the trial court for entry of a new sentencing order. The court did not find appellant's ability to prepare for trial was compromised. The court also did not err in restricting appellant's cross examination or in refusing to allow him to testify on redirect about his offer to plead. As to the penalty phase, the court did err in failing to expressly evaluate, find, and weigh unrebutted mitigation, and the sentencing order contained inadequate discussion of the mitigation offered. The court remanded for entry of a new sentencing order expressly discussing and weighing the evidence offered in mitigation according to the terms the court outlined in cases like Campbell.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because it found no reversible error in the guilt phase and found sufficient competent evidence to support the jury verdict, but remanded to the trial court for entry of a new sentencing order expressly discussing and weighing all mitigation evidence presented.

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Alachua County, Stan R. Morris, Judge - Case No. 91-3832-CF-A.



DISPOSITION: Rolling's sentences of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Alachua County (Florida), sentencing him to death after adjudicating him guilty of each of five murders and holding a penalty phase proceeding pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 921.141 (1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to five murders, and the trial court imposed five death sentences following a penalty phase proceeding pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 921.141 (1). Damiano v. McDaniel


No. 87,831


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


689 So. 2d 1059; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 299; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 121



March 13, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District - Case No. 95-0068 (Broward County).



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the negative, decision below approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner husband and petitioner wife challenged the judgment of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) that affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment to respondent doctor on their medical malpractice claim on the ground that their claim was barred by Fla. Stat. Ann. § 95.11(4)(b). The question certified for review was whether § 95.11(4)(b), as applied, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner wife received an HIV-infected blood transfusion in June of 1986 and tested positive for HIV in April of 1990. By that time, she had infected petitioner husband. Petitioners filed suit in 1992 against respondent doctor and the blood center. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of respondent on the ground that the suit was barred by the statute of repose for medical malpractice, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 95.11(4)(b). The district court affirmed the summary judgment, but certified for review the question of whether § 95.11(4)(b) was unconstitutionally applied in barring an action for medical malpractice where the injury, resulting in AIDS, did not manifest itself within the statutory four-year period from the date of the incident resulting in the subsequent infection. On review, the court affirmed the summary judgment granted to respondent. Section 95.11(4)(b) was constitutional and represented a legislative determination that there had to be an outer limit beyond which medical malpractice suits could not be instituted. The court was not authorized to second-guess the legislature's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment to respondent doctor on petitioners' medical malpractice claim because the statute of repose for medical malpractice cases was constitutional and barred their claim.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the decision from the District Court of Appeal, Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, First District (Florida), which expressly declared invalid the conclusive presumption provision of Fla. Stat. ch. 440.09(3) (1991).

The court excised the provision by removing words that allowed the statute to continue the legislative intent to discourage drug and alcohol abuse while respecting due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the intermediate court order that held that the conclusive presumption provision of a workers' compensation statute was unconstitutional because the presumption created a high potential for inaccuracy and violated due process.

Lawrence v. State


No. 82,256


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


691 So. 2d 1068; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 306; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 125

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 18, 1997. Released for Publication April 18, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 118 S. Ct. 205, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5615, 139 L. Ed. 2d 141.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, Edward P. Nickinson, III, Judge - Case No. 89-1759.



DISPOSITION: Lawrence's sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of murder, kidnapping, and armed robbery, contested the death sentence imposed in the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida), arguing eight errors, including the trial judge's failure to properly instruct the sentencing jury, error in allowing inadmissible evidence and the trial testimony of an unavailable witness, and error in the application of improper aggravating and mitigating factors.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder, kidnapping, and armed robbery. In his death sentence appeal, where appellant failed to timely object, issues on jury instructions and ineffective assistance of counsel were not preserved for appeal. The court concluded that he had fair opportunity and rejected his contention that admission of the testimony required vacation of his death sentence. The prosecutor's biblical references during closing did not amount to fundamental error. The court found that the evidence showed beyond a reasonable doubt that the murder was committed for pecuniary gain. Therefore, the court upheld the lower court's finding of the pecuniary gain aggravator and found that the lower court properly evaluated mitigating factors. Finally, in affirming, the court concluded that death was still a proper and proportionate sentence.


OUTCOME: Finding that death was still an appropriate sentence for appellant following his conviction for murder, kidnapping, and armed robbery, the court affirmed and denied relief for alleged errors in introducing prior trial testimony of an unavailable witness, in allowing inflammatory comments by the prosecutor, and in applying aggravating and mitigating factors.
