Kuhnlein v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 88,266


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


689 So. 2d 266; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 167; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 97



March 6, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Orange County, Lawrence R. Kirkwood, Judge, Case No. CI92-6224 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District, Case No. 96-378.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court's order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vehicle owners sought review of an order of the Trial Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which denied appellants' motion for an award of postjudgment interest after the trial court ordered appellee revenue department to refund vehicle impact fees that were collected from appellants.


OVERVIEW: Appellant vehicle owners commenced a class action lawsuit against appellee revenue department, contending that a vehicle impact fee, Fla. Stat. ch. 319.231 (1991), was unconstitutional. The trial court held that the statute was unconstitutional and ordered appellee to refund payments to appellants. Appellants moved for and were denied postjudgment interest, following the trial court's order for attorney fees and expenses. Appellants challenged the denial and contended they were entitled to postjudgment interest pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 55.03(2) when a final judgment was created ordering attorney fees and expenses. Appellee argued that no final money judgment resulted, the statute was inapplicable to tax refunds, sovereign immunity applied and had not been waived, and there was no evidence of appellee's unreasonableness regarding refunds. The supreme court affirmed the order and held that appellants were not entitled to postjudgment interest when no final money judgment existed. Moreover, the court reasoned that appellants would only be entitled to interest if appellee did not exercise reasonable diligence in issuing refunds to appellants.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying appellant vehicle owners' motion for postjudgment interest was affirmed. Postjudgment interest was not warranted when appellants never obtained a final money judgment against appellee revenue department. Additionally, the court noted that appellee would only have to pay postjudgment interest if it did not exercise reasonable diligence in the refund process.

 

138 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fla. Police Benevolent Ass'n


No. 89,181


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


688 So. 2d 326; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 134; 21 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1862; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 85



February 20, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, Philip J. Padovano, Judge, Case No. 88-2944 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 96-3535.



DISPOSITION: District court's decision reversed, order quashed, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state obtained direct appeal of a judgment from the trial court, in and for Leon County (Florida), which granted appellee unions' motion for summary judgment, and ordered certain benefits restored pursuant to a collective bargaining agreement. Appellant contended that the trial court's judgment was invalid because it was based on a quashed order.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state employees' union obtained certain benefits via collective bargaining. The state legislature effectively rescinded the agreement, and ordered certain accrued benefits forfeited. In a prior appeal, it had been determined that collective bargaining agreements entered on behalf of public employees were subject to the appropriations power of the legislature, which was not bound to fund any agreed-to program, except where the legislature provided enough money to implement the negotiated program but attempted to unilaterally change the benefit. On remand, the trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment, reinstated the agreement, and awarded back benefits. The court affirmed the judgment in part, and reversed it in part. The court dismissed appellant's contention that the order was beset by jurisdictional defects. Noting the complicated procedural history, the court held that the order was valid. The court restricted the scope of the order, however, to effect the terms of the original bargaining agreement for only one year, because appellees had concluded new agreements that had superceded and cancelled all prior agreements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed it in part. The court held that appellant state's jurisdictional attack on the judgment was misplaced. The court restricted the effect of the judgment to the period after the agreement went into effect and before it was superceded by further bargaining.

 

139 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Medina v. State


Nos. 89,758 & 89,762


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


690 So. 2d 1241; 1997 Fla. LEXIS 17; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 75



February 10, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Appeals from the Circuit Court in and for Orange and Bradford Counties, Richard F. Conrad, Judge - Case Nos. CR82-2935, CR82-1908 & 97-13CFA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part, with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Orange and Bradford Counties (Florida), which denied his motions for postconviction relief. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court improperly denied him an oral hearing on his motion for stay of execution. Defendant also claimed he was denied access to exculpatory evidence and was incompetent to proceed at a previous postconviction relief hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's death sentence and convictions for first-degree murder and auto theft were affirmed because defendant was competent to stand trial, however, where conflicting evidence existed as to his competency to be executed, an evidentiary hearing was required. Defendant was convicted of murdering his neighbor. Defendant brought appeals at both the state and federal level, which were denied. Defendant brought a motion for postconviction relief and claimed he was not competent to proceed at a previous postconviction hearing and was incompetent to be executed. The reviewing court reversed in part and stayed defendant's execution. Because conflicting expert opinions existed as to whether defendant was competent to be executed, an evidentiary hearing was required. Because defense counsel was notified of a hearing to determine defendant's competency to proceed in postconviction matters and failed to present live witnesses, the court did not abuse its discretion by accepting live testimony of the witnesses present and by accepting the affidavits of defendant's experts. Because the trial court applied the correct standard at the hearing, defendant's convictions were upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motions for postconviction relief following his convictions for first-degree murder and auto theft. The trial court was required to hold an evidentiary hearing on defendant's competency to be executed because conflicting expert opinion existed as to his competency. Because defendant was deemed competent to proceed at a previous postconviction hearing, the convictions were upheld.

 

140 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. 84,014


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


690 So. 2d 568; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2207; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 25



December 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1997. Released for Publication March 25, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5616.
Writ of certiorari denied Jones v. Florida, 522 U.S. 880, 118 S. Ct. 205, 139 L. Ed. 2d 141, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5616 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jones v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 561 (Fla., Apr. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, R. Hudson Olliff, Judge - Case No. J93-2757- CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed convictions and sentence of death.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which sentenced him to death. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the murder for pecuniary gain aggravator and in finding the aggravator; erred in giving the standard jury instruction to define the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator and in finding the aggravator, and that sentence was disproportionate.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to death for murdering a used car salesman's daughter during the course of an attempted murder of the salesman. Finding no error in the application of aggravating factors, the court affirmed. The court held that a pecuniary gain instruction was warranted, and that the evidence supported the finding of this aggravator. The court held that the evidence showed that appellant had bounced a check in connection with the purchase of a vehicle, and that the murder was committed in connection with an attempt to avoid having to make good the check. The court held that appellant had waived his objection to the cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) aggravator. Noting appellant's pretrial motions regarding CCP, the court held that appellant had not properly preserved the issue by making a specific objection to the instruction as worded or offering a limiting or alternative instruction. In any event, the court found any error in the instruction obviated, because the murder was the result of cool reflection, carefully planned and premeditated, and without pretense of moral or legal justification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's death sentence. The court held that the evidence supported findings of both the pecuniary gain and cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) aggravators. The court held that appellant had failed to preserve the issue of the constitutionality of the CCP instruction given, because he had not specifically objected to the instruction as worded, nor offered any alternative or limiting instruction.

 

141 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Espinosa


No. 87,633


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


686 So. 2d 1345; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2202; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 1



December 26, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fifth District - Case No. 95-842 (Orange County).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed with directions that this cause be remanded for a finding by the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal in the Fifth District (Florida) certified a question to the court as one of great public importance after it reversed defendant's conviction for resisting an officer without violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with resisting arrest with violence. On defendant's express request, the trial court gave a lesser-included offense instruction that informed the jury that it could convict defendant for resisting arrest without violence. Defendant was convicted by a jury of resisting arrest without violence. The appellate court reversed the conviction and certified a question to the court that asked whether resisting an officer without violence was a lesser-included offense of resisting with violence. The court answered the certified question in the affirmative, quashed the appellate court's decision, and remanded the case with directions for a finding by the trial court as to the sufficiency of the evidence on the greater offense. The court held that there was some evidence regarding the legality of the arrest and that, therefore, the trial court properly gave the instruction on the lesser-included offense. The court ruled that a defendant who requested an instruction on a lesser-included offense could contest the sufficiency of the evidence on the lesser-included offense only when the evidence was insufficient to convict the defendant on the greater charge as well.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the affirmative, quashed the appellate court's decision, and remanded the case with directions for a finding by the trial court as to the sufficiency of the evidence on the greater offense.

 

142 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. D.H.W.


No. 87,173


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


686 So. 2d 1331; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2140; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 545



December 19, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case No. 95-00883 (Collier County).



DISPOSITION: First certified question answered in the negative and the second question affirmative. Decision of the district court regarding the constitutionality of section 943.059(2), Florida Statutes (1993), Quashed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After affirming a trial court's holding that Fla. Stat. ch. 943.059(2) (1993) was unconstitutional because the eligibility certificate and fee requirements for sealing nonjudicial criminal records were procedural in nature, the Second District Court of Appeal, Collier County (Florida), certified for review questions relating to the legislative and judicial requirements for sealing records.


OVERVIEW: Respondent filed a petition under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.692 and Fla. Stat. ch. 943.059 (1993) to seal all of respondent's judicial and nonjudicial criminal history records. The trial court sealed all court records and ordered law enforcement agencies to seal nonjudicial records, concluding that the certificate and fee requirements for sealing nonjudicial records were procedural in nature and, therefore, Fla. Stat. ch. 943.059(2) (1993), was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling, but certified for review questions relating to legislative requirements and court standards for sealing records. On review, the court concluded that the ch. 943.059(2) requirements did not violate separation of powers, Fla. Const. art. II, § 3, or the court's rulemaking authority, Fla. Const. art. V, § 2, because creating such requirements was within the legislature's exclusive control. The court then found that a court was not required to apply the constitutional test set out in relevant case law before it sealed judicial records pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.692 as long as the court addressed that rule's requirements and those of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.989.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision that found the Florida statute that established certificate and fee requirements as conditions precedent to sealing nonjudicial records unconstitutional and remanded the case. The court held that creating such requirements was within the legislature's exclusive control. The court also held that a court did not have to apply the constitutional test set out in relevant case law before it sealed judicial records.

Henyard v. State


No. 84,314


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


689 So. 2d 239; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2145; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 14



December 19, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5124.
Writ of certiorari denied Henyard v. Florida, 522 U.S. 846, 118 S. Ct. 130, 139 L. Ed. 2d 80, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5124 (1997)
Dismissed by Henyard v. State, 733 So. 2d 515, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1096 (Fla., 1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Henyard v. State, 883 So. 2d 753, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 859 (Fla., 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Henyard v. Crosby, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 45525 (M.D. Fla., Aug. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, Mark J. Hill, Judge - Case No. 93-159- CF-A-MH.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged judgment and sentence from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida) imposing the death penalty on three counts of armed kidnapping, one count of sexual battery with the use of a firearm, attempted first-degree murder, robbery with a firearm, and two counts of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and a co-defendant kidnapped a woman and her two young daughters. Appellant drove to a remote location and both men raped the woman, shooting her four times. Then they pushed her off the side of the road. Next, they shot the two girls at close range, killing them. Appellant was found guilty of three counts of armed kidnapping, Fla. Stat. § 787.01 (1995), one count of sexual battery with the use of a firearm, Fla. Stat. § 794.011(3) (1995), one count of attempted first-degree murder, Fla. Stat. §§ 782.04(1)(a)(1) and 777.04(1) (1995), one count of robbery with a firearm, Fla. Stat. § 812.13(2)(a) (1995), and two counts of first-degree murder, Fla. Stat. § 782.04(1)(a) (1995). Affirming the trial court convictions and sentence, the supreme court held that the trial court had not abused its discretion in failing to grant appellant's motion for change of venue. The court learned during voir dire that although each juror stated he had heard something about the case, he or she had not formed an opinion and would consider only the evidence presented during the trial in making a decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and death penalty on armed kidnapping, sexual battery with the use of a firearm, attempted first-degree murder, robbery with a firearm, and two counts of first-degree murder because the trial court had not abused its discretion in failing to grant appellant's motion for change of venue or during jury selection by granting the state's challenge for cause of a prospective juror, among other things.

Gwong v. Singletary


No. 87,824


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


683 So. 2d 109; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2077; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 444



November 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 683 So. 2d 109 at 114.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Mandamus.

Original Opinion of October 10, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1719.



DISPOSITION: Rehearing Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed a petition for rehearing requesting an order staying the finality of the opinion in petitioner's case pending review of a case which the United States Supreme Court had granted review.


OVERVIEW: In the criminal proceeding against petitioner, the state filed a petition for rehearing requesting that the court issue an order staying the finality of its opinion in petitioner's case pending a decision by the United States Supreme Court. The case pending before the United States Supreme Court allegedly concerned a previous decision by the Court which held that changes in incentive gain-time statutes resulted in an increase in the inmate's penalty, and consequently, violated the ex post facto clause. The court held that granting the requested stay would allow respondent department of corrections to continue implementing the administrative rule that the United States Supreme Court had held was clearly unconstitutional. Therefore, the court was compelled to deny the state's request for an indefinite stay, and the petition for rehearing was accordingly denied.


OUTCOME: Motion for rehearing was denied because the court was compelled to deny the state's request for an indefinite stay where such a stay would have allowed respondent to continue to implement an administrative rule which had been held to violate the ex post facto clause.

147 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Jennings v. State


No. 87,587


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


682 So. 2d 144; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1861; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 472



October 31, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. First District - Case No. 95-411. (Columbia County).



DISPOSITION: District court approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted an application for review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District, Columbia County (Florida), which expressly declared constitutionally valid Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(1)(c) (1993) regarding the sale or possession of cocaine with the intent to sell within 1,000 feet of a school between the hours of 6 a.m. and 12 a.m.


OVERVIEW: Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(1)(c) (1993) provided that the sale or possession of cocaine with the intent to sell, although otherwise a second-degree felony, was a first-degree felony if the crime was committed within 1,000 feet of a school and occurred between the hours of 6 a.m. and 12 a.m. Petitioner was convicted under the statute for selling cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school and for possessing cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school with the intent to sell. The relevant incidents occurred at 7:28 p.m. and 1:20 p.m. The court reviewed a district court of appeal decision that expressly declared that the statute was constitutionally valid. Approving the decision, the court rejected petitioner's argument on appeal that the term "12 a.m." in the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to put reasonable persons on notice as to whether the period of time in which an offense was subject to reclassification ended at noon or midnight. The court held that in context 12 a.m. meant midnight, and that the statute covered the 18-hour period from 6 a.m. until 12 a.m.


OUTCOME: The court approved the district court of appeal decision that expressly declared that the statute was constitutionally valid, because the term "12 a.m." in the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

148 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


King v. State


No. 85,026


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


681 So. 2d 1136; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1866; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 456



October 24, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 93-1261 (Escambia County).



DISPOSITION: Answered certified question in the negatived, quash the decision below, and remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reviewed a decision of the First District Court of Appeal, Escambia County (Florida), and answered a certified question regarding imposition of an habitual felony offender sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court addressed a certified question from the district court. The issue was whether a trial judge, upon revocation of probation, could lawfully impose an habitual felony offender sentence, despite having declined to impose such a sentence at the original proceeding. The answer was no. Petitioner was convicted of burglary and robbery, which were punishable as provided in Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082, 775.083, and 775.084 (1989). The original sentencing judge explicitly rejected the habitual offender sentencing option and imposed a guidelines sentence under ch. 775.082, which specified the maximum imprisonment term for each offense classification. The sentencing judge could impose an habitual offender sentence or a guidelines sentence, but not both. Having served the imprisonment portion of his sentence under the guidelines, petitioner could not be sentenced as an habitual offender on revocation of probation. The hybrid sentence must be reversed. Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.701(d)(14) required sentences imposed after revocation of probation be in accordance with the guidelines. The court disapproved Davis to the extent it was inconsistent with its opinion.


OUTCOME: The court answered a certified question in the negative after determining petitioner was improperly sentenced as an habitual offender upon revocation of his probation, quashed the decision below, and remanded.

Chicone v. State


No. 85,136


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


684 So. 2d 736; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1868; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 458



October 24, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 10, 1996. Released for Publication December 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Fifth District - Case No. 93-2659 (Orange County).



DISPOSITION: Remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reviewed a decision of the District Court of Appeal, Orange County (Florida), which affirmed petitioner's convictions of possession of cocaine, Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(1)(f) (1991), and possession of drug paraphernalia, Fla. Stat. ch. 893.147(1) (1995), but reversed on several sentencing issues.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of possession of cocaine, Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(1)(f) (1991), and possession of drug paraphernalia, ch. 893.147(1) (1995). Petitioner appealed, contending that the information should have been dismissed because neither count contained the essential element of knowledge, and that the court should have instructed the jury that the state had to prove he knew the substance he possessed was cocaine, and the object he possessed was drug paraphernalia. The district court rejected these contentions, but reversed on several sentencing issues. The court quashed the decision below. The court held that the state was required to prove that petitioner knew of the illicit nature of the items he possessed under ch. 893.13(6)(a) and 893.147(1), and that petitioner was entitled to a specific jury instruction on knowledge as requested, and remanded. Guilty knowledge must be established in a simple drug possession case. The legislature would not ordinarily criminalize the "innocent" possession of illegal drugs. Silence did not suggest that the legislature dispensed with scienter here. However, the information was not defective because it tracked the language in each statute.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the lower court decision because the state must prove petitioner knew of the illicit nature of the items he possessed under the Florida statutes for possession of controlled substance and possession of drug paraphernalia, found petitioner was entitled to a more specific jury instruction on knowledge, and remanded.

Bush v. State


No. 89,118


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


682 So. 2d 85; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1794; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 455



October 16, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Martin County, C. Pfeiffer Trowbridge, Senior Judge - Case No. 82-352CF.



DISPOSITION: Denial of Bush's motion for postconviction relief affirmed and his emergency application for extraordinary relief, petition for writ of mandamus, and petition for prohibition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Martin County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief related to a death warrant issued for his murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to being sentenced to death for his murder conviction, appellant argued that his death warrant should be stayed pending resolution of a hearing involving a codefendant. Appellant argued that, if the codefendant's death sentence was reduced, appellant's death sentence would be improperly disproportional. However, the court rejected appellant's argument, holding that appellant's death sentence would be proper even if his codefendant's sentence was reduced, in light of appellant's predominant role in the crime and appellant's prior history. The court then held that appellant's failure to object at the trial level to an instruction to his sentencing jury precluded his challenge to the instruction on appeal, despite the fact that the instruction had been found unconstitutionally vague. Thus, the court upheld the denial of appellant's claim for postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying appellant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed because appellant's role in the murder for which he was convicted warranted imposition of the death penalty, and appellant's failure to object to a jury instruction at the trial level precluded his challenge to the instruction on appeal.

Chiles v. Milligan


No. 88,296


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


682 So. 2d 74; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1720; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 435



October 10, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Challenged proviso language is unconstitutional and directed that it be expunged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner governor asked for a writ of mandamus that would require the expunction of proviso language that allegedly violated Fla. Const. art. III, § 12, by attempting to amend existing law on a subject other than appropriations by allowing respondent district school boards to spend up to 20 percent of the funds appropriated to a categorical program for purposes other than those required by the categorical program.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner governor asked the court for a writ of mandamus requiring the expunction of the proviso language relating to the expenditure of funds appropriated to categorical programs for instructional material and student transportation. Petitioner challenged the proviso language that allowed respondent district school boards to spend up to 20 percent of the funds appropriated to a categorical program for purposes other than those required by the categorical program. The court held that the challenged proviso language was unconstitutional and directed the secretary of state to expunge the proviso language. The proviso language at issue clearly violated Fla. Const. art. III, § 12 by attempting to amend an existing statute on a subject other than appropriations. Because the court believed that the parties would comply with its findings, it withheld the formal issuance of a writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court directed the expunction of the proviso language challenged by petitioner governor as unconstitutional. The language, which involved respondent district school boards' expenditure of funds appropriated to categorical programs, attempted to amend an existing statute on a subject other than appropriations. The court did not issue the writ of mandamus because it believed the parties would comply with its order.

Albertson'S, Inc. v. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation


No. 86,247


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


681 So. 2d 708; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1712; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 416



October 3, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. First District - Case No. 94-1592. (Leon County).



DISPOSITION: Decision of district court approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a drug store chain, sought review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which determined that a portion of Fla. Stat. ch. 408.706(10), containing an independent pharmacy exemption, did not violate the Commerce Clause.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, a drug store chain, were subject to Fla. Stat. ch. 408.706(10), which set up community health purchasing alliances, required independent pharmacies to provide service at the same (or a lesser) rate as a contract pharmacy, and required them to meet any other qualifications necessary for participation in the specific health partnership. Petitioners asserted that the statute illegally limited certain Florida-based companies' access by barring both all pharmacies licensed under another state's law and all pharmacies with more than 12 Florida locations. The lower court determined that Fla. Stat. ch. 408.706(10) did not violate the Commerce Clause. The court affirmed, holding that there was no discrimination against out-of-state businesses because they were treated the same as in-state businesses under the statute. The court ruled that the critical consideration was the overall effect of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of constitutionality of a statute containing an exemption for independent pharmacies. The court held that the critical consideration was the overall effect of the statute and that there was no discrimination against out-of-state businesses because they were treated the same as in-state businesses under the statute.

Consalvo v. State


No. 82,780


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


697 So. 2d 805; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1709; 22 Fla. L. Weekly S 494



October 3, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing October 16, 1997. As Revised on Denial of Rehearing July 17, 1997. Released for Publication July 17, 1997. Revised Opinion Released for Publication October 16, 1997. Certiorari Denied May 4, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 3028.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Howard M. Zeidwig, Judge - Case No. 91-19140CF-10A.



DISPOSITION: Convictions and sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) that convicted him of armed burglary and murder and sentenced him to death. Appellant asserted discovery violations, an abuse of discretion in admitting evidence relating to a collateral burglary, prosecutorial misconduct regarding a suicide defense, and sentencing errors.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of armed burglary and murder and received a death sentence. Appellant sought review, alleging discovery violations, wrongful admission of evidence relating to a collateral burglary, prosecutorial misconduct regarding a suicide defense, and sentencing errors. On review, the appellate court found no error in the trial court's determination as to discovery violations. The appellate court found that a collateral burglary committed by appellant was closely connected to the murder and was part of the entire context of the crime. The court indicated that the trial court properly admitted details of the burglary because it was inextricably intertwined with the murder but the state's use of the facts from the burglary exceeded the scope for which they were admitted. While the prosecutor's comments about those facts was error, it was harmless. The court found that that appellant opened the door to prosecutorial comment on suicide and there was no misconduct. As to sentencing, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to uphold the finding of the avoid arrest aggravator and that the death sentence was not disproportionate. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant of armed burglary and murder was affirmed. There were no discovery violations, the trial court properly admitted details of a collateral burglary that was inextricably intertwined with the murder, prosecutor's comments as to burglary facts were harmless error, and appellant opened the door to prosecutorial comment on suicide. The avoid arrest aggravator was shown and the death sentence was not disproportionate.

Williamson v. State


No. 84,198


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


681 So. 2d 688; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1629; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 383



September 19, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied April 28, 1997, Reported at 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2741.
Writ of certiorari denied Williamson v. Florida, 520 U.S. 1200, 117 S. Ct. 1561, 137 L. Ed. 2d 708, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2741 (1997)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Williamson v. State, 994 So. 2d 1000, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1915 (Fla., 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Williamson v. Fla. Dep't of Corr., 2015 U.S. App. LEXIS 19165 (11th Cir. Fla., Nov. 3, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Richard D. Eade, Judge - Case Nos. 90-9560 CF10B & 92-15642 CF A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed appellant's convictions and sentence of death.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder, armed burglary, extortion, attempted murder, armed kidnapping, and armed robbery and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered a house, stabbed the wife to death, shot the other inhabitants, threatened to torture a witness's family if the witness talked, and burglarized the house. Because of the threats, the witness took three years to identify appellant, which left the witness's credibility in question. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, armed burglary, extortion, attempted murder, armed kidnapping, and armed robbery and sentenced to death. On appeal, he argued that the trial court erred in admitting prior crimes evidence during the guilt phase, in not severing the extortion count, and in admitting documentary evidence. Appellant also claimed there was insufficient evidence and that there were sentencing errors. The court affirmed the judgment. The court noted that, because the witness's credibility was at issue, evidence regarding appellant's threats to the witness was admissible. The court found the documentary evidence admissible to prove appellant's identity. The court also found sufficient evidence to support the verdict and that the mitigating factors were subject to scrutiny because questioning was needed to clarify the effects of those circumstances on appellant.


OUTCOME: Appellant's death sentence and convictions for first-degree murder and other crimes were affirmed. The court found that the evidence regarding the star witness's credibility was necessary because the witness did not identify appellant for three years because of threats appellant made toward the witness's family. Additionally, the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict and the sentencing errors alleged were either not error or harmless.

Ferrell v. State


No. 83,076


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


686 So. 2d 1324; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1627; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 388



September 19, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 10, 1996. Released for Publication December 10, 1996. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4828. Certiorari Denied April 14, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2340.
Rehearing denied by, 12/10/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Ferrell v. Florida, 520 U.S. 1173, 117 S. Ct. 1443, 137 L. Ed. 2d 549, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2340 (Apr. 14, 1997)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ferrell v. State, 29 So. 3d 959, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 42 (Fla., Jan. 14, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, R. Hudson Olliff, Judge - Case No. 91-8142 CF.
Hartley v. State, 686 So. 2d 1316, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1628 (Fla., Sept. 19, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed Ronnie Ferrell's convictions for armed robbery, armed kidnapping, first-degree murder, and his sentence of death for first-degree murder conviction. Sentences for armed robbery and armed kidnapping convictions, we remand this case to trial court with instructions that Ferrell's habitual offender sentences be ordered to run concurrently rather than consecutively.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Raising numerous issues in the guilt and penalty phase of his trial, appellant sought review from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which convicted him and sentenced him for armed robbery, armed kidnapping, and first-degree murder, including a sentence of death for the first-degree murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his co-defendants beat and robbed a victim. Appellant knew the victim, but was not recognized. Two days later, appellant lured the victim to a place where they kidnapped the victim, and one of the co-defendants shot the victim. The trial judge sentenced appellant to death after finding and giving great weight to aggravating circumstances. He gave slight weight to the mitigating circumstance that appellant was not the actual shooter because he used his friendship with the victim to lure the victim to his death. On appeal numerous issues were raised in the guilt and penalty phase. The court remanded his habitual offender sentences to be ordered to run concurrently rather than consecutively. The only other argument the court agreed with was that the trial judge erred in finding that the murder was heinous, atrocious, or cruel. However, the court found this error to be harmless in light of the remaining aggravating factors (cold, contemplated and premeditated, prior violent felonies, committed during the course of a kidnapping, and committed for financial gain) and minimal mitigation. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions for armed robbery, armed kidnapping, and first-degree murder, and his sentence of death were affirmed because the trial court's error in finding that the murder was heinous, atrocious, or cruel was harmless, but his habitual offender sentences were remanded to be ordered to run concurrently rather than consecutively.

Hartley v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


686 So. 2d 1316; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1628; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 391



September 19, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Ferrell v. State, 686 So. 2d 1324, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1627 (Fla., Sept. 19, 1996)
Writ of certiorari denied Hartley v. Florida, 522 U.S. 825, 118 S. Ct. 86, 139 L. Ed. 2d 43, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4828 (Oct. 6, 1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hartley v. State, 990 So. 2d 1008, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 918 (Fla., May 22, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hartley v. State, 175 So. 3d 757, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 1334 (Fla., June 18, 2015)
Related proceeding at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Hartley v. Jones, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 519 (Fla., Mar. 10, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, R. Hudson Olliff, Judge - Case No. 91-8144 CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed Kenneth Hartley's convictions and sentences for armed robbery, armed kidnapping, and first-degree murder, including sentence of death for first-degree murder conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court, Duval County (Florida) where he was convicted of armed robbery, armed kidnapping, and first degree murder and was sentenced to death for the murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of armed robbery, armed kidnapping, and first degree murder and was sentenced to death for the murder. The trial judge found six aggravating circumstances: prior violent felony conviction; committed during the course of kidnapping; committed to prevent lawful arrest; committed for pecuniary gain; heinous, atrocious, or cruel; and cold, calculated, and premeditated. The judge further found minimal mitigation. The state supreme court affirmed appellant's convictions and sentencing and held a police officer's testimony regarding appellant's arrest was properly admitted as similar fact evidence under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2)(a). The trial judge properly found evidence of a confession to the murder by another person to be unreliable and inadmissible as uncorroborated. Opening statements by the prosecutor, referring to appellant's character, were improper. The state could not comment or introduce evidence regarding appellant's character unless the defense had first made an issue of his character. However, evidence of appellant's character was admitted to support comments made by the state in opening. Thus, the comments did not entitle appellant to a new trial.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed appellant's convictions for armed robbery, armed kidnapping, and first degree murder as well as his sentence of death for the first degree murder conviction because improper comments by the prosecutor during the opening statement did not entitle appellant to a new trial. Evidence was produced that supported the comments.

 

157 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Steiner v. Bentley


No. 86,903


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


679 So. 2d 770; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1456; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 361; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 402



September 5, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Second District - Case No. 95-01376.



DISPOSITION: District court decision approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, Second District (Florida), denied petitioner's request for a writ of prohibition against respondent judge and certified the question of whether Fla. Stat. ch. 741.30(8)(a) (Supp. 1994) was to be interpreted as mandatory, and if it was, whether ch. 741.30(8)(a) an unconstitutional encroachment on the contempt power of the judicial branch, in violation of Fla. Const. art. II, § 3.


OVERVIEW: In a previous decision, the district court denied petitioner's writ of prohibition pursuant to case law authority. The court affirmed and held that the word "shall," as used in Fla. Stat. ch. 741.30(8)(a) (Supp. 1994), which governed the use of contempt proceedings in domestic violence cases, was to be interpreted as directory rather than mandatory. The reasoning applied equally to Fla. Stat. ch. 784.046(9)(a) (Supp. 1994), which governed the use of contempt proceedings in repeat violence cases. Therefore, ch. 741.30(8)(a) and ch. 784.046(9)(a) did not encroach on the judicial branch's contempt power and did not violate Fla. Const. art. II, § 3.


OUTCOME: The court approved the decision of the district court, which denied petitioner's request for writ of prohibition, on the grounds that the term "shall," as used in the statute that governed the use of contempt proceedings in domestic violence cases, was to be interpreted as directory rather than mandatory. Therefore, the statute did not unconstitutionally encroach on the judiciary's contempt power.

161 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Beagle v. Beagle


No. 85,971


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


678 So. 2d 1271; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1419; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 340



August 22, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 94-337 (Duval County).



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions to affirm judgment of trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reviewed a decision of the District Court of Appeal, Duval County (Florida) and addressed a certified question regarding grandparental visitation rights and the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(e) (1993).


OVERVIEW: The court addressed a certified question on grandparental visitation rights. The question asked whether Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(e) (1993) was facially unconstitutional because it constituted impermissible state interference with parental rights protected by either Fla. Const. art. I, § 23 or the Due Process Clause of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV? The answer was yes. Based on the Florida Constitution's privacy provision, the court held that the state could not intrude on parents' fundamental right to raise their children except where the child was threatened by harm. The court limited its holding to situations where a child was living with both natural parents, and at least one parent objected to the visitation. The court struck the section and quashed the court of appeal's decision that the statute was constitutional. The challenged paragraph's major flaw was its failure to require a showing of harm to the child before any award of grandparental visitation rights. This requirement resulted in the state being unable to satisfy the compelling interest standard announced in the court's decisions construing Fla. Const. art. I, § 23.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the affirmative and determined that the state may not constitutionally impose grandparental visitation on an intact family after at least one parent has objected to such visitation without first demonstrating harm to the child. The court quashed the district court of appeal's decision and remanded with directions to affirm the judgment of the trial court.

 

162 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. Bentley


No. 86,568


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


678 So. 2d 1265; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1420; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 336



August 22, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case No. 95-01084.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, Second District (Florida) certified for review the question of whether it had authority, under Fla. Stat. ch. 741.30(8)(a), to prevent the circuit court from exercising its power of indirect criminal contempt to punish petitioner for violating a domestic violence injunction.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought to prevent the circuit court from exercising its power of indirect criminal contempt to punish his alleged violation of a domestic violence injunction. In denying the petition, the district court found that the legislature had no authority to limit a circuit court's inherent power of contempt, as it apparently attempted to do by restricting its jurisdiction to the use of civil contempt in enforcing injunctions issued under Fla. Stat. ch. 741.30. The court held that its power to punish for contempt was inherent and independent of any statutory grant of authority. Although the legislature could limit sanctions, it could not eliminate the ability of circuit courts to apply its inherent power of civil or criminal contempt and any attempt to do so directly affected the separate and distinct function of the judicial branch. Thus, in interpreting the statute so that it would withstand constitutional scrutiny, the court interpreted the phrase "shall enforce, through a civil contempt proceeding" in Fla. Stat. ch. 741.30(8)(a) as directory rather than mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court responded that the word "shall" was directory and not mandatory and that the circuit court could enforce its domestic violence injunction by way of an indirect criminal contempt proceeding.

 

163 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Scruggs (in Re Estate of Smith)


Nos. 84,385, 84,386


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


685 So. 2d 1206; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1237; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 332



July 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 8, 1997. Released for Publication January 8, 1997. Certiorari Denied June 9, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 3571.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Consolidated Cases: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction, and An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District - Case No. 93-731 (Clay County).

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of November 22, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1952.



DISPOSITION: Quashed the decision below and directed that the judgment of dismissal be reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants filed an application for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District, Clay County (Florida), after the appellate court reversed the judgment of the trial court that held that appellee's claim was barred by the statute of limitations for the adjudication of paternity.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, at the age of 60, asserted she was the natural daughter of decedent and filed a petition for revocation of probate and letters of administration, alleging decedent lacked testamentary capacity and that undue influence had been exerted. The trial court dismissed respondent's claim, holding it was barred by Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(3)(b), the statute of limitations for adjudication of paternity. The appellate court reversed and held that under Fla. Stat. ch. 732.108(2)(b), respondent could bring a paternity action in probate for the purpose of establishing her right to intestate succession. Petitioners filed a motion for rehearing which the court granted. The court held that the fact that paternity may be adjudicated in the course of probate proceedings did not mean that § 95.11(3)(b) was inapplicable because there was no provision in the probate code that removed paternity adjudications brought in probate from the general statute of limitations. Further, the court held the statute began to run when the child reached the age of majority. The court therefore quashed the decision below and reinstated the trial court's judgment of dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision below and directed that the judgment of dismissal be reinstated because it held that the general statute of limitations applied to paternity actions brought in probate to determine heirship.

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

Post-conviction relief denied at Foster v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 488 (Fla., Mar. 23, 2006)

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) convicting him of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, and kidnapping and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with three other men, carjacked a vehicle, attempted to rob the passengers, and then shot and killed two of the four passengers. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, and kidnapping, and sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant raised 12 issues pertaining to both the guilt and penalty phases of his trial. Addressing each of the issues raised by defendant, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. Addressing defendant's sentence, the court concluded that the trial court did not err in instructing the jury on the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator. Finally, the court determined that the trial court did not err by refusing to find the statutory mitigator of extreme emotional disturbance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, holding that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's convictions and that it was not a palpable abuse of discretion for the trial court to refuse to find the statutory mitigator of extreme emotional disturbance.

Mosher v. Speedstar Div. of Amca Int'l


No. 85,745


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


675 So. 2d 918; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1059; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,665; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 270



June 27, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certified Question of Law from the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit - Case No. 93-3555.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit certified the question of whether Florida precedent granted a reliance exception to plaintiffs in products' liability actions whose claims arose during a period of time when the Florida Supreme Court held Florida's statute of repose, Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031(2), unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant consumers filed suit against appellee manufacturer after appellant husband was injured using appellee's product. Appellee moved to dismiss appellants' lawsuit, claiming the statute of repose barred the claim. A federal district court granted the motion reluctantly, but on appeal the federal appellate court decided to certify the question to the state supreme court. On certification, the state supreme court held that appellants were entitled to sue because they could rely upon state precedent which for a time deemed the statute of repose, Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031(2), unconstitutional. The court determined that a reliance exception operated to preserve product liability claims that accrued during the statute of repose's period of unconstitutionality, as appellants' claim did.


OUTCOME: Product liability plaintiffs, including appellant consumers, were entitled to continue to cite reliance exception for product liability lawsuits accruing during period of time when Florida's statute of repose was deemed unconstitutional.

Coalition for Adequacy & Fairness in Sch. Funding v. Chiles


No. 85,375


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


680 So. 2d 400; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1060; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 271



June 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied October 2, 1996. Released for Publication October 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, L. Ralph Smith, Judge, Case No. 94-1906 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 95-776.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an educational coalition on adequacy and fairness, sought review of decision from the Leon County Court (Florida), which dismissed with prejudice appellants' complaint against appellees, who were the governor, the education commissioner, and the state legislature. Appellants sought declaratory relief against appellees and asked the court to declare that an adequate education was a fundamental right under the Florida Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, an educational coalition on the adequacy and fairness of public education, brought an action against appellees, the governor, the education commissioner, the senate, and the house seeking declaratory relief. Appellants sought a declaration that education was a fundamental right under Fla. Const. art. IX, § 1, and that the state failed to provide its students that fundamental right by failing to allocate adequate resources for a uniform system of free public schools as provided for in Fla. Const. art. IX, § 1. The lower court dismissed appellants' complaint with prejudice. On appeal to the state supreme court, the dismissal was affirmed. The state supreme court held that dismissal was warranted because appellants failed to demonstrate in their allegations, or in their arguments on appeal, an appropriate standard for determining adequacy that would not present a substantial risk of judicial intrusion into the powers and responsibilities assigned to the legislature, both generally, in determining appropriations, and specifically, in providing by law for an adequate and uniform system of education.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court dismissing with prejudice appellant educational coalition's declaratory action against appellees, the governor, the education commissioner, the senate, and the house of representatives was affirmed. The court held appellants failed to demonstrate in their allegations a violation of the legislature's duties under the Florida Constitution and that judicial intrusion would be inappropriate.

Agency for Health Care Admin. v. Associated Indus.


No. 86,213


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


678 So. 2d 1239; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1057; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 276



June 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 6, 1996. Released for Publication September 6, 1996.As Corrected. Certiorari Denied March 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 1655.


PRIOR HISTORY: Notice and Cross-Notice of Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, F. E. Steinmeyer, Judge, Case No. 94-3128 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 95-2578.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appellee association's declaratory judgment action, the trial court found that appellant agency's structure violated Fla. Const. art. IV, § 6 and that certain provisions of the Medicaid Third-Party Liability Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 409.910 (1995), were unconstitutional. The parties filed cross-appeals, and the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified that the judgment required immediate resolution by the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: After the governor ordered relevant executive branch officials to recover Medicaid expenditures only from the tobacco industry, appellee association sought a declaratory judgment that the Medicaid Third-Party Liability Act (the Act), Fla. Stat. ch. 409.910 (1995), was unconstitutional and that appellant agency was structured in violation of the Florida Constitution. When the trial court found significant portions of the Act unconstitutional, the appellate court certified the parties' appeal. The court partially affirmed and reversed, holding that appellant's structure did not violate the 25 department limitation in Fla. Const. art. IV, § 6. The court then held that the Act's abrogation of affirmative defenses was facially constitutional, but this did not preclude a later action challenging the Act's application. Moreover, the authority to pursue an action without identifying individual Medicaid recipients had to be stricken; the abolition of a statute-of-repose defense was ineffective to revive time-barred claims; and the provision for combining theories of market share liability and joint and several liability had to be stricken even though either theory could be used separately.


OUTCOME: The court partially affirmed and partially reversed the trial court's ruling on the constitutionality of appellant agency and the Medicaid Third-Party Liability Act (the Act), holding that appellant's structure was constitutional and that the Act was facially valid except that the state had to identify individual Medicaid recipients; and that market share liability and joint and several liability theories could not be used together.

 

168 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Knealing v. Puleo


No. 85,849


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


675 So. 2d 593; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1013; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 263



June 20, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District - Case No. 93-2778 (Broward County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the question of whether the time requirements in Fla. Stat. ch. 44.102 (1993) represented an unconstitutional intrusion of the legislature on the rule-making authority of the Supreme Court of Florida.


OVERVIEW: The trial court set plaintiff's auto negligence action for trial and ordered mediation. Fifteen days after mediation and 11 days before trial, defendants served an offer of judgment for $ 15,001, which plaintiff rejected. The case went to trial, and the jury ruled in plaintiff's favor for $ 15,000. The verdict was reduced by collateral sources to $ 5,000. Thereafter, defendants moved to assess costs and attorney fees pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 768.79 (1989). The trial court denied the motion as untimely. The lower court reversed and then certified the question of whether the time requirements in Fla. Stat. ch. 44.102 (1993) represented an unconstitutional intrusion of the legislature on the rule-making authority of the Supreme Court of Florida. The lower court's question was based upon its conclusion that § 44.102(6)(b) enlarges the time to serve an offer of judgment in a case in which a court-ordered mediation has taken place. The reviewing court held that § 44.102(6) was unconstitutional, and hence an offer of judgment made after an unsuccessful mediation still had to comply with the time requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. § 768.79 (1989) as incorporated into Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court held that the statutory time requirement was unconstitutional, and hence an offer of judgment made after an unsuccessful mediation had to comply with the time requirements in the state rules of civil procedure.

 

169 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Capaldo v. State


No. 86,390


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


679 So. 2d 717; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1014; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 262



June 20, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 6, 1996. Released for Publication September 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fifth District - Case No. 93-2022 (Volusia County).



DISPOSITION: For the reasons discussed above, we answer the reworded certified question in the affirmative, quash the decision below, and remand for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the question of whether it was necessary to prove the existence of stolen property in order to convict under Fla. Stat. ch. 812.019(1) (1995). The court affirmed petitioner's conviction for trafficking or endeavoring to traffic in stolen property after holding that there need not be stolen property to sustain a conviction.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner discussed purchasing some discounted electronics merchandise from an undercover officer. The officer arranged to meet petitioner in a park, where he would then lead petitioner to his place of business. When petitioner arrived at the park, he was arrested and charged with trafficking or endeavoring to traffic in stolen property in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 812.019(1) (1995). Petitioner appealed his conviction, which was affirmed by the lower court on the ground that there need not be stolen property to sustain a conviction. Thereafter, the lower court certified the question of whether it was necessary to prove the existence of stolen property in order to convict under Fla. Stat. ch. 812.019(1) (1995). On appeal, the court quashed the decision and remanded to the trial court to vacate petitioner's conviction because the requisite criminal intent was not proven. Noting that petitioner was never given an opportunity to view or inspect the property to determine if he would purchase it, the court ruled that there had to be some actual property which formed the basis of the charge whether or not it was actually stolen, or otherwise proving intent was problematic.


OUTCOME: The appellate court quashed the decision and remanded to the trial court to vacate petitioner's conviction because the requisite criminal intent was not proven. The appellate court ruled that there had to be some actual property which formed the basis of the charge trafficking or endeavoring to traffic in stolen property, whether or not the property was actually stolen.

Pope v. State


No. 81,797


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


679 So. 2d 710; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 971; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 257



June 13, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing September 5, 1996. Certiorari Denied February 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 909.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Susan W. Roberts, Judge - Case No. CF92-0793.



DISPOSITION: Convictions and the sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida) convicting him of first-degree murder and robbery and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant beat a woman, stabbed her, and kicked her in the head repeatedly. She dragged herself to a neighbor's and made various statements to the neighbor, a police officer, and a paramedic. She died in the hospital eight days after surgery for her wounds. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and robbery and sentenced to death. On appeal, he raised nine issues. The court affirmed his convictions and death sentence. The trial court did not err by admitting excited utterances made to the neighbor and police, dying declarations made to the paramedic, or photographs of the victim's bloody clothes as their relevance was not so shocking as to outweigh their probative value. Evidence that he battered the victim several months before the murder should not have been admitted, but the error was harmless. Appellant was not entitled to a limiting instruction that the battery was relevant solely to prove motive because he failed to ask for one. His jury selection arguments failed as he failed to show an objectionable juror was selected. Florida's death penalty statute was not unconstitutional, and his sentence was proportional. Appellant's various remaining arguments lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions of first-degree murder and robbery and his death sentence because it found no reversible error in his nine issues raised on appeal.

Roberts v. State


No. 87,438


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


678 So. 2d 1232; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 952; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 245



June 6, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 4, 1996. Released for Publication September 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Harold Solomon, Senior Judge - Case No. 84-13010.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Dade County (Florida), which denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief from his death sentence for first degree murder, armed sexual battery, and kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction for murder, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying him an evidentiary hearing regarding a witness's recanting of her testimony. Reviewing the record, the court held that a witness's recanting of her claim that defendant had confessed the murder constituted newly discovered evidence for which the trial court should have held an evidentiary hearing. The court reasoned that, in light of the newly discovered evidence, the trial court was permitted to deny post-conviction relief without a hearing only if the case conclusively showed defendant was not entitled to such relief. The court noted the trial court failed to explain its reasoning for denying a hearing and held the denial was erroneous. The court then held that the trial court erred in refusing, without explanation, to hear defendant's motion to compel witness responses to depositions concerning public records. Thus, the court remanded the case to the trial court.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion for post-conviction relief was remanded for consideration of newly discovered evidence because the trial court erred in failing to hold an evidentiary hearing.

Comm'n on Ethics v. Barker


No. 85,860


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


677 So. 2d 254; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 733; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 193



May 2, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 23, 1996. Released for Publication July 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Third District - Case No. 94-1062.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ethics commission challenged a decision from the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which declared Fla. Stat. ch. 112.313(4) facially unconstitutional. The state had filed a complaint with appellant alleging that appellee city commissioner had accepted complimentary country club memberships in violation of the statute.


OVERVIEW: While serving as a city commissioner, appellee accepted complimentary memberships from two country clubs. A complaint was filed with appellant ethics commission, alleging that appellee had accepted the memberships in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 112.313(4). The statute prohibited a public official from accepting items of value if the official had actual or constructive knowledge of a donor's intent to influence that public official's vote or other official action. Appellant adopted a hearing officer's recommendation that appellee violated the statute. A district court found that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and reversed appellant's decision. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the statute was facially constitutional because it gave adequate notice of the conduct proscribed. On remand, the district court was directed to determine whether the hearing officer's findings were supported by competent, substantial evidence. Appellee sufficiently preserved that question for review by filing exceptions to the hearing officer's recommended order.


OUTCOME: The district court's decision that found a statute prohibiting public officials such as appellee city commissioner from accepting influential gifts to be unconstitutional was reversed and remanded because the statute constitutionally gave adequate notice of the proscribed conduct.

Farina v. State


No. 80,985


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


680 So. 2d 392; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 673; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 173



April 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 24, 1996. Released for Publication September 24, 1996.
Rehearing denied by, 09/24/1996
Writ of mandamus granted, Sub nomine at Allen v. Butterworth, 756 So. 2d 52, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 768 (Fla., Apr. 14, 2000)
Post-conviction relief granted at Farina v. State, 763 So. 2d 302, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1439 (Fla., July 13, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Notice and Cross-Notice of Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, Richard B. Orfinger, Judge - Case No. 92-32128 CFAES.
Farina v. State, 679 So. 2d 1151, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 671 (Fla., Apr. 18, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we affirm Farina's convictions and noncapital sentences. We vacate his sentence of death and remand for a new sentencing proceeding. This proceeding shall include an advisory verdict to be rendered by a jury chosen in compliance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida) and his convictions and six consecutive life sentences for three counts of attempted first-degree murder, armed robbery, burglary with a battery, and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder. Appellee state cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his brother were tried together and convicted of fatally shooting a 17-year-old victim in a restaurant robbery. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and six other offenses and sentenced to death. Appellant challenged his convictions and death sentence. Appellee state cross-appealed. The court affirmed appellant's convictions and non-capital sentences, but vacated his death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding because the trial court erroneously excused for cause a qualified juror. That alone required the court to vacate the death sentence. Under controlling authority of the U.S. Supreme Court, it was reversible error to exclude for cause a juror whose views did not prevent or substantially impair him or her from performing the duties as a juror in accordance with the instructions and oath. The juror could follow her instructions and oath, and was qualified to serve under the Witherspoon-Witt standard. As to appellee's cross appeal, on remand it could present victim impact evidence that comported with the Payne case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions and non-capital sentences, vacated his death sentence because the trial court erroneously excused for cause a prospective juror who was qualified to serve, and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding.

Larzelere v. State


No. 81,793


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


676 So. 2d 394; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 523; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 147



March 28, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing July 11, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, John W. Watson, III, Judge - Case No. 91-2561 CFAES. CIR.CT.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida) convicting her of first-degree murder and imposing the death penalty. Appellant alleged numerous errors arising from the conviction and penalty phases of the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged her conviction for first-degree murder and the resulting death penalty. After addressing each of appellant's issues, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court held, inter alia, that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by excluding reputation testimony against one of the state's key witnesses. The court held that the trial judge had wide discretion in admitting or excluding the reputation testimony and that the exclusion of this evidence did not have an effect on the outcome of the jury's verdict. The court also found that although the "doctrine of completeness" was violated by the trial court's ruling that the defense had to show prejudice, the error was harmless because there was no reasonable probability that exclusion of the redacted statements affected the jury's verdict. The trial court's finding that the murder was both cold, calculated, and premeditated, and committed for financial gain, was not error because the facts in a given case could support multiple aggravating factors provided the factors were not based on the same essential feature of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of appellant for first-degree murder. The court also affirmed the imposition of the death penalty. The court held, inter alia, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by excluding reputation evidence, admitting portions of taped statements, or by using the same facts to support multiple aggravating factors.

Hitchcock v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


673 So. 2d 859; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 480; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 139

However, it was vacated by the U.S. Supreme Court. On remand, the death sentence was again imposed. That sentence was also vacated. In the third sentencing proceeding the jury unanimously recommended the death penalty, which the trial court imposed. Hassen v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


No. 85,300


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


674 So. 2d 106; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 333; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 102



March 7, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 20, 1996. Released for Publication May 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case No. 94-01241 (Pinellas County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an insured and her husband, challenged a Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) decision in favor of respondent insurer, which reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in their declaratory action. Petitioners claimed that the appellate court's ruling incorrectly held that the trial court's retrospective application of Fla. Stat. ch. 627.727(6) (Supp. 1992) was unconstitutional under Fla. Const. art. I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, an insured and her husband, sought payment from an underinsured motorist. The motorist's insurance company made a settlement offer. Petitioners informed respondent insurer of the offer. Respondent denied permission to settle and declined to pay the amount the motorist had offered. Petitioners still settled with the motorist and sought to recover from respondent, who refused to pay. Petitioners brought a declaratory judgment action against respondent, and the trial court granted summary judgment for petitioners, which obligated respondent to pay them. Respondent appealed the ruling. The appellate court held that retrospective application of Fla. Petitioners challenged this reversal by arguing to the court that the trial court's application of ch. 627.727(6) was constitutional. Based on this statute's history, the court determined that it was a substantive prospective statute and therefore declined to reach the constitutional issues. The court disagreed with the appellate court's reasoning, but affirmed its result for respondent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in favor of respondent insured the appellate court's reversal of the trial court's decision to grant summary judgment by retrospectively applying the Florida underinsured motorist statute in favor of petitioners, am insured and her husband. While the court agreed with the appellate court's result, the court disagreed with its reasoning and therefore declined to address the Florida Constitution issues that were raised.
