Geralds v. State


No. 81,738


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


674 So. 2d 96; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 141; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 85



February 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 20, 1996. Released for Publication May 20, 1996.
Writ of certiorari denied Geralds v. Florida, 519 U.S. 891, 117 S. Ct. 230, 136 L. Ed. 2d 161, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 5813 (Oct. 7, 1996)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Geralds v. State, 111 So. 3d 778, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1540 (Fla., Sept. 16, 2010)
Related proceeding at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Geralds v. Jones, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 522 (Fla., Mar. 10, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Don T. Sirmons, Chief Judge - Case No. 89-0495.
Geralds v. State, 601 So. 2d 1157, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 829 (Fla., Apr. 30, 1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida), entering defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's first-degree murder conviction and death sentence were upheld because murder was heinous and substantial mitigation factors did not exist. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and the death penalty was imposed. Defendant appealed, claiming, inter alia, the state's cross-examination of defendant exceeded the scope of testimony, expert testimony was improperly admitted, and the trial court improperly found the murder was heinous and premeditated. The court affirmed, holding that because the victim was severely beaten and conscious after the fatal wound was inflicted, the murder was heinous. Because defendant failed to prove the elements for a continuance, the motion was properly denied. Cross-examination did not exceed the scope of direct because defendant opened the door to questions regarding defendant's link to the murder. Because an expert witness who did not perform the victim's autopsy testified to the cause of death, this testimony was admissible in that it was the expert's opinion in response to facts disclosed at trial. Although the trial court improperly found the murder was premeditated, this was harmless error because other aggravators existed.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the trial court's entry of defendant's first-degree murder conviction and sentence of death. Because the victim was severely beaten and bound and was conscious following the fatal blow, the murder was heinous and the death penalty properly imposed. The trial court's improper finding of premeditation was harmless error due to a lack of mitigating factors.

Roberts v. Butterworth


No. 87,389


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


668 So. 2d 580; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 151; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 89



February 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, F. E. Steinmeyer, III, Judge - Case No. 95-4802.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida) denying his complaint for disclosure of public records by the Attorney General's Office, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 119.01(1) on the basis that some were not public records and others were exempt from disclosure pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 119.07(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner filed a civil complaint for disclosure of public records. Appellee Attorney General made the records available for viewing by appellant's counsel, but withheld certain documents. The lower court ruled the withheld documents either were not public records or were statutorily exempt from disclosure and dismissed the claim for possible Brady material in the withheld documents. In affirming the decision on appeal, the court held that handwritten documents fell under the work product exemption pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 119.07(3)(1), which was remedial in nature and therefore retroactive. It also ruled that the work product exemption applied equally whether a death-sentenced person was represented by private counsel or state-appointed counsel. Since the statute applied to all death-sentenced inmates, there was no constitutional violation. The court also found that Brady had no application to clemency proceedings and that clemency materials were not subject to disclosure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying disclosure of certain material because the work product exemption applied retroactively and there was no distinction whether death-penalty defendant was represented by public or private counsel. Clemency materials were not subject to disclosure.

 

182 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Holsman v. Cohen


Nos. 85,900, 85,901


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


667 So. 2d 769; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 92; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 61



February 8, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Consolidated Cases. Two Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal. Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District. Case Nos. 95-0553 & 95-0554 and Two Original Proceedings. Writs of Prohibition.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we answer the certified question in the affirmative, deny the petitions for writs of prohibition, and quash the decision of the district court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida District Court certified the question of whether the continuing assignment of the circuit judge to preside over domestic violence issues was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were each charged with misdemeanor battery involving domestic violence. Petitioners sought a writ of prohibition alleging that the continuing assignment of the judge was unconstitutional. The district court denied the petitions. On appeal, the supreme court held that the district court lacked jurisdiction to review the administrative assignment. Nonetheless, the supreme court denied petitioners' writ. The supreme court held that a county court judge could be assigned to hear circuit court work on a temporary, regular basis, provided the assignment was directed to a specified, limited class of cases, was used to maximize the efficient administration of justice, and required the county judges to supplement and aid the circuit court judges rather than to replace them. The supreme court found that the assignment of the judge to handle a limited number of county court domestic violence misdemeanors was appropriate because the assignment was directed to a specified class of cases, was used to maximize the efficient administration of justice, and supplemented and assisted the domestic violence county court judge rather than replace him.


OUTCOME: The supreme court denied petitioner's writ of prohibition because the assignment of the judge was not unconstitutional and was appropriate where assignment was directed to a specified class of cases, was used to maximize the efficient administration of justice, and supplemented and assisted the domestic violence county court judge rather than replace him.

Marcolini v. State


Nos. 85,225 & 85,226


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


673 So. 2d 3; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 25; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 25



January 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Motion to Clarify.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Fourth District - Case Nos. 93-3825 & 94-0055 (Palm Beach County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida), which reversed the earlier dismissal of charges against them that alleged theft of electricity in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 812.14 (1991). Respondent state filed a motion to clarify.


OVERVIEW: In separate cases, petitioners were charged with theft of electricity in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 812.14 (1991). A trial court dismissed the charges against one of the petitioners holding that the statute created an unconstitutional mandatory rebuttable presumption. The district court reversed, holding that trial court erred in determining the constitutionality of the statute facially rather than applied because the statute created a permissive inference as opposed to a mandatory rebuttable presumption. In consolidated appeals, petitioners challenged the district court's decision. The state supreme court agreed with the district court that the statute created a permissive inference rather than a mandatory rebuttable presumption and that the constitutionality of the statute must therefore be determined as applied rather than facially. The state supreme court determined that a rational connection existed between the facts in the record and the ultimate fact to be presumed because it was more likely than not that petitioners violated the statute. Therefore, the state supreme court held that the permissive inference was constitutional and affirmed the district court's decision.


OUTCOME: In a revised opinion, the state supreme court affirmed the district's court decision that reversed the dismissal of the theft of electricity charges against petitioners. The statute supreme court held that the theft of electricity statute created a permissive inference rather than an unconstitutional mandatory rebuttable presumption. The state supreme court denied respondent state's motion to clarify in light of the revised opinion.

Bottoson v. State


CASE No. 81,411


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


674 So. 2d 621; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 18; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 38



January 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 9, 1996. As Corrected. As Revised on Denial of Rehearing May 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Gary L. Formet, Sr., Judge - Case No. CR79-4512 Div. 14.



DISPOSITION: Motion for rehearing denied. Denial of Bottoson's motion for postconviction relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment of the Orange County Circuit Court (Florida) denying his request for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Appellant raised numerous claims of error, including that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate the qualifications of a state expert witness and present mental disturbance evidence during the penalty phase and that the jury instructions were improper.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Appellant challenged a trial court judgment denying his request for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Appellant raised numerous claims of error, including that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate the qualifications of a state witness and present mental disturbance evidence during the penalty phase and that trial court erred in only instructing the jury on the statutory mitigating factors. The appeals court affirmed. The appeals court ruled that counsel's decision not to probe into the witness's qualifications or to present mental disturbance evidence was not deficient, and even if it were, the evidence against appellant was so overwhelming that there was no reasonable probability that the result would have been different in the absence of such deficiency. Similarly, the appeals court ruled that even though the trial court erred by permitting the presentation of nonstatutory mitigating evidence and by not instructing the jury to consider such evidence, any such error was harmless due to the strong aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's request for postconviction relief. The appeals court rejected appellant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim because the evidence against him was so overwhelming that there was no reasonable probability that the result would have been different in the absence of any deficiency and rejected his improper jury instruction claim because of the strong aggravating circumstances.

 

185 of 1586 DOCUMENTS



Terry v. State


No. 83,002


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


668 So. 2d 954; 1996 Fla. LEXIS 4; 21 Fla. L. Weekly S 9



January 4, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 29, 1996. Released for Publication February 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, Shawn L. Briese, Judge - Case No. 92-33929 CFAES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his murder and robbery convictions and death sentence from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, armed robbery, and principal to aggravated assault, and received a death sentence. On appeal, he raised 18 claims. The court affirmed appellant's convictions but vacated his death sentence, and reduced his sentence to life imprisonment without eligibility of parole for 25 years. Appellant's death penalty was disproportionate, and this issue was dispositive of all his other penalty-phase claims. The proportionality review required the court to consider the totality of the circumstances and to compare the case with other capital cases. The court concluded that the circumstances did not meet the Dixon test to extract the death penalty for only the most aggravated and indefensible of crimes. The court found only one valid aggravator, no statutory mitigators, and minimal nonstatutory mitigation. It was clear that the murder took place during a robbery. But the circumstances surrounding the actual shooting were unclear. There was evidence in the record to support the theory that this was a robbery gone bad. The court could not conclusively determine what transpired immediately before the shooting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions finding no reversible error, but vacated his death sentence because to impose such a sentence would not be proportionate, and reduced his sentence to life imprisonment without eligibility of parole for 25 years.

Atkins v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a death row inmate, sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida) denying his motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 for collateral relief from his death sentence and a second decision from the same court denying him access to files under the Florida public records law, Fla. Stat. ch. 119 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of killing a child and was sentenced to death. P. 3.850, and the other seeking files from the state's attorney on the theory that he had a right to them under the Florida public records law, Fla. Stat. ch. 119 (1993). With respect to the second case, the supreme court ruled that appellant's claim was not procedurally barred, but that the records he sought, namely notes of the state's attorney relating to the investigation, and annotated copies of decisional law, were not "public records" subject to disclosure under the Florida public records law.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of appellant's claims for postconviction relief was affirmed by the supreme court as was the trial court's denial of appellant's claim that he had a right under the Florida public records statute to files of the state's attorney.

Singletary v. Hamilton


No. 84,945


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


661 So. 2d 816; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1692; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 541



October 19, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 93-288 (Leon County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which affirmed in part and denied in part an order denying respondent prisoner's writ of mandamus. The district court certified a question regarding the authority of the department to implement its pro rata conversion of incentive gain-time earned under Fla. Laws ch. 83-131, § 8, to work and extra gain-time available under Fla. Stat. ch. 944.275.


OVERVIEW: Respondent prisoner filed a petition for a writ of mandamus. Respondent challenged the method used by the department of corrections (DOC) to compute awards of basic and incentive gain-time to eligible prisoners. The trial court denied the petition. The district court ruled on appeal that the DOC's computation scheme was improper and that it deprived respondent of due process of law. However, the DOC was found not to have abused its discretion by not awarding respondent the maximum amount of gain-time available. The district court certified a question regarding the DOC's authority to implement its pro rata conversion of incentive gain-time earned under Fla. Laws ch. 83-131, § 8, to work and extra gain-time available under Fla. Stat. ch. 944.275. The supreme court answered in the affirmative and held that the DOC's conversion scheme was proper in light of an earlier decision that changed how such awards were to be computed. Therefore, the district court decision was reversed in part. However, the supreme court affirmed the district court's determination that the DOC's refusal to award respondent the maximum amount of gain-time available was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the district court's decision that found the time computation scheme used to reduce prison sentences was improper, but upheld the ruling that denial of an award of the maximum amount of gain-time available was not an abuse of discretion. A certified question regarding whether the department of corrections had authority to implement a conversion of incentive gain-time was answered in the affirmative.

Merck v. State


No. 83,063


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


664 So. 2d 939; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1619; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 537



October 12, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 22, 1995. Released for Publication December 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Claire K. Luten, Judge - Case No. CRC91-16659CFANO.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the conviction and remand for resentencing consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and imposed a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Victim died after appellant stabbed him in the back while they were in the parking lot of a bar. Appellant had attempted to provoke the victim into a fight but the victim had refused. Appellant came after the victim stating he would teach him how to bleed. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, and the jury recommended death. The trial court found as aggravating factors that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel and that appellant had previous felony convictions involving the use or threat of violence. The trial court sentenced appellant to death. The court affirmed the conviction and found that the trial court did not err in refusing to grant appellant's motion for mistrial after the lead detective made reference to a prior trial. The court found that the failure of the detective to preserve certain evidence was not a denial of due process because the evidence was neither material nor exculpatory. The court remanded for resentencing and held that the trial court erred in considering a prior juvenile adjudication as an aggravating factor because it was not a conviction within the meaning of Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(b).


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for first-degree murder was affirmed, but the matter was remanded for resentencing. The court found that there was no abuse of discretion in denying a mistrial motion based upon inadvertent reference by the case detective to the first trial of the case because the reference was isolated and appeared to have been inadvertent. However, the trial court erred in including a juvenile adjudication as an aggravating factor.

 

190 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Parker v. Dugger


Nos. 74,978, 78,700


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


660 So. 2d 1386; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1611; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 510



October 5, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, R. Hudson Olliff, Judge - Case No. 82-1658CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a convicted murder, filed a petition for habeas corpus, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel, and appealed the order from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) that denied his second motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Civ. P. 3(b)(1) and (9) as being untimely.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a convicted murderer, filed a motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Civ. P. 3.850, which was denied by the trial court. When the denial was affirmed on appeal, petitioner retained new counsel and filed an original petition for habeas corpus with the court, in which he alleged ineffective assistance of counsel. Pursuant to instructions from the court, petitioner filed a second Fla. R. Civ. P. 3.850 motion with the trial court. The trial court denied the motion as being untimely. On appeal, the court held that because petitioner filed his second motion within the time provided by the court, it was not untimely. However, because the trial court did not rule on the merits of petitioner's claims, the court was unable to review them. The court held that because the jury was instructed on premeditation and felony murder, and because there was sufficient evidence to convict petitioner on premeditation, petitioner's counsel was not ineffective for not arguing that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of felony murder. Therefore, the court denied the petition for habeas corpus but remanded the case for reconsideration of petitioner's motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order finding that petitioner's second motion for postconviction relief was untimely and remanded it for reconsideration of the merits, because the court had granted petitioner the right to file the second motion, but the petition for habeas corpus was denied, because petitioner's counsel was not ineffective for not raising a nonmeritorious issue on direct appeal.

Cave v. State


No. 82,333


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


660 So. 2d 705; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1547; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 484



September 21, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Thomas J. Walsh, Jr., Judge - Case No. 82-9546-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of murder and sentenced to death, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) that entered a death sentence following the denial of a motion to disqualify the judge under Fla. R. Jud. Admin. 2.160(d), (f) and Fla. Stat. ch. 38.10 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of numerous crimes, including murder and was sentenced to death. Following post-conviction proceedings, the death sentence was vacated, and a second sentencing hearing was conducted. At resentencing, defendant moved to disqualify the judge under Fla. Stat. ch. 38.10 (1993) because the judge had previously been employed by the state office that prosecuted defendant. The trial court conducted a hearing, allowing the state to present evidence, and denied the motion at the conclusion of the hearing. Defendant was, again, sentenced to death. The court reversed the sentence and remanded for resentencing, instructing that a new judge be appointed. The court found that by conducting an evidentiary hearing, the trial court failed to follow the procedural process outlined in Fla. R. Jud. Admin. 2.160(d), (f), which provided that the trial judge shall determine only the legal sufficiency of the motion and not pass on the truth of the facts alleged.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding before a new judge because the trial court erroneously conducted an evidentiary hearing on the factual allegations contained in defendant's motion to disqualify the judge.

 

192 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Iacovone


No. 84,215


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


660 So. 2d 1371; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1549; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 475



September 21, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Notice and Cross-Notice of An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Second District - Case No. 92-02438 (Hillsborough County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties cross-appealed a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed defendant's conviction for attempted murder in the third degree of a law enforcement officer because the Florida statutes under which defendant was convicted were unconstitutional, in that attempted third degree murder was punished more severely than the completed offense.


OVERVIEW: This case was brought before the court on cross-appeals regarding a decision which reversed defendant's conviction for attempted murder in the third degree of a law enforcement officer, because the Florida statutes under which defendant was convicted were unconstitutional in that attempted third degree murder was punished more severely than the completed offense. The court affirmed the decision based upon the rules of statutory construction, not reaching the constitutional issue. The court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 784.07(3) and Fla. Stat. ch. 775.0825, which applied to attempted murder of a law enforcement officer, applied only to first-degree murder. If it applied to defendant's attempted murder in the third degree, the result would be that the attempt carried a greater penalty than the completed offense, with the result that a criminal who attempted the murder of a law enforcement officer would have substantial incentive to complete the offense so as to avoid the harsher penalty.


OUTCOME: The decision reversing defendant's conviction was affirmed because defendant's sentence was incorrectly calculated using statutes that did not apply to attempted murder in the third degree.

 

193 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Roque v. State


No. 84,182


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


664 So. 2d 928; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1550; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 476



September 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 20, 1995. Released for Publication December 20, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Third District - Case No. 93-981 (Dade County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held that Fla. Stat. ch. 838.15 was a valid commercial statute prohibiting "commercial bribe receiving."


OVERVIEW: This case came before the court upon an application for review of a decision which held that Fla. Stat. ch. 838.15 was a valid commercial statute prohibiting "commercial bribe receiving." Petitioner credit manager had been prosecuted under the statute for receiving "paybacks" from an independent contractor. The court held the statute to be vague and subject to arbitrary application, and therefore invalid. The statute made it a third-degree felony for an employee to accept a benefit in return for violating a "common law duty." The court pointed out that few workers would be aware that they owe such a "common law duty" to their employers and fewer still could define the dimensions of that duty. In fact, substantial legal research would be required by many employees to determine their obligations under the law.


OUTCOME: The statute prohibiting "commercial bribe receiving" was invalid as vague and subject to arbitrary application.

 

194 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Mungin v. State


CASE NO. 81,358


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


689 So. 2d 1026; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 2203



September 7, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised On Denial of Rehearing February 8, 1996. As Revised On Denial of Rehearing March 6, 1997. Released for Publication March 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, John D. Southwood, Judge - Case No. 92-3178 CF. Cir. Crt. Case No. 92-3178 CF (Duval County).



DISPOSITION: Motion for Rehearing denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for first-degree murder and the imposition of the death penalty by the Duval County Circuit Court (Florida). Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in denying his motion for acquittal on the first degree murder charge and committed fundamental error by allowing testimony that provided a false impression of a life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for first degree murder and the imposition of the death penalty. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred by denying his motions for acquittal on both first degree murder and felony murder because insufficient evidence existed to convict on either charge. The court agreed that the trial court erred in denying the motion for a judgment of acquittal on first degree murder. The court did not reverse defendant's conviction because the trial court correctly denied the motion for acquittal on felony murder. The court held that although the trial court failed to instruct the jury on both charges, the error was harmless. The court reasoned that because the evidence supported a conviction for felony murder, the jury could convict defendant of first-degree murder. The court held no fundamental error occurred when a defense witness testified that inmates who served life sentences could be released. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to give the instruction that defendant's age could be considered for mitigation. All of defendant's other issues were meritless. Thus, the conviction and penalty were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and the imposition of the death penalty, because the evidence was sufficient to warrant the first degree murder conviction and the imposition of the death penalty.

 

195 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Chiles v. Milligan


No. 85,870


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


659 So. 2d 1055; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1393; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 441



August 24, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Mandamus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner governor sought a writ of mandamus which would require the secretary of state to expunge an allegedly unconstitutional proviso to Specific Appropriation 150 of the 1995-1996 General Appropriations Act and the comptroller to ensure that the expunction was reflected in the state's financial operations.


OVERVIEW: A proviso adjusted upward or downward the amount of money allocated to a school district under Fla. Stat. ch. 236.081 depending upon whether the school district met a targeted ratio of classroom salaries to total staff salaries. It was designed to induce school districts to redirect financing from non-classroom employees to classroom teachers in order to reduce the size of classes in the schools. Petitioner governor vetoed the proviso without vetoing the appropriation in its entirety. Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus that required expunction of the allegedly unconstitutional proviso from the state's records. Respondent legislature filed a counter-petition for a writ of mandamus that required the secretary of state to expunge petitioner's veto. The supreme court found that the proviso was unconstitutional because it violated Fla. Const. art. III, § 12 and also found that petitioner's veto violated the same constitutional provision. The court held that the legislature could not enact or amend a law on a subject other than appropriations in an appropriation act simply because the legislature expressed an intent to do so.


OUTCOME: The court found that the challenged proviso violated the state constitution and the challenged veto also violated the constitution. The court directed the secretary of state to expunge the unconstitutional proviso and petitioner's veto from the official records of the state.

Tgi Friday's v. Dvorak


No. 83,811


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


663 So. 2d 606; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1394



August 24, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 27, 1995. Released for Publication November 27, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Notice and Cross-Notice for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Fourth District - Case No. 91-3569 (Broward County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties appealed an order from the 4th District Court of Appeal (Florida), approving the constitutionality of an offer of judgment statute, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 768.79 (1987) and holding that it expressly provided for the award of attorneys' fees regardless of the reasonableness of an offeree's rejection of an offer of judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant restaurant corporation was liable to plaintiff for attorneys' fees and costs arising from plaintiff's tort suit where plaintiff made reasonable offers of judgment and state statutes and procedural rule entitled plaintiff to an award. Plaintiff brought an action following her slip-and-fall at defendant's restaurant. Following judgment in plaintiff's favor, plaintiff brought a motion for attorneys' fees and costs based on her previous offers of judgment made under Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 768.79 and 45.061 (1987) and under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442 (1990). Defendant brought a motion to strike the offers of judgment and to determine plaintiff's entitlement to attorneys' fees. The trial court granted defendant's motion and denied plaintiff's. Plaintiff appealed. The appellate court reversed as to the denial of fees under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 768.79. Both parties appealed. The court affirmed, holding where Fla. Stat. Ann. § 768.79 provided for the award of attorneys' fees regardless of the reasonableness of an offeree's rejection of an offer of judgment, an award was proper. Therefore, plaintiff was entitled to fees because defendant rejected plaintiff's offers.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the appellate court's reversal of the trial court's denial of plaintiff tort litigant's motion for attorneys' fees and costs against defendant restaurant corporation. Plaintiff was entitled to an award of costs and fees because defendant rejected her offers of judgment and applicable statute required an award of fees and costs following such rejection without regard to the reasonableness of the rejection.

198 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Barwick v. State


No. 80,446


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


660 So. 2d 685; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1151; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 405



July 20, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 19, 1995. Released for Publication September 19, 1995.
Writ of certiorari denied Barwick v. Florida, 516 U.S. 1097, 116 S. Ct. 823, 133 L. Ed. 2d 766, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 816 (1996)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Barwick v. State, 88 So. 3d 85, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1518 (Fla., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Clinton Foster, Judge - Case No. 86-940.
Barwick v. State, 547 So. 2d 612, 1989 Fla. LEXIS 559 (Fla., 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, armed burglary, attempted sexual battery, and armed robbery and was sentenced to death in the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida). Appellant sought review, asserting that his motion to disqualify the trial judge was improperly denied and that a mistrial should have been granted after the prosecutor made comments that shifted the burden of proof to appellant and referred to his silence.


OVERVIEW: After appellant confessed to stabbing a woman, he was convicted of murder and other offenses and was sentenced to death. Appellant obtained a new trial with a new judge and claimed that the judge's conduct indicated he was biased against appellant. Appellant was again convicted and sentenced to death. He sought review, arguing that a motion to disqualify the trial judge should have been granted and that a mistrial should have been declared after comments by the prosecutor shifted the burden of proof to appellant and referred to his silence. On review, the supreme court found that the motion to disqualify was not legally sufficient in that appellant did not have a well-grounded fear that he would not receive a fair trial from the presiding judge. As to the prosecutor's comments, the supreme court found that the remarks did not have the effect of instructing the jury that appellant bore the burden of presenting evidence in his defense. The supreme court found that competent, substantial evidence supported the verdict. Other arguments were rejected where any error was found to be harmless, and the convictions and sentences were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Convictions for murder, armed burglary, attempted sexual battery, and armed robbery were affirmed. The motion to disqualify a judge was not sufficient, appellant did not have a well-grounded fear that he would not receive a fair trial, and prosecutor's comments did not impact appellant's burden of proof or right to a fair trial. The court also affirmed the sentences, including a death sentence, holding that any error was harmless.

G.W.B. v. J.S.W. (in Re Baby E.A.W.)


No. 84,819


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


658 So. 2d 961; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1167; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 376



July 20, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Second Correction.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 93-3040 (Palm Beach County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner biological father sought review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), that determined that petitioner abandoned a baby based on a consideration of petitioner's conduct toward the baby's mother during her pregnancy in an adoption proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner biological father impregnated the birth mother. During the pregnancy petitioner offered the birth mother little financial and emotional support. The birth mother moved out of petitioner's home after he physically abused her and informed petitioner that she was considering adoption. Petitioner told her to do whatever she had to do. After being notified that the baby was being put up for adoption, petitioner finally sought legal aid. The summation of various lower court proceedings ultimately was a determination that petitioner abandoned the baby. Petitioner asserted that consideration of how he treated the birth mother was improperly weighted. The court affirmed the determination, holding that evidence of a parent's prebirth conduct was relevant to whether that parent had abandoned the child and that the evidence indicated that petitioner showed little to no interest in the birth mother or the unborn child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the abandonment determination. The court held that the evidence indicated that petitioner biological father showed little to no interest in the birth mother or the unborn child. Evidence of a parent's prebirth conduct was relevant to whether a parent has abandoned a child.
